%%
%% Explicit closed forms for the weighted Virasoro Riccati-metric
%% shadow coefficients through weight 8, derived by Wick reduction of
%% the Maurer-Cartan master equation on the ordered convolution dGLA.
%% Extends the S_4, S_5 framework (thm:s5-vir-closed-form) and pins the exact
%% rational-in-c pole structure through the Zamolodchikov factor
%% (5c + 22)^{floor((r-2)/2)}.
%%
%% Vol I theory sequence. Depends on: bar-complex part (ordered bar,
%% Theta_A, shadow tower, see \ref{part:bar-complex}),
%% higher_genus_modular_koszul.tex (thm:riccati-
%% algebraicity, thm:obstruction-recursion), motivic_shadow_tower.tex
%% (weight stratification), miura_transfer.tex (thm:miura-cross-
%% universality).
%%
%% Cross-volume sweep: Vol III m_8 = 4144720/19683 is verified as
%% the c = 1 specialisation of \widehat S^{wt}_8(Vir_c) (sec:s8 below).
%%

\chapter{Higher Virasoro Shadow Coefficients}
\label{ch:shadow-tower-higher-coefficients}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section*{Prologue}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

The Virasoro shadow tower $\{S_r(\Vir_c)\}_{r \geq 2}$ records the
Maurer--Cartan coefficients of the universal element
$\Theta_{\Vir_c}$ in the ordered convolution dGLA (Vol~I bar-complex
part, \ref{part:bar-complex}).
Through weight $5$ the entries are closed rational functions of $c$:
\[
 S_2(\Vir_c) = \tfrac{c}{2}, \qquad
 S_3(\Vir_c) = 2, \qquad
 S_4(\Vir_c) = \tfrac{10}{c (5c + 22)}, \qquad
 S_5(\Vir_c) = \tfrac{-48}{c^2 (5c + 22)}.
\]
The denominator factor $5c + 22$ is the Zamolodchikov quasi-primary
norm of $\Lambda = {:}T T{:} - \tfrac{3}{10} \partial^2 T$ (weight-$4$
scalar quasi-primary); the identity
$\langle \Lambda \mid \Lambda \rangle = c (5c + 22)/10$ governs the
Wick reduction of every higher-weight correlator through the stress
tensor OPE channel.

The chapter establishes explicit closed forms for
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_6,\widehat S^{\rm wt}_7,\widehat S^{\rm wt}_8$
and the weighted master-equation recurrence that generates every
subsequent weighted coefficient. Section~\ref{sec:sth-setup} records the
setup, fixing the $A_\infty$ coproduct correction $\delta^{(r)}$ and
the shadow transport operator. Section~\ref{sec:sth-recurrence}
states and proves the Virasoro weighted shadow recurrence
(Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence}), the common engine for
all higher weighted coefficients. Section~\ref{sec:sth-s6-s7-s8}
establishes the three closed forms through weight $8$ and verifies the
Zamolodchikov pole
structure $(5c+22)^{\lfloor (r-2)/2 \rfloor}$. Section~\ref{sec:sth-boundary}
discharges the boundary-value checks at $c = 1$, $c = \tfrac{1}{2}$,
$c = 13$. Section~\ref{sec:sth-leading-asymp} extracts the large-$c$
asymptotic
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c) \sim A_r / c^{r-2}$ with explicit
$A_r$ for $4 \le r \le 8$ and separates the Kummer-congruence content
(which lives on the $Z_g$ numerators, not on the Virasoro
asymptotics directly) from the bare shadow behaviour. Section~\ref{sec:sth-motivic}
cross-links to the motivic lift: every weighted Virasoro coefficient
computed here is rational in $c$, which pins the absence of
$\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(n)$
contributions at Virasoro through weight $8$ (the first non-rational
lift appears at $W_3$, weight $6$, by
Proposition~\ref{prop:s6-w3-mot}).

\begin{remark}[Two coefficient normalisations]
\label{rem:sth-rectified-normalisation}
There are two coefficient extractions in the Virasoro tower. The
square-root metric identity
$H_{\mathrm{wt}}(t)^2=t^4Q_L(t)$ with
$H_{\mathrm{wt}}(t)=\sum_{r\ge2}rS_rt^r$ computes the weighted
Riccati-metric coefficients; at weight $6$ this gives
\[
\widehat S^{\mathrm{wt}}_6(\Vir_c)
=\frac{80(45c+193)}{3c^3(5c+22)^2}.
\]
The manuscript shadow normalisation used in
Theorem~\ref{thm:S6-Vir-closed} is instead fixed by the order-$t^8$
null-state equation
$2S_2S_6+2S_3S_5+S_4^2=0$, and gives
\[
S_6(\Vir_c)
=\frac{4(240c+1031)}{c^3(5c+22)^2}.
\]
Thus the recurrence proved in
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence} is the weighted
Riccati-metric recurrence. Its coefficients are denoted
$\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}$. The manuscript shadow coefficients are
unhatted; the first split occurs at weight~$6$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Independent BPZ--Wick verification of $S_5$]
\label{rem:s5-bpz-wick-verification}
The closed form $S_5(\Vir_c) = -48 / (c^2 (5c + 22))$ admits a third
genuinely independent verification via direct Belavin--Polyakov--Zamolodchikov
$5$-point Wick contraction. The Wick chain extracts $\langle \Lambda
\mid \Lambda \rangle = c (5c + 22)/10$ from the Schur complement of the
Virasoro level-$4$ Gram matrix (Kac--Feigin--Fuchs determinant
$\det G_4 = c^2 (5c + 22)/2$), reads off $S_3 = 2$ from the universal
BPZ $3$-point Ward identity, counts $\Lambda$-mediated chord-diagram
topologies on $K_5$ via inclusion--exclusion cumulant inversion (signed
weight $-48/10$), and assembles the Arnold $d{\log}$ residue at
simultaneous collision on $\mathrm{Conf}_5(\mathbb{P}^1)$. This chain
shares no intermediate symbol with the Riccati MC recursion: the latter
takes $(\kappa, S_3, S_4)$ as inputs, while the Wick chain derives the
$\Lambda$-norm and $S_3$ from the Virasoro algebra and OPE. The
implementation is at \texttt{compute/lib/s5\_virasoro\_wick.py} with the
independent verification check at
\texttt{compute/tests/test\_s5\_virasoro\_wick.py::TestWickIndependentVerification}
covering all six finite calibration points
$c \in \{\tfrac12, \tfrac{7}{10}, \tfrac{4}{5}, 1, 2, 24\}$. (At
$c = -22/5$ both routes exhibit the same Lee--Yang pole at $5c+22=0$.)
\end{remark}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Setup}
\label{sec:sth-setup}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

Fix a vertex algebra $\cA$ on a curve $X$. The bar complex
$B^{\mathrm{ord}}(\cA)$ carries a canonical $A_\infty$-coalgebra
structure (Vol~I, \ref{part:bar-complex}); projecting its deconcatenation coproduct
onto the scalar $(1,\ldots,1)$ channel defines the shadow coproduct
corrections
\[
 \delta^{(r)} \colon \cA \longrightarrow \cA^{\otimes r},
 \qquad r \geq 2.
\]
The shadow coefficient
\[
 S_r(\cA) \;:=\; \delta^{(r)}(1, \ldots, 1) \;\in\; k
\]
is the $\Sym^r$-coinvariant residue of the bar coproduct at the
universal $\Theta_{\cA}$ insertion. At $\cA = \Vir_c$, each
$\delta^{(r)}$ factors through the stress tensor OPE
\[
 T(z)\, T(w) \;\sim\; \frac{c/2}{(z-w)^4}
 + \frac{2 T(w)}{(z-w)^2}
 + \frac{\partial T(w)}{z - w}
\]
and the descendant-channel corrections it generates. We write $c$
for the central charge throughout.

\begin{definition}[\label{def:shadow-transport-operator}Weighted shadow
transport operator]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For a chiral algebra $\cA$ on a single primary line with
$\kappa(\cA) = S_2(\cA) \neq 0$, define the shadow transport
operator $\mathrm{Transp}_{\cA,r}^{\rm wt}$ acting on the weighted
Riccati-metric sequence
$(\widehat S^{\rm wt}_2,\widehat S^{\rm wt}_3,\ldots,
\widehat S^{\rm wt}_{r-1})$ by
\[
 \mathrm{Transp}^{\rm wt}_{\cA, r}(\widehat S^{\rm wt}_{\bullet})
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{2 r \kappa(\cA)}
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 3 \le j \le k < r}}
 f(j, k)\, j k\, \widehat S^{\rm wt}_j\,\widehat S^{\rm wt}_k,
\]
where $f(j, k) = 1$ for $j < k$ and $f(j, j) = \tfrac{1}{2}$. The
sum runs over unordered integer pairs $(j, k)$ with $j + k = r + 2$,
$j \geq 3$, $k < r$; the endpoints $j = 2$ and $k = r$ are absorbed
into the linearised nabla-operator on $\Theta_{\cA}$ and do not
appear in the transport.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sth-why-range}Why $j \geq 3$ and $k < r$]
The constraint $j \geq 3$ arises because $j = 2$ gives $S_2 = \kappa$
as a factor, which is absorbed into the overall $1/(2 r \kappa)$
prefactor and becomes part of the linearised operator $\nabla_H$
rather than an obstruction. The constraint $k < r$ is the basic
inductive property: the transport determines $\widehat S^{\rm wt}_r$
from strictly
lower-weight data. Together these constraints force $3 \leq j \leq
(r+2)/2$ and make the recurrence closed on the lower-weight tuple
$(\widehat S^{\rm wt}_3, \ldots, \widehat S^{\rm wt}_{r-1})$.
\end{remark}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{The Virasoro shadow recurrence}
\label{sec:sth-recurrence}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence}Virasoro
weighted shadow recurrence]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For $r \geq 5$ the weighted Riccati-metric coefficient
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c)$ is
determined by the initial data
\[
 \kappa = \tfrac{c}{2}, \qquad S_3 = 2, \qquad
 S_4 = \tfrac{10}{c (5c + 22)}
\]
and the recurrence
\[
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c)
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{r c}
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 3 \le j \le k < r}}
 f(j, k)\, j k\,
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_j(\Vir_c)\,\widehat S^{\rm wt}_k(\Vir_c),
\]
with $f(j, k) = 1$ for $j < k$ and $f(j, j) = \tfrac{1}{2}$. In
particular $\widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c) \in \mathbb{Q}(c)$ for
every $r \geq 2$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The master-equation recurrence of
\texttt{higher\_genus\_modular\_koszul.tex}
(thm:obstruction-recursion) applied to a single primary line with
curvature $\kappa$ yields
\[
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_r \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{2 r \kappa}
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 3 \le j \le k < r}}
 f(j, k)\, j k\, \widehat S^{\rm wt}_j\,\widehat S^{\rm wt}_k.
\]
Specialise to $\Vir_c$: $\kappa = c/2$, so $2 r \kappa = r c$, and
the recurrence takes the stated form for the weighted metric
coefficients. The bracket
structure on a single primary is governed by the stress tensor OPE,
whose only non-central channel is the descendant $2 T(w)/(z-w)^2$
contribution; the Zamolodchikov quasi-primary
$\Lambda = {:}TT{:} - \tfrac{3}{10} \partial^2 T$ has
$\langle \Lambda \mid \Lambda \rangle = c (5c+22)/10$, which
produces the $(5c + 22)$ factor in every subsequent weighted
denominator.

Rationality in $c$ follows by induction on $r$: the initial data
$(\kappa, S_3, S_4) = (c/2, 2, 10/(c(5c+22)))$ are rational; the
recurrence is a finite rational product-sum on rational inputs,
hence preserves rationality.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sth-two-chains}Two disjoint derivation
chains]
The same $\widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c)$ is produced by the Riccati
$\sqrt{Q_L}$ Taylor expansion
\[
 Q_L(t) \;=\; 4 \kappa^2 + 12 \kappa\, S_3\, t +
 (9 S_3^2 + 16 \kappa\, S_4)\, t^2,
 \qquad
 H_{\rm wt}(t) \;=\; t^2 \sqrt{Q_L(t)}
 \;=\; \sum_{r \geq 2} r\,\widehat S^{\rm wt}_r\, t^r.
\]
Chain (A) is the master-equation combinatorial recurrence of
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence}; chain (B) is the
analytic square-root Taylor expansion. Agreement of (A) with (B)
is the content of thm:riccati-algebraicity
(higher\_genus\_modular\_koszul.tex), and is cross-checked
numerically at $c \in \{1, 1/2, 13, 25\}$ through $r = 8$ by
\texttt{test\_shadow\_tower\_higher.py}
(\texttt{test\_virasoro\_shadow\_recurrence\_cross\_check}).
\end{remark}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Closed forms through weight 8}
\label{sec:sth-s6-s7-s8}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\subsection{Weight 6}
\label{sec:sth-s6}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:s6-virasoro-closed-form}Closed form for
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_6(\Vir_c)$]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The weight-$6$ weighted Riccati-metric coefficient is
\[
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_6(\Vir_c)
 \;=\; \frac{80\,(45 c + 193)}{3\, c^{3}\, (5 c + 22)^{2}}
 \;\in\; \mathbb{Q}(c).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
At $r = 6$ the transport sum runs over pairs $(j, k)$ with
$j + k = 8$, $3 \leq j \leq k < 6$: namely $(j, k) = (3, 5)$ and
$(j, k) = (4, 4)$. Applying the recurrence of
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence},
\[
 S_6
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{6 c}
 \bigl[\, 3 \cdot 5 \cdot S_3 S_5 + \tfrac{1}{2} \cdot 4 \cdot 4 \cdot S_4^2 \,\bigr]
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{6 c}
 \bigl[\, 15 \cdot 2 \cdot S_5 + 8\, S_4^2 \,\bigr].
\]
Substituting $S_4 = 10/(c (5c+22))$ and
$S_5 = -48/(c^2(5c+22))$:
\[
 S_6
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{6 c}
 \left[\, 30 \cdot \tfrac{-48}{c^2 (5c+22)}
 + 8 \cdot \tfrac{100}{c^2 (5c + 22)^2} \,\right]
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{6 c} \cdot
 \frac{-1440 (5 c + 22) + 800}{c^2 (5 c + 22)^2}.
\]
Simplify the numerator:
\[
 -1440 (5 c + 22) + 800
 \;=\; -7200 c - 31680 + 800
 \;=\; -7200 c - 30880
 \;=\; -160 \cdot (45 c + 193).
\]
Hence
\[
 S_6
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{6 c} \cdot \frac{-160 (45 c + 193)}{c^2 (5 c + 22)^2}
 \;=\; \frac{160 (45 c + 193)}{6\, c^3 (5 c + 22)^2}
 \;=\; \frac{80 (45 c + 193)}{3\, c^3 (5 c + 22)^2},
\]
as stated.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sth-s6-pole}Pole structure at $r = 6$]
The denominator $c^{3} (5 c + 22)^{2}$ encodes two structural facts:
\begin{enumerate}
\item $c^{3}$: each application of the recurrence introduces a
 factor of $c$ from the $1/(r c)$ prefactor, producing $c^{r-3}$
 at weight $r$ (confirmed $c^{1}, c^{2}, c^{3}$ at $r = 4, 5, 6$).
\item $(5 c + 22)^{2}$: the Zamolodchikov $\Lambda$-channel
 contraction contributes one factor of $(5 c + 22)^{-1}$ whenever
 a Virasoro descendant chain of weight $\geq 4$ is re-contracted;
 weights $r = 4, 5$ contribute one factor and the re-contraction
 at $r = 6$ elevates the power to $2$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{remark}

\subsection{Weight 7}
\label{sec:sth-s7}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:s7-virasoro-closed-form}Closed form for
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_7(\Vir_c)$]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The weight-$7$ weighted Riccati-metric coefficient is
\[
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_7(\Vir_c)
 \;=\; \frac{-2880\,(15 c + 61)}{7\, c^{4}\, (5 c + 22)^{2}}
 \;\in\; \mathbb{Q}(c).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
At $r = 7$ the transport sum runs over pairs $(j, k)$ with
$j + k = 9$, $3 \leq j \leq k < 7$: namely $(3, 6)$ and $(4, 5)$
(the pair $(j, k) = (5, 4)$ is identified with $(4, 5)$ and the
degenerate pair $j = k$ does not occur for $j + k = 9$). Hence
\[
 S_7
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{7 c}
 \bigl[\, 3 \cdot 6 \cdot S_3 S_6 + 4 \cdot 5 \cdot S_4 S_5 \,\bigr]
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{7 c}
 \bigl[\, 18 \cdot 2 \cdot S_6 + 20\, S_4 S_5 \,\bigr].
\]
Substitute the known closed forms:
\[
 S_6 = \tfrac{80 (45 c + 193)}{3 c^3 (5c+22)^2}, \quad
 S_4 S_5
 = \tfrac{10}{c (5c+22)} \cdot \tfrac{-48}{c^2 (5c+22)}
 = \tfrac{-480}{c^3 (5c + 22)^2}.
\]
Then
\[
 S_7
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{7 c}
 \left[\, 36 \cdot \tfrac{80 (45 c + 193)}{3 c^3 (5c+22)^2}
 + 20 \cdot \tfrac{-480}{c^3 (5c+22)^2} \,\right]
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{7 c} \cdot
 \frac{960 (45 c + 193) - 9600}{c^3 (5 c + 22)^2}.
\]
Simplify the numerator:
\[
 960 (45 c + 193) - 9600
 \;=\; 43200 c + 185280 - 9600
 \;=\; 43200 c + 175680
 \;=\; 2880 (15 c + 61).
\]
Therefore
\[
 S_7
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{7 c} \cdot \frac{2880\,(15 c + 61)}{c^{3} (5 c + 22)^{2}}
 \;=\; \frac{-2880\,(15 c + 61)}{7\, c^{4}\, (5 c + 22)^{2}},
\]
as claimed.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sth-s7-parity}On $S_7$ sign and parity]
Unlike the ordered bar on a single-line abelian chiral algebra, the
Virasoro shadow does not enforce $S_{2k+1} = 0$ for any $k$: the
cubic $S_3 = 2$ is manifestly nonzero (it records the three-point
Ward identity of $T(z)$), and the odd-weight $S_5, S_7$ inherit
nonzero values. The alternating sign pattern
$S_4 > 0$, $S_5 < 0$, $S_6 > 0$, $S_7 < 0$ reflects the sign of the
transport operator $-1/(r c)$ applied to a product of
positive-leading-coefficient lower-weight shadows.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Weight 8}
\label{sec:sth-s8}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:s8-virasoro-closed-form}Closed form for
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_8(\Vir_c)$]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The weight-$8$ weighted Riccati-metric coefficient is
\[
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_8(\Vir_c)
 \;=\; \frac{80\,(2025 c^{2} + 16470 c + 33314)}
 {c^{5}\, (5 c + 22)^{3}}
 \;\in\; \mathbb{Q}(c).
\]
In particular $\widehat S^{\rm wt}_8(\Vir_1) = 4144720/19683$,
matching the Vol III $m_8$ identity at the weighted specialisation
$c = 1$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
At $r = 8$ the transport sum runs over pairs $(j, k)$ with
$j + k = 10$, $3 \leq j \leq k < 8$: namely $(3, 7)$, $(4, 6)$, and
$(5, 5)$. Applying the recurrence:
\[
 S_8
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{8 c}
 \bigl[\, 3 \cdot 7 \cdot S_3 S_7 + 4 \cdot 6 \cdot S_4 S_6
 + \tfrac{1}{2} \cdot 5 \cdot 5 \cdot S_5^2 \,\bigr]
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{8 c}
 \bigl[\, 21 \cdot 2 \cdot S_7 + 24\, S_4 S_6 + \tfrac{25}{2}\, S_5^2 \,\bigr].
\]
Substitute the closed forms from
Theorems~\ref{thm:s6-virasoro-closed-form}
and~\ref{thm:s7-virasoro-closed-form}:
\begin{align*}
 42\, S_7 &= 42 \cdot \tfrac{-2880 (15 c + 61)}{7 c^4 (5c + 22)^2}
 = \tfrac{-17280 (15 c + 61)}{c^4 (5c + 22)^2}, \\
 24\, S_4 S_6 &= 24 \cdot \tfrac{10}{c(5c+22)}
 \cdot \tfrac{80 (45 c + 193)}{3 c^3 (5c+22)^2}
 = \tfrac{6400 (45 c + 193)}{c^4 (5c + 22)^3}, \\
 \tfrac{25}{2}\, S_5^2 &= \tfrac{25}{2} \cdot
 \tfrac{(-48)^2}{c^4 (5c+22)^2}
 = \tfrac{28800}{c^4 (5c+22)^2}.
\end{align*}
Place everything over the common denominator
$c^4 (5 c + 22)^3$:
\begin{align*}
 42\, S_7 \cdot (5 c + 22)
 &= \tfrac{-17280 (15 c + 61)(5 c + 22)}{c^4 (5c+22)^3}, \\
 24\, S_4 S_6
 &= \tfrac{6400 (45 c + 193)}{c^4 (5c+22)^3}, \\
 \tfrac{25}{2}\, S_5^2 \cdot (5 c + 22)
 &= \tfrac{28800 (5 c + 22)}{c^4 (5c+22)^3}.
\end{align*}
Expand the numerators:
\begin{align*}
 -17280 (15 c + 61)(5 c + 22)
 &= -17280 (75 c^{2} + 330 c + 305 c + 1342) \\
 &= -17280 (75 c^{2} + 635 c + 1342), \\
 6400 (45 c + 193)
 &= 288000 c + 1235200, \\
 28800 (5 c + 22)
 &= 144000 c + 633600.
\end{align*}
Combine:
\begin{align*}
 -17280 \cdot 75 c^{2}
 &= -1296000 c^{2}, \\
 -17280 \cdot 635 c + 288000 c + 144000 c
 &= -10972800 c + 432000 c
 \;=\; -10540800 c, \\
 -17280 \cdot 1342 + 1235200 + 633600
 &= -23189760 + 1868800
 \;=\; -21320960.
\end{align*}
So the combined numerator is
\[
 -1296000\, c^{2} \;-\; 10540800\, c \;-\; 21320960
 \;=\; -640 \cdot (2025 c^{2} + 16470 c + 33314).
\]
Dividing by $8 c$ (and flipping sign from the overall $-1/(8 c)$
prefactor):
\[
 S_8
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{8 c} \cdot
 \frac{-640\, (2025 c^{2} + 16470 c + 33314)}{c^{4} (5 c + 22)^{3}}
 \;=\; \frac{80\, (2025 c^{2} + 16470 c + 33314)}{c^{5} (5 c + 22)^{3}}.
\]
For the Vol III cross-check, substitute $c = 1$:
\[
 2025 + 16470 + 33314 \;=\; 51809,
 \qquad
 5 + 22 \;=\; 27,
 \qquad
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_8(\Vir_1) \;=\; \frac{80 \cdot 51809}{1 \cdot 27^{3}}
 \;=\; \frac{4144720}{19683}.
\]
This matches Vol III's $m_8 = 4144720/19683$ identity
(Vol III shadow-tower check through the $m_8$ row; see
\texttt{calabi-yau-quantum-groups/compute/lib/a\_infinity\_bar\_w1inf.py}:956). The Vol III
datum is computed via a categorical sl$_2$ trace on a K3-fiberwise
chiral algebra, disjoint from the present MC recursion; agreement
at $c = 1$ is a genuine cross-volume verification.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sth-zamolodchikov-multiplicity}Zamolodchikov
multiplicity]
The denominator $(5 c + 22)^{3}$ at weight $r = 8$ confirms the
pattern $(5 c + 22)^{\lfloor (r-2)/2 \rfloor}$: each pair of
successive weights introduces one additional Zamolodchikov factor
through re-contraction of the $\Lambda$ quasi-primary. Explicitly
\[
 r = 4{:} \; (5c+22)^{1}, \quad
 r = 5{:} \; (5c+22)^{1}, \quad
 r = 6{:} \; (5c+22)^{2}, \quad
 r = 7{:} \; (5c+22)^{2}, \quad
 r = 8{:} \; (5c+22)^{3}.
\]
This refines the $S_4 \sim 10/(c(5c+22))$ observation: the
Zamolodchikov factor is
structural, not an artefact of the weight-$4$ specialisation.
\end{remark}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Boundary-value checks}
\label{sec:sth-boundary}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{proposition}[\label{prop:sth-boundary-checks}Weighted boundary
values through weight 8]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The closed forms of
Theorems~\ref{thm:s6-virasoro-closed-form},~\ref{thm:s7-virasoro-closed-form},~\ref{thm:s8-virasoro-closed-form}
take the following rational values at the three canonical specialisations
$c \in \{1, \tfrac{1}{2}, 13\}$:
\[
 \begin{array}{r|ccc}
 & c = 1 & c = \tfrac{1}{2} & c = 13 \\
 \hline
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_6(\Vir_c) & \tfrac{19040}{2187} & \tfrac{551680}{7203}
 & \tfrac{62240}{49887279} \\[2pt]
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_7(\Vir_c) & -\tfrac{24320}{567} & -\tfrac{12625920}{16807}
 & -\tfrac{81920}{168138607} \\[2pt]
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_8(\Vir_c) & \tfrac{4144720}{19683} & \tfrac{861291520}{117649}
 & \tfrac{47171920}{244497554379}
 \end{array}
\]
Each entry is verified both by direct substitution into the closed-form
rational expression and, independently, by running the Riccati
$\sqrt{Q_L}$ Taylor expansion in pure \texttt{Fraction} arithmetic
to weight $8$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Direct substitution. At $c = 1$: $5 c + 22 = 27$; the closed form of
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_6$ gives $80 \cdot 238 / (3 \cdot 729) = 19040 / 2187$;
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_7$ gives
$-2880 \cdot 76 / (7 \cdot 729) = -218880 / 5103 = -24320 / 567$;
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_8$ gives $80 \cdot 51809 / 19683 = 4144720/19683$.
At $c = 1/2$:
$5c + 22 = 49/2$, so $(5c+22)^{2} = 2401/4$ and $(5c+22)^{3} =
117649/8$; combined with $c^{3} = 1/8, c^{4} = 1/16, c^{5} = 1/32$
the values reduce to $551680/7203, -12625920/16807, 861291520/117649$
respectively (elementary). At $c = 13$: $5 c + 22 = 87$; powers
and products give the stated values. The Fraction-arithmetic
independent check is implemented in
\texttt{compute/tests/test\_shadow\_tower\_higher.py}
(\texttt{test\_s6\_virasoro\_boundary\_values},
\texttt{test\_s7\_virasoro\_boundary\_values},
\texttt{test\_s8\_virasoro\_c1\_voliii\_match}), all of which pass.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sth-c13-self-dual}Self-dual point $c = 13$]
The value $c = 13$ is the Koszul self-dual point of Virasoro:
$\Vir^{!} = \Vir_{26 - c}$ is fixed by $c = 13$, and $\kappa + \kappa' =
13$ (Vol I key constants). The $S_r(\Vir_{13})$ values are not
particularly simple (they involve $87 = 5 \cdot 13 + 22$ in the
denominator), but they record the ordered shadow spectrum at the
self-dual central charge, which matters for the
complementarity-via-index statement of Koszulness
equivalence (vii) at genus $0$.
\end{remark}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Large-$c$ asymptotics}
\label{sec:sth-leading-asymp}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{proposition}[\label{prop:sth-leading-asymp}Leading large-$c$
asymptotic coefficient for the weighted tower]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
As $c \to \infty$,
\[
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c) \;\sim\; \frac{A_r}{c^{r - 2}},
 \qquad A_r \in \mathbb{Q},
\]
with
\[
 A_4 = 2, \quad A_5 = -\tfrac{48}{5}, \quad A_6 = 48, \quad
 A_7 = -\tfrac{1728}{7}, \quad A_8 = 1296.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Extract $c^{r-2}$ from the closed forms. $S_6 \sim 80 \cdot 45 c /
(3 c^{3} \cdot 25 c^{2}) = 3600 / (75 c^{4}) = 48 / c^{4}$, so
$A_6 = 48$. $S_7 \sim -2880 \cdot 15 c / (7 c^{4} \cdot 25 c^{2}) =
-43200/(175 c^{5}) = -1728 / (7 c^{5})$, so $A_7 = -1728/7$.
$S_8 \sim 80 \cdot 2025 c^{2} / (c^{5} \cdot 125 c^{3}) = 162000 /
(125 c^{6}) = 1296 / c^{6}$, so $A_8 = 1296$. The $A_4 = 2$ and
$A_5 = -48/5$ values are read off from the closed forms of
$S_4, S_5$ analogously. The \texttt{sympy.limit} computation at
\texttt{test\_virasoro\_leading\_asymptotic} confirms the five
coefficients to full symbolic precision.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sth-kummer-scope}Kummer congruences live on
$Z_g$, not on $S_r$ leading]
The leading coefficients $\{A_r\}_{r \leq 8}$ are pure $2^{a} 3^{b}$
rationals:
\[
 A_4 = 2, \quad A_5 = -\tfrac{2^{4} 3}{5}, \quad
 A_6 = 2^{4} 3, \quad
 A_7 = -\tfrac{2^{6} 3^{3}}{7}, \quad A_8 = 2^{4} 3^{4}.
\]
No Bernoulli-leading Kummer-irregular prime ($691$ or $3617$) appears in any
$A_r$ numerator through weight $8$. Extending the computation
through weight $16$ (via the same recurrence) shows that the
leading coefficients remain in the $\{2, 3, 5, 7, 11, 13, 17\}$-rough
set: $A_{12} = 1119744 = 2^{9} \cdot 3^{7}$ and
$A_{16} = 1088391168 = 2^{11} \cdot 3^{12}$. In particular the
expected Kummer primes do \emph{not} appear in the Virasoro
shadow-tower leading asymptotic.

This is not a contradiction with the Kummer-congruence prediction of
Theorem~\ref{thm:kummer-from-motivic}
(\texttt{motivic\_shadow\_tower.tex}): that prediction concerns the
$Z_g(n)$ genus-expansion numerators, linked to
$S_{2g-2}(\Vir_c)$ through the shadow-Feynman bridge
$F_g \leftrightarrow S_{2g - 2}$ and the leading Bernoulli
normalisation
$(-1)^g2^{g-1}B_{2g-2}/(2g-2)!$. The Kummer content is transferred
to $Z_g$ through the genus Bernoulli factor, not through the
Virasoro leading-$c$ behaviour of $S_{2g-2}$. The two statements
measure different arithmetic invariants and are not in conflict.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sth-alpha-asymptotic}Relation to
large-$c$ asymptotic]
The large-$c$ result $S_4(\Vir_c) \sim 2/c^{2}$ is the $A_4 =
2$ entry of Proposition~\ref{prop:sth-leading-asymp}. The
incorrect asymptotic $2/(5 c^{2})$ misses the cancellation of the
leading factor $5$ in $10/(c (5c+22))$; the correct coefficient is
$A_4=2$.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:shadow-exponential-base-Virasoro}
The shadow-exponential base of Virasoro is $C_\Vir = 6$]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The large-$r$ geometric ratio
\[
 C_\Vir \;:=\; \limsup_{r \to \infty}
 \bigl|A_{r+1}^\Vir / A_r^\Vir\bigr|
 \;=\; \lim_{r \to \infty} \frac{6 r}{r+1}
 \;=\; 6.
\]
The factor $6$ decomposes as the product of the lowest non-trivial
shadow depth $r_0 = 3$ and the Riccati seed coefficient
$S_{r_0}(\Vir) = 2$:
\[
 C_\Vir \;=\; r_0 \cdot S_{r_0}(\Vir) \;=\; 3 \cdot 2 \;=\; 6.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
From Proposition~\ref{prop:sth-leading-asymp},
$A_r^\Vir = 8 \cdot (-6)^{r-4} / r$ for $r \ge 4$ (extended from the
stated closed forms; see
\verb|compute/lib/shadow_tower_higher_vir.py::leading_asymptotic|
for the general formula). The ratio
$|A_{r+1}/A_r| = |(-6)^{r-3}/(r+1)| \cdot |r/(-6)^{r-4}|
= 6 \cdot r/(r+1) \to 6$.

The factorisation $C_\Vir = r_0 \cdot S_{r_0}$ follows from the
leading-order analysis of the rescaled Riccati recurrence
$r \cdot \Phi_r \cdot c = -\sum f(j, k) j k \Phi_j \Phi_k$ with
$\Phi_3 = 2c$ (the unique $O(c)$ seed) and $\Phi_r = A_r + O(1/c)$
for $r \ge 4$ ($O(1)$). The only $O(c)$ contribution to the
right-hand side at large $c$ comes from the $j = 3$ term; the
constraint $j + k = r + 2$ forces $k = r - 1$. Extracting:
\[
 r \cdot A_r \cdot c
 \;=\; -f(3, r-1) \cdot 3 \cdot (r-1) \cdot \Phi_3 \cdot A_{r-1}
 \;=\; -6 (r-1) c A_{r-1},
\]
so $A_r / A_{r-1} = -6 (r-1) / r$, giving $|A_r/A_{r-1}| \to 6$.
The decomposition $6 = 3 \cdot 2$ identifies the ratio base as
$r_0 \cdot S_{r_0}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:universal-class-M-C-is-6}
T-line dominance criterion for $C=6$]
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $\cA$ be an ordinary vertex algebra on~$X$ whose scalar shadow
tower is non-terminating, and fix a Virasoro sub-chiral-algebra
generated by a stress tensor~$T$ of conformal weight~$2$. Assume:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\arabic*)]
 \item the $T$-line seed is $S_3(\cA,T)=2$, as in the
 $T(z)T(w)$ OPE;
 \item for every bar-depth $r\ge3$, every generator line other than
 $T$ contributes to the leading-$c$ projection at order
 $O(c^{-\alpha})$ relative to the $T$-line, for some
 $\alpha>0$ independent of~$r$.
\end{enumerate}
Then the leading-$c$ $T$-line shadow-exponential base is
\[
 C_\cA^{T} \;=\; 6.
\]
This is a criterion for the chosen $T$-line. It is not a statement
about the total scalar shadow tower when a non-$T$ primary line
contributes at the same leading order, and it is not a statement
about strict $E_1$-chiral deformations.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Under hypotheses~(1) and~(2), the rescaled Riccati recurrence for
$\cA$ has exactly one $O(c)$ contribution on the right-hand side
(the $j = 3$ term, from $\Phi_3 = 2c$ paired with $\Phi_{r-1} =
A_{r-1} + O(1/c)$). All other contributions are $O(1)$ or smaller.
The argument of
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-exponential-base-Virasoro} carries through
uniformly in~$r$: $A_r / A_{r-1} = -6 (r-1) / r$, and
$|A_r / A_{r-1}| \to 6$.

Uniformity in~$r$: hypothesis~(2) excludes higher-$j$ cross-channel
terms from contributing at $O(c)$ at \emph{any} depth~$r$, which is
precisely the hypothesis that the $T$-line dominance is uniform.
Under this hypothesis, no bar-depth correction survives the
leading-$c$ asymptotic analysis.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:C-A-scope-E-infinity}
The scope is the ordinary vertex-algebra $T$-line]
Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-class-M-C-is-6} is restricted to
ordinary vertex algebras with a chosen stress-tensor line satisfying
the two dominance hypotheses. Strict $E_1$-chiral algebras
(Yangians, quantum vertex algebras of Etingof--Kazhdan, and
factorisation algebras on $\mathrm{Ran}^{\mathrm{ord}}(X)$) do not
automatically carry such a Virasoro primary line; when a stress
tensor exists, its ordered-bar recurrence must be computed in that
ambient category. No value of the strict $E_1$ shadow-exponential
base is asserted here.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[\label{prop:W3-T-line-matches-Vir-subleading}
$\cW_3$ $T$-line subleading asymptotic matches Virasoro]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For the principal $\cW_3$ algebra at generic central charge, the
$T$-line shadow coefficient $S_4(\cW_3, T) = 10 / [c(5c + 22)]$
has large-$c$ expansion
\[
 S_4(\cW_3, T)(c)
 \;=\;
 \frac{2}{c^2} - \frac{44}{5 c^3} + \frac{968}{25 c^4}
 - \frac{21296}{125 c^5} + \cdots,
\]
giving $A_4^{\cW_3, T} = 2$ (leading) and $B_4^{\cW_3, T} = -44/5$
(subleading), both matching the Virasoro values. The $W$-line
shadow $S_4(\cW_3, W) = 2560 / [c(5c+22)^3]$ has expansion
$S_4(\cW_3, W)(c) = 512/(25 c^4) + O(c^{-5})$, i.e.\ contributes
only at sub-sub-leading ($k \ge 2$) order and vanishes at
leading and subleading.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Direct Taylor expansion of the closed forms in $c^{-1}$ via
\verb|sympy.series|, verified against
\verb|compute/lib/shadow_tower_extended_families.py|. The $T$-line
closed form $10/[c(5c+22)]$ factors as $(10/5c^2) \cdot (1/(1 +
22/(5c)))$, whose large-$c$ expansion recovers the Virasoro
$S_4$ expansion at central charge $c$. The $W$-line closed form
carries an additional $(5c+22)^{-2}$ factor relative to the
$T$-line, pushing the leading contribution to $c^{-4}$ order.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[\label{cor:universal-class-M-subleading-uniformity}
Subleading uniformity under $T$-line dominance]
\ClaimStatusConditional
Under the hypotheses of
Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-class-M-C-is-6}, add the subleading
dominance condition that no generator line other than $T$ contributes
at $c^{-(r-1)}$ order. Then the $T$-line subleading coefficient
$B_r^{\cA,T}$ equals the Virasoro coefficient $B_r^\Vir$ at that
bar-depth. For $\cW_3$, this is verified at $r = 4$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:W3-T-line-matches-Vir-subleading}); for BP,
the same holds via the parallel analysis of
$S_4(\mathrm{BP}, T) = S_4^{\Vir}(c_{\mathrm{BP}}(k))$
(the $T$-line dominance hypotheses).

Consequently, the equalities
$\Sigma_\cA^T(z)=\Sigma_\Vir(z)$ and
$(\Sigma_\cA^T)^{(1)}(z)=\Sigma_\Vir^{(1)}(z)$ hold on any lane
where the leading and subleading dominance hypotheses have been
checked. They are not asserted for the total scalar tower of
$\cW_N$ at $N\ge4$ or for non-$T$ generator lanes without an explicit
OPE-seed computation.
\end{corollary}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:universal-class-M-verifications}
Checked instances and open mathematical conditions]
The $T$-line dominance criterion is checked symbolically for:
\begin{itemize}
 \item \emph{Virasoro} (Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-exponential-base-Virasoro}).
 \item \emph{Principal $\cW_3$}: $S_3(\cW_3, T) = 2$,
 $S_3(\cW_3, W) = 0$; T-line dominates at leading-$c$.
 Verified via
 \verb|compute/lib/shadow_tower_extended_families.py|.
 \item \emph{Bershadsky--Polyakov BP}: $S_3(\mathrm{BP}, T) = 2$,
 $S_3(\mathrm{BP}, J) = S_3(\mathrm{BP}, G^\pm) = 0$; the $J$-line
 is class~G (terminating), the $G^\pm$-line is subleading,
 only the T-line dominates. Verified via the BP block of
 \verb|compute/lib/shadow_tower_extended_families.py|.
\end{itemize}
For principal $\cW_N$ with $N\ge4$, non-logarithmic cosets, and
Schellekens holomorphic $c=24$ VOAs, the required open mathematical condition
is explicit: compute the non-$T$ generator-line seeds and prove the
uniform large-$c$ order estimate in hypothesis~(2). Lattice VOAs
$V_L$ remain class~G in the scalar shadow table of
\texttt{landscape\_census.tex}; the existence of a Sugawara stress
tensor does not by itself move them into the non-terminating
$T$-line-dominance stratum. The criterion does not extend to:
\begin{itemize}
 \item \emph{Pure Heisenberg $\cH_k$}: class~G (terminating); the
 shadow-exponential base is undefined in the non-terminating
 sense.
 \item \emph{Logarithmic $\cW(p)$}: Gevrey-$\alpha$ stratum; $C_\cA$
 is undefined because the tower growth is factorial-modified
 exponential, not pure exponential.
\end{itemize}
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:shadow-series-closed-form-Virasoro}
Closed-form Virasoro shadow series]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The leading-asymptotic generating function
$\Sigma_\Vir(z) := \sum_{r \ge 4} A_r^\Vir z^r$ has the closed form
\[
 \Sigma_\Vir(z)
 \;=\;
 \frac{4}{9} z^3 \;-\; \frac{1}{9} z^2 \;+\; \frac{1}{27} z
 \;-\; \frac{1}{162} \log(1 + 6 z).
\]
The function is holomorphic on the slit plane after a choice of
branch for $\log(1+6z)$ and has a \emph{logarithmic branch point}
at~$z = -1/6$; the radius of convergence of the Taylor series is
$1/6$, matching $C_\Vir = 6$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Starting from $A_r = 8 (-6)^{r-4}/r$ (valid for $r \ge 4$) and
making the substitution $u = -6 z$:
\[
 \Sigma_\Vir(z)
 \;=\;
 \sum_{r=4}^{\infty} \frac{8 (-6)^{r-4}}{r} z^r
 \;=\;
 \frac{8 z^4}{u^4} \sum_{k=0}^{\infty} \frac{u^k}{k + 4}.
\]
The tail sum is the standard log-generating function shifted by
four terms:
\[
\sum_{k=0}^{\infty} \frac{u^k}{k+4}
= u^{-4} \sum_{m=4}^{\infty} \frac{u^m}{m}
= u^{-4} [-\log(1 - u) - u - u^2/2 - u^3/3],
\]
after absorbing the four missing low-order terms. Substituting
$u = -6z$ gives $1 - u = 1 + 6z$ and
\begin{align*}
 \Sigma_\Vir(z)
 &= 8 z^4 \cdot (-6z)^{-4} \cdot \bigl[-\log(1 + 6z) + 6z - 18 z^2
 + 72 z^3\bigr] \\
 &= \frac{8}{1296}
 \bigl[-\log(1 + 6z) + 6z - 18 z^2 + 72 z^3\bigr] \\
 &= \frac{1}{162}
 \bigl[-\log(1 + 6z) + 6z - 18 z^2 + 72 z^3\bigr] \\
 &= \frac{4 z^3}{9} - \frac{z^2}{9} + \frac{z}{27}
 - \frac{\log(1 + 6z)}{162}.
\end{align*}
The logarithmic branch point is at~$z = -1/6$. Taylor expansion to
order~$z^9$ (checked symbolically via
\verb|sympy.series|) reproduces
$\{A_4, \ldots, A_9\} = \{2, -48/5, 48, -1728/7, 1296, -6912\}$,
confirming the closed form.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:shadow-series-closed-form-Virasoro-subleading}
Closed-form subleading Virasoro shadow series]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The subleading-asymptotic generating function $\Sigma_\Vir^{(1)}(z)
:= \sum_{r \ge 4} B_r^\Vir z^r$, where $B_r^\Vir = -4 (-6)^{r-4}
(5 r^2 - 45 r + 496) / (45 r)$, has the closed form
\[
 \Sigma_\Vir^{(1)}(z)
 \;=\;
 \frac{16 z^5}{(6z + 1)^2}
 \;+\; \frac{20 z^4}{9 (6z + 1)^2}
 \;-\; \frac{992 z^3}{405}
 \;+\; \frac{248 z^2}{405}
 \;-\; \frac{248 z}{1215}
 \;+\; \frac{124 \log(6z + 1)}{3645}.
\]
Singular structure at $z = -1/6$: a \emph{double pole} combined
with a logarithmic branch point.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Starting from $B_r = -(4/45) \cdot (-6)^{r-4} \cdot (5r^2 - 45r + 496)/r$,
factoring out $1/r$ to get $(5r^2 - 45r + 496)/r = 5r - 45 + 496/r$,
and evaluating three standard sums under the substitution $u = -6z$:
\[
 \sum_{r \ge 4} r \cdot u^{r-4}
 \;=\;
 \frac{4 - 3u}{(1 - u)^2},
 \qquad
 \sum_{r \ge 4} u^{r-4}
 \;=\;
 \frac{1}{1 - u},
 \qquad
 \sum_{r \ge 4} \frac{u^{r-4}}{r}
 \;=\;
 \frac{1}{u^4}\bigl[-\log(1 - u) - u - \tfrac{u^2}{2} - \tfrac{u^3}{3}\bigr].
\]
Substituting these into
\[
 \Sigma_\Vir^{(1)}(z) = -\frac{4}{45} z^4
 \bigl[5 \cdot \textstyle\sum r u^{r-4}
 - 45 \cdot \sum u^{r-4}
 + 496 \cdot \sum u^{r-4}/r\bigr],
\]
simplifying, and expanding polynomially yields the stated closed
form. Taylor expansion to order $z^{11}$ (checked symbolically via
\verb|sympy.series|) reproduces $\{B_4, \ldots, B_{11}\} =
\{-44/5, 1056/25, -3248/15, 40896/35, -32832/5, 190464/5,
-5660928/25, 75396096/55\}$, confirming the closed form.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:subleading-sharper-singularity}
Subleading series strengthens the singularity to a double pole]
The leading series $\Sigma_\Vir(z)$ has only a logarithmic branch
point at $z = -1/6$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-series-closed-form-Virasoro}). The
subleading series $\Sigma_\Vir^{(1)}(z)$ has, at the same point,
both a logarithmic branch AND a double pole $(6z + 1)^{-2}$. The
singularity strength strictly increases at higher orders of the
$1/c$ expansion.

The pattern for higher orders: $\Sigma_\Vir^{(k)}(z)$ has a pole
of order $2k$ at $z = -1/6$ plus a logarithmic branch point. For
$k = 2$ (sub-subleading), this gives a pole of order~$4$. Verified
symbolically:
\[
 \Sigma_\Vir^{(2)}(z)
 \;=\;
 \frac{P_4(z) + Q_4(z) \log(6z + 1)}{164025 \cdot (6z + 1)^4},
\]
where $P_4(z)$ is a polynomial of degree~$7$ and $Q_4(z)$ is a
polynomial of degree~$4$, with specific coefficients derivable from
the sum decomposition
\[
 \Sigma_\Vir^{(2)}(z)
 \;=\;
 \frac{484}{25}\, \Sigma_\Vir(z)
 + \frac{22}{45}\bigl[z^2 \Sigma_\Vir'' - 8 z \Sigma_\Vir' + 20 \Sigma_\Vir\bigr]
 + \frac{1}{972}\bigl[z^4 \Sigma_\Vir^{(4)} + 6 z^3 \Sigma_\Vir^{(3)}
 + 7 z^2 \Sigma_\Vir'' + z \Sigma_\Vir' - 22 (\ldots) + \ldots\bigr],
\]
applied to the closed form of
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-series-closed-form-Virasoro}.
The $(6z + 1)^4$ denominator arises from the fourth derivative of
$-\log(1 + 6z)/162$, which produces $(6z + 1)^{-4}$ via FaĂ  di
Bruno. Taylor expansion to order~$z^{11}$ reproduces the engine's
sub-subleading coefficients exactly.

The singular surface of the full shadow tower summed over all
$1/c$ orders is therefore not a pure logarithmic branch point
but a \emph{confluent} singularity at $z = -1/6$, mixing a
sequence of polar singularities of increasing order with the
logarithmic branch. This is the genuine singular structure
encoded by the shadow-exponential base $C_\Vir = 6$.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:pole-doubling-all-k}
Pole-doubling pattern for all $k$]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For every $k \ge 0$, the $k$-th-order $1/c$ asymptotic shadow series
\[
 \Sigma_\Vir^{(k)}(z) \;:=\; \sum_{r \ge 4} A_r^{(k)} z^r,
 \qquad
 \Phi_r(c) \;=\; \sum_{k \ge 0} \frac{A_r^{(k)}}{c^k}
 \;=\; A_r^{\Vir} \cdot \varphi_k(r) \;+\; (\text{lower-order in } r),
\]
has a pole of order $2k$ at $z = -1/6$ combined with a logarithmic
branch point, of the schematic form
\[
 \Sigma_\Vir^{(k)}(z)
 \;=\;
 \frac{P_k(z) \;+\; Q_k(z) \log(1 + 6z)}{(1 + 6z)^{2k}},
\]
where $P_k, Q_k \in \mathbb{Q}[z]$ are polynomials with
$\deg P_k \le 2k + 3$ and $\deg Q_k \le 2k$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
The coefficient polynomial $\varphi_k(r)$ in the $1/c^k$ asymptotic
expansion of $\Phi_r(c)$ has degree $2k$ in $r$. For $k = 0$:
$\varphi_0(r) = 1$ (constant). For $k = 1$: $\varphi_1(r) =
-(1/45) \cdot (5 r^2 - 45 r + 496)$ (quadratic in $r$). For
$k = 2$: $\varphi_2(r) = 484/25 + (22/45)(r-4)(r-5) +
(r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)/972$ (quartic). In general the degree-$2k$
structure follows from the recursive structure of the rescaled
Riccati: each higher-order correction in $1/c$ doubles the maximum
polynomial degree in $r$.

Applied to the $r$-polynomial via the operator identities
$z^j d^j/dz^j \cdot \sum A_r z^r = \sum r(r-1)\cdots(r-j+1) A_r z^r$
and Stirling-number re-expansion from falling factorials to
monomials, the degree-$2k$ polynomial action on $\Sigma_\Vir(z)$
produces at most $z^{2k} d^{2k}/dz^{2k}$. Since $\Sigma_\Vir(z) =
-\log(1 + 6z)/162 + (\text{polynomial in } z)$, and
$d^{2k}/dz^{2k}[-\log(1+6z)/162] = (2k-1)! \cdot 6^{2k} /
(162 \cdot (1+6z)^{2k})$ (the $(-1)^{2k}=+1$ factor from
even-order differentiation of $\log$ gives a positive sign), the
pole structure of
$\Sigma_\Vir^{(k)}$ carries a factor $(1+6z)^{-2k}$. The
polynomial part and the log-branch contribute polynomial
numerators $P_k, Q_k$ bounded by the degree constraints above.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[\label{prop:phi-k-leading-coefficient-arithmetic}
Arithmetic of the leading $\varphi_k$ coefficient]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For $k \ge 1$, the leading $r$-coefficient of $\varphi_k(r)$ (the
polynomial in $r$ appearing as
$\Phi_r(c) - \Phi_r^{(<k)}(c) = A_r \cdot \varphi_k(r)/c^k +
O(c^{-k-1})$) satisfies
\[
 \text{leading coeff of } \varphi_k(r)
 \;=\;
 \frac{(-1)^k}{2^{2k-2} \cdot 3^{3k-1}}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Verified symbolically at $k = 1, 2, 3$:
\begin{itemize}
 \item $k = 1$: leading coefficient is $-(5/45) = -1/9 = -1/(2^0 \cdot 3^2)$;
 matches with the exponent assignment $2k - 2 = 0$, $3k - 1 = 2$,
 sign $(-1)^1 = -1$.
 \item $k = 2$: leading coefficient is $1/972 = 1/(2^2 \cdot 3^5)$;
 $2k - 2 = 2$, $3k - 1 = 5$, sign $(-1)^2 = +1$.
 \item $k = 3$: leading coefficient is $-1/104976 = -1/(2^4 \cdot 3^8)$;
 $2k - 2 = 4$, $3k - 1 = 8$, sign $(-1)^3 = -1$.
\end{itemize}
The pattern follows from the Riccati recurrence structure: the
leading $r$-power contribution at each $1/c$ order doubles the
exponent (from $2(k-1)$ to $2k$) via the $j = 3$ dominant term, and
the constant prefactor accumulates a factor of $-1/108 = -1/(2^2
\cdot 3^3)$ per iteration. The ratio of consecutive leading
coefficients is verified to be uniformly $-1/108$:
\[
 \frac{\varphi_2^{\mathrm{lead}}}{\varphi_1^{\mathrm{lead}}}
 \;=\;
 \frac{1/972}{-1/9}
 \;=\;
 -\frac{1}{108},
 \qquad
 \frac{\varphi_3^{\mathrm{lead}}}{\varphi_2^{\mathrm{lead}}}
 \;=\;
 \frac{-1/104976}{1/972}
 \;=\;
 -\frac{1}{108}.
\]
The exponent shift per iteration is $(+2, +3)$ in $(2\text{-adic},
3\text{-adic})$ valuation, matching $108 = 2^2 \cdot 3^3$.
Induction on $k$ using this uniform ratio yields the stated
$2^{2k-2} \cdot 3^{3k-1}$ denominator.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:phi-k-arithmetic-significance}
\{$2$, $3$\}-adic structure of the Virasoro shadow]
The clean $\{2, 3\}$-adic content $2^{2k-2} \cdot 3^{3k-1}$ of the
leading $\varphi_k$ denominator reflects the arithmetic of the
Riccati recurrence at the Virasoro seed. No primes $p \ne 2, 3$
appear in the leading-$r$ denominators at any $k$; the purity
applies specifically to the leading-$r$ coefficient of
$\varphi_k(r)$ (see
Remark~\ref{rem:sub-leading-r-arithmetic-ramification} for the
sub-leading-$r$ structure). This is consistent
with the absence of Kummer-irregular primes (the first of which is
$691$) in the leading Laurent asymptotic of the Virasoro shadow
tower (Remark~\ref{rem:sth-kummer-scope}). The $\{2, 3\}$-structure
arises from the per-iteration factor $108 = 2^2 \cdot 3^3$, which
itself decomposes as $108 = 4 \cdot 27 = (r_0 \cdot S_{r_0}
(\Vir))^{?}$. Explicitly:
\begin{itemize}
 \item $r_0 \cdot S_{r_0}(\Vir) = 3 \cdot 2 = 6$, decomposing as
 $C_\Vir = 2 \cdot 3$; each factor squared gives
 $6^2 = 36 = 2^2 \cdot 3^2$.
 \item The extra factor of $3$ in $108 = 36 \cdot 3$ comes from the
 additional subleading-pair contribution of the Riccati kernel
 at $j = 3, k = r - 1$, which scales linearly with $r$ at
 $r \to \infty$.
 \item The Riccati kernel $f(j, k) \in \{1/2, 1\}$ contributes
 exclusively $2$-adic content at the doubling-pair terms.
\end{itemize}
The $\{2, 3\}$-arithmetic of the leading coefficients is an
\emph{invariant} of the checked $T$-line dominance lane; by
Corollary~\ref{cor:universal-class-M-subleading-uniformity} the
same $2^{2k-2} \cdot 3^{3k-1}$ structure applies only after the
dominance hypotheses have been verified for the chosen line.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[\label{cor:arithmetic-uniformity-class-M}
$\{2, 3\}$-adic arithmetic on a dominated $T$-line]
\ClaimStatusConditional
For every ordinary vertex algebra $\cA$ satisfying the $T$-line
dominance hypotheses of Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-class-M-C-is-6},
the leading-$r$ coefficient of $\varphi_k^\cA(r)$ equals
$(-1)^k/(2^{2k-2} \cdot 3^{3k-1})$ at the $T$-line leading $1/c$
order, identical to Virasoro.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-class-M-C-is-6} and Corollary
\ref{cor:universal-class-M-subleading-uniformity}, the $T$-line
leading-$c$ asymptotic of $\cA$ coincides with Virasoro's at all
$k$. The leading-$r$ coefficient of $\varphi_k^\cA(r)$ is therefore
equal to $\varphi_k^\Vir(r)$'s leading-$r$ coefficient,
namely $(-1)^k/(2^{2k-2} \cdot 3^{3k-1})$ per Proposition~
\ref{prop:phi-k-leading-coefficient-arithmetic}. For $\cW_3$ and BP
this is a checked $T$-line statement. For $\cW_N$ at $N\ge4$,
non-logarithmic cosets, and Schellekens VOAs it is a proof
obligation, not a theorem of this chapter.

The sub-leading-$r$ content may differ between algebras (e.g.\
the prime $31$ appearing in Virasoro's $\varphi_1$ from $496 =
\dim \mathfrak{so}(32)$ is Virasoro-specific), but the leading-$r$
$\{2, 3\}$-adic structure is invariant on every checked dominated
$T$-line.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sub-leading-r-arithmetic-ramification}
Sub-leading-$r$ content of $\varphi_k$ ramifies through additional primes]
Proposition~\ref{prop:phi-k-leading-coefficient-arithmetic} applies
\emph{only} to the leading-$r$ coefficient. The sub-leading-$r$
coefficients of $\varphi_k(r)$ carry primes beyond $\{2, 3\}$:
\begin{itemize}
 \item $\varphi_1(r) = -(5 r^2 - 45 r + 496)/45$. Leading $-r^2/9$
 is $\{2, 3\}$-adic; constant term $-496/45$ factors as
 $-2^4 \cdot 31 / (3^2 \cdot 5)$, introducing primes $5$ and
 $31$ (the latter via $496 = \dim \mathfrak{so}(32) = \dim
 (\mathfrak{e}_8 \oplus \mathfrak{e}_8)$, a signature
 familiar from heterotic anomaly cancellation).
 \item $\varphi_2(r) = 484/25 + (22/45)(r-4)(r-5) +
 (r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)/972$. Leading $r^4/972$ is $\{2, 3\}$-adic;
 the constant term $484/25 = 2^2 \cdot 11^2 / 5^2$ and the
 linear-in-$(r-4)$ term $(22/45)(r-4)(r-5)$ introduce primes
 $5$ and $11$.
\end{itemize}
The full $\varphi_k(r)$ denominator prime content is $\{2, 3\} \cup
S_k$ where $S_k$ is a finite set of non-$\{2, 3\}$ primes reflecting
Virasoro Zamolodchikov OPE structure constants. Only the leading-$r$
coefficient is uniformly $\{2, 3\}$-adic; sub-leading-$r$ structure
ramifies through additional primes $\{5, 11, 31, \ldots\}$ as a
specific arithmetic signature of the subleading Riccati mixing at
$c^{-k}$ order.

This refines the Kummer-arithmetic picture:
the leading-$r$ invariant is free of the Bernoulli-leading pair
$\{691,3617\}$; sub-leading-$r$ structure can carry
Kummer-irregular primes at other Bernoulli indices. The distinction
between size-order and Bernoulli-index order is recorded in
Theorem~\ref{thm:kummer-laurent-depth-controlled}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:pole-doubling-k3-verification}
Numerical verification at $k = 3$ (sub-sub-subleading)]
Using the engine's \verb|sub_sub_subleading_asymptotic(r)|, the
ratio $\Delta_r / A_r$ at $r = 4, 5, \ldots, 11$:
\[
 \left\{-\tfrac{10648}{125}, -\tfrac{10648}{125}, -\tfrac{34364}{375},
 -\tfrac{13068}{125}, -\tfrac{419276}{3375}, -\tfrac{510796}{3375},
 -\tfrac{17029417}{91125}, -\tfrac{21155527}{91125}\right\},
\]
which a degree-$6$ polynomial in $r$ fits exactly:
\[
 \frac{\Delta_r}{A_r}
 \;=\;
 -\frac{r^6}{104976}
 + \frac{13 r^5}{34992}
 - \frac{10253 r^4}{524880}
 + \frac{2261 r^3}{6480}
 - \frac{7730987 r^2}{1312200}
 + \frac{4185679 r}{109350}
 - \frac{4911664}{30375}.
\]
The leading coefficient $-1/104976 = -1/(2^4 \cdot 3^8)$ has
clean $2$-adic and $3$-adic content, reflecting the underlying
Riccati recurrence arithmetic. Degree-$6 = 2 \cdot 3$ confirms
$\deg \varphi_3 = 2 k$ for $k = 3$, in accordance with
Theorem~\ref{thm:pole-doubling-all-k}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:pole-doubling-confluent-singularity}
Confluent singularity at $z = -1/6$]
The $k \to \infty$ limit of the pole structure is a
\emph{confluent singularity} at $z = -1/6$: at each order in the
$1/c$ asymptotic expansion, the singularity strengthens by a factor
of $(1+6z)^{-2}$. The full shadow series at fixed finite $c$,
\[
 \tilde\Sigma_\Vir^{\rm wt}(z, c)
 \;=\; \sum_{r \ge 4} \widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c) z^r,
\]
has radius of convergence $c/6$ (not $1/6$); as $c \to \infty$, the
radius shrinks to $0$ while the $1/c$-coefficient-wise singular
structure progressively concentrates at $z = -1/6$. The universal
singularity at $z = -1/6$ is an artifact of the $c \to \infty$
limit's interchange with the series expansion, not a singularity
of $\tilde\Sigma$ at any finite $c$.

Conditional on the Theorem~F holographic functor, the same analytic
datum becomes a source-coupling obstruction for the large-$c$
expansion: the coefficient-wise expansion is holomorphic for
the checked $T$-line on $|z|<1/6$, and continuation beyond that
circle requires a finite-$c$ resummation. This paragraph is an
interpretation of the proved radius statement, not an additional
bulk reconstruction theorem.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:Sigma-branch-singularity}
The logarithmic branch at $z = -1/6$]
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-series-closed-form-Virasoro} identifies the
shadow-exponential base $C_\Vir = 6$ with a specific analytic
feature: the position of the \emph{unique} logarithmic branch point
of~$\Sigma_\Vir(z)$. The branch point is at $z = -1/6$, on the real
axis, with the monodromy around it given by the classical
$\log(1 + 6z) \mapsto \log(1 + 6z) + 2\pi i$ path.

For every lane satisfying Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-class-M-C-is-6},
the same leading $T$-line computation gives a logarithmic branch
point at $z=-1/6$ (up to the stated subleading corrections). No
claim is made here about non-$T$ lanes or about the total scalar
series before channel summation has been controlled.
If the Theorem~F dictionary identifies $z$ with a source coupling,
the monodromy
$\log(1+6z)\mapsto\log(1+6z)+2\pi i$ is the analytic datum that the
functor must carry. The chapter proves the shadow-side branch and
monodromy; it does not reconstruct a physical bulk theory from this
branch point alone.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[\label{prop:C-A-inverse-radius}
$C_\cA$ is the inverse radius of convergence of the shadow series]
\ClaimStatusConditional
For any formal shadow series with shadow-exponential base $C_\cA$,
\[
 \Sigma_\cA(z) \;:=\; \sum_{r \ge r_0} A_r z^r
\]
has radius of convergence equal to $1/C_\cA$. For $\cA = \Vir$ and
for every checked $T$-line satisfying
Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-class-M-C-is-6},
\[
 \rho(\Sigma_\cA) \;=\; 1/6,
 \qquad
 \text{i.e.\ } \Sigma_\cA(z) \text{ is holomorphic on } |z| < 1/6.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Use the root-growth definition
$C_\cA=\limsup_{r\to\infty}|A_r|^{1/r}$; when the consecutive
ratio has a limit, as in the Virasoro and checked $T$-line cases
below, it equals this root-growth constant. The
Cauchy--Hadamard formula gives
$\rho(\Sigma_\cA)=1/\limsup |A_r|^{1/r}=1/C_\cA$. For
Virasoro, $C_\Vir = 6$ by
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-exponential-base-Virasoro}, so
$\rho(\Sigma_\Vir) = 1/6$. For any checked $T$-line satisfying
Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-class-M-C-is-6}, the same criterion gives
$C=6$, hence $\rho=1/6$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:shadow-series-analytic-stratification}
Shadow-series analytic stratification]
Proposition~\ref{prop:C-A-inverse-radius} reframes the four-stratum
decomposition at the $r$-index as a stratification of the
\emph{radius of convergence} of $\Sigma_\cA$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
 \item \emph{Polynomial / terminating.} $\Sigma_\cA$ is a
 polynomial in $z$ (finite tail). Radius $=\infty$.
 \item \emph{Exponential $C = 6$.} The checked $T$-line series is
 analytic on $|z| < 1/6$; singularities lie on the circle
 $|z| = 1/6$ for that lane. Virasoro, the $\cW_3$ $T$-line, and the
 BP $T$-line are the verified non-logarithmic class~M instances here.
 \item \emph{Gevrey-$\alpha$.} $\Sigma_\cA$ is a \emph{formal
 series with radius of convergence $0$}, Borel-summable of
 Gevrey order $\alpha$. Logarithmic C$_2$-cofinite; $\cW(p)$.
 \item \emph{Non-Borel-summable.} Radius $0$; not Borel-summable.
\end{enumerate}

The C$=6$ lane is thus a convergent shadow series with radius of
convergence $1/6$. Two algebras satisfying the same $T$-line
dominance hypotheses have their checked $T$-line series analytic on
the same disk; this does not decide the summed scalar series before
non-$T$ channels are controlled.

\textbf{Analytic input for Theorem F.} Any Theorem~F holographic
realisation using this shadow series must distinguish:
\begin{itemize}
 \item \emph{Convergent shadow series.} The checked $T$-line series
 has a genuine analytic disk and supplies the analytic input required
 by an $(\infty,2)$-adjoint equivalence.
 \item \emph{Divergent-but-Gevrey shadow series.} The logarithmic
 $\cW(p)$ lane requires Borel resummation before it can feed an
 $(\infty,1)$-adjoint morphism; the Gurarie--Flohr Massey obstruction
 measures the missing $(\infty,2)$ upgrade.
 \item \emph{Non-Borel-summable shadow series.} No analytic input for
 a holographic functor is supplied by the shadow series alone.
\end{itemize}
The three layers are analytic constraints on $\Sigma_\cA(z)$, not
bulk-existence theorems.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:cross-volume-leading-vs-finite-c}
Cross-volume coherence: leading-$c$ vs fixed-$c$ shadow regimes]
There are three distinct analytic regimes.

First, the coefficient-wise large-$c$ expansion of the weighted tower
has leading series
$\Sigma_\Vir(z)=\sum_{r\ge4}A_rz^r$ with logarithmic branch point
at $z=-1/6$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-series-closed-form-Virasoro}).
This is a statement about the Laurent coefficient
$A_r=\lim_{c\to\infty}c^{r-2}\widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c)$, not
about the finite-$c$ shadow series.

Second, for fixed $c_0$ the ordinary series
$\widetilde\Sigma_\Vir(z,c_0)=
\sum_r\widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_{c_0})z^r$ is a different
resummation problem. A Gevrey-$1$ Borel bound of the form
$|\widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(c_0)|\le C M^r r!$ is an upper bound on
the factorially normalised transform; it does not assert that the
unscaled coefficients must grow factorially. The finite-$c$ root
growth and the Gevrey type of
$\sum_r \widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(c_0)\zeta^r/r!$ are therefore
different invariants.

Third, the quadratic Borel model attached to the Virasoro
Riccati metric gives explicit candidate singularities. At $c=1$,
with $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}=1/2$ and
$S_4=10/27$, the quadratic
$Q_L(\zeta)=q_0+q_1\zeta+q_2\zeta^2$ has
\[
 q_0=\frac{206}{27},\qquad q_1=-4,\qquad q_2=2,
\]
so its roots are
\[
 \omega_\pm=1\pm i\sqrt{\frac{76}{27}},\qquad
 |\omega_\pm|=\sqrt{\frac{103}{27}}.
\]
For general $c$ in this quadratic model,
\[
 |\omega_\pm|^2
 =1+\frac{15c+61}{5c+22}
 =\frac{20c+83}{5c+22}.
\]
Thus $c=-22/5$ is the Lee--Yang denominator pole of the universal
Virasoro Verma formula $S_4=10/[c(5c+22)]$; it is not a singularity
of the simple Lee--Yang quotient after null vectors are divided out.
At $c=-83/20$ the quadratic has $q_0=0$ and factors as
\[
 Q_L(\zeta)=\frac{83}{10}\,\zeta(2-\zeta),
\]
so the model roots are $0$ and $2$. The root at $0$ is a
degeneracy of the quadratic approximation, while the root at $2$
is the positive-real Borel obstruction predicted by that model.

The Sugawara equation
$8k/(k+3)=-83/20$ gives the admissible
$\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3$ level $k=-83/81=-3+160/81$.
The same rational central charge is realised by admissible
$\mathfrak{sl}_n$ levels for other $n$ as well; this is a
rational-central-charge phenomenon, not evidence that the
Virasoro Borel quadratic singles out a unique affine algebra.

As $c\to\infty$ the two non-real roots in the positive-$c$ regime
approach
\[
 \omega_\pm\longrightarrow 1\pm i\sqrt3
 =2e^{\pm i\pi/3}\in\mathbb Q(\zeta_6).
\]
The equality of the limiting angle $\pi/3$ with $2\pi/C_\Vir$ is
specific to the Virasoro weighted quadratic and the value
$C_\Vir=6$; it should not be promoted to a general formula for an
arbitrary exponential base.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:shadow-stratification-at-r-index}
Four-stratum decomposition at $r$-index]
The shadow-exponential base stratifies the computed scalar lanes into
four layers at the shadow-depth ($r$) index:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
 \item \emph{Finite (terminating).} Classes~G/L/C (Heisenberg,
 affine Kac--Moody non-critical, $\beta\gamma$); $S_r = 0$
 for $r > r_0$; $C_\cA$ is undefined (zero-tail).
 \item \emph{Exponential $C = 6$.} Checked non-logarithmic
 $T$-line dominated lanes; $|A_r| \sim 6^r/r$ for the leading-$c$
 lane.
 \item \emph{Gevrey-$\alpha$ with $\alpha > 0$.} Logarithmic
 C$_2$-cofinite (e.g.\ $\cW(p)$); factorial-modified
 exponential growth.
 \item \emph{Non-Borel-summable.} Non-C$_2$-cofinite; outside the
 tempered stratum.
\end{enumerate}
The second stratum is a checked $T$-line stratum, not a theorem
about every non-logarithmic standard vertex algebra. The full scalar
series of an algebra with additional leading primary lanes may
refine this stratification. The $C=6$ versus divergent/Gevrey
distinction is the analytic input relevant to the Theorem~F
holographic scope.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:class-C-beta-gamma-termination}
The $\beta\gamma$ row remains class $\mathsf C$]
The scalar G/L/C/M depth assignment used in this chapter is the
landscape-census assignment
\[
\mathsf G:\ r_{\max}=2,\qquad
\mathsf L:\ r_{\max}=3,\qquad
\mathsf C:\ r_{\max}=4,\qquad
\mathsf M:\ r_{\max}=\infty .
\]
For the rank-one $\beta\gamma_\lambda$ system the nonzero datum is
the quartic contact class in the charged scalar lane; the ordered
scalar tower satisfies $S_r(\beta\gamma_\lambda)=0$ for $r\ge5$.
A Sugawara stress tensor may define a separate $T$-line Virasoro
projection, but that projection is not the scalar tower used for the
class-$\mathsf C$ assignment and does not move $\beta\gamma_\lambda$
into the non-terminating class-$\mathsf M$ row.
\end{remark}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\subsection{W-line shadow tower: closed form and exponential base $C = 12$}
\label{subsec:w3-wline-closed-form}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

The $T$-line dominance criterion
(\ref{thm:universal-class-M-C-is-6}) identifies $C_\cA^T=6$ on any
checked stress-tensor lane whose non-Virasoro generator-line
contributions are $O(c^{-\alpha})$ subleading. For
$W_3 = W(\mathfrak{sl}_3)$ at generic central charge~$c$, this
$T$-line hypothesis is met
(Proposition~\ref{prop:w3-tline-virasoro-inheritance}) and
$C_{W_3}^{T\text{-line}} = 6$ is inherited. The $W$-line is a
\emph{second} lane, with its own shadow recursion, generator
Zamolodchikov norm $N_W = c/3$, and closed-form
structure. We establish the $W$-line analogue here: a
\emph{distinct} exponential base $C_{W_3}^{W\text{-line}} = 12$,
twice the $T$-line value, with an explicit central-binomial closed
form for the integer sequence.

\paragraph{Setup (restricted $W$-line recursion).}
On the $W$-line $x_T = 0$ of the two-variable $W_3$ shadow potential,
the $Z_2$ parity $W \to -W$ forces all odd-depth shadows to vanish;
only even-depth $S_{2m}$ carry. Let
$Q_{WW} := 2560 / [c (5c+22)^3]$
be the quartic seed (Proposition~\ref{prop:w3-wline-closed-form}
in \texttt{chapters/theory/shadow\_tower\_other\_class\_M\_platonic.tex}),
and define the normalised integer sequence
\[
 a_m \;:=\; |N_{2m}| \,/\, 2560^{\,m-1},
 \qquad
 S_{2m}(W_3) \;=\; (-1)^{m+1} a_m \cdot
 \frac{2560^{\,m-1}}{c^{\,2m-3} (5c+22)^{3(m-1)}}.
\]
Then $a_2 = 1$, and by the $W$-line Poisson recurrence
(\texttt{compute/lib/w3\_wline\_shadow\_tower.py}),
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-wline-recursion}
 a_n \;=\; \frac{3}{n}\,\sum_{\substack{j+k = n+1 \\ 2 \le j \le k}}
 w(j, k)\, j\, k\, a_j\, a_k,
 \qquad
 w(j, k) = \begin{cases} 1/2 & j = k \\ 1 & j \ne k \end{cases}.
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:w3-wline-closed-form}
$W_3$ $W$-line integer sequence closed form]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The normalised sequence $(a_n)_{n \ge 2}$ from
\eqref{eq:w3-wline-recursion} admits the central-binomial closed
form
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-wline-central-binomial}
 a_n \;=\; \frac{2 \cdot 3^{\,n-2} \, (2n-4)!}
 {(n-2)!\, n!}
 \;=\; \frac{2 \cdot 3^{\,n-2}}{n(n-1)} \,
 \binom{2n-4}{n-2},
 \qquad n \ge 2.
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the consecutive-term ratio is exactly rational:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-wline-ratio}
 \frac{a_{n+1}}{a_n} \;=\; \frac{6\,(2n-3)}{n+1},
 \qquad n \ge 2.
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The ratio identity~\eqref{eq:w3-wline-ratio} is equivalent
to~\eqref{eq:w3-wline-central-binomial} via the telescoping
product $a_n = a_2 \cdot \prod_{k=2}^{n-1} 6(2k-3)/(k+1)
= 6^{n-2} \cdot 1 \cdot 3 \cdot 5 \cdots (2n-5) / [3 \cdot 4 \cdots n]
= 6^{n-2} \cdot (2n-5)!!\,/(n!/2) = 2 \cdot 6^{n-2} (2n-5)!!\, / n!$,
and $(2n-5)!! = (2n-4)! / [2^{n-2} (n-2)!]$. The factor
$6^{n-2} / 2^{n-2} = 3^{n-2}$ gives the stated form.

For~\eqref{eq:w3-wline-ratio}, proceed by strong induction. The
base cases $n = 2, 3, 4$ check: $a_3/a_2 = 2 = 6 \cdot 1 / 3$,
$a_4/a_3 = 9/2 = 6 \cdot 3 / 4$, $a_5/a_4 = 6 = 6 \cdot 5 / 5$.
Assuming~\eqref{eq:w3-wline-central-binomial} for all $k \le n$,
substitute into the recursion~\eqref{eq:w3-wline-recursion}:
\[
 n \cdot a_n / 3 \;=\;
 \tfrac{1}{2} \sum_{\substack{j + k = n+1 \\ j < k}} 2\, j\, k\, a_j a_k
 + \tfrac{1}{2} \mathbf{1}_{n\text{ odd}} \cdot \bigl[\tfrac{n+1}{2}\bigr]^2
 a_{(n+1)/2}^2.
\]
Substituting the central-binomial closed form for $a_j, a_k$ and
collecting into a single sum of products of central binomial
coefficients yields, via the Vandermonde--Chu convolution identity
$\sum_{j} \binom{2j-4}{j-2} \binom{2(n-j)-2}{n-j-1} / [(j)(n-j)]
 = \binom{2n-4}{n-1} / n$ (evaluated over the admissible range
$2 \le j \le n-1$), the prediction
$a_n = 2 \cdot 3^{n-2} (2n-4)! / [(n-2)! n!]$. Full verification has
been carried out symbolically through $n = 25$ in
\texttt{compute/lib/w3\_wline\_shadow\_tower.py::normalized\_recursion};
the match is exact for every $n$ tested.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:w3-wline-exponential-base}
$W$-line shadow-exponential base $C_{W_3}^{W\text{-line}} = 12$]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
Let $\cA = W_3$ at generic central charge $c \in
\mathbb{C} \setminus \{0, -22/5\}$. The $W$-line integer sequence
$(a_n)$ from Theorem~\ref{thm:w3-wline-closed-form} has
shadow-exponential base
\begin{equation}
 C_{W_3}^{W\text{-line}} \;:=\;
 \lim_{n \to \infty} \frac{a_{n+1}}{a_n}
 \;=\; \lim_{n \to \infty} \frac{6\,(2n-3)}{n+1}
 \;=\; 12,
\end{equation}
with Stirling asymptotic
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-wline-stirling}
 a_n \;\sim\; \frac{2}{\sqrt{\pi}} \cdot
 \frac{12^{\,n-2}}{n^{5/2}}
 \;=\; \frac{1}{72 \sqrt{\pi}} \cdot
 \frac{12^{\,n}}{n^{5/2}},
 \qquad n \to \infty.
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The ratio
formula~\eqref{eq:w3-wline-ratio} gives $a_{n+1}/a_n = 6(2n-3)/(n+1)
= 12 - 30/(n+1)$, so $\lim a_{n+1}/a_n = 12$. For the Stirling
asymptotic, apply $\binom{2m}{m} \sim 4^m / \sqrt{\pi m}$ to the
central binomial $\binom{2n-4}{n-2}$:
\[
 a_n \;=\; \frac{2 \cdot 3^{n-2}}{n(n-1)}
 \binom{2n-4}{n-2}
 \;\sim\; \frac{2 \cdot 3^{n-2} \cdot 4^{n-2}}
 {n^2 \sqrt{\pi (n-2)}}
 \;=\; \frac{2 \cdot 12^{\,n-2}}{n^{5/2} \sqrt{\pi}}
 \cdot (1 + O(1/n)),
\]
which rearranges to~\eqref{eq:w3-wline-stirling}.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:w3-wline-generating-function}
Exact generating-function closed form for the $W$-line sequence]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The generating function
$F(z) := \sum_{n \ge 2} a_n z^n$ of the $W_3$ $W$-line integer
sequence \eqref{eq:w3-wline-central-binomial} admits the exact
algebraic closed form
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-wline-gf-derivative}
 F'(z) \;=\; \frac{1 - \sqrt{1 - 12 z}}{3},
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-wline-gf-integrated}
 F(z) \;=\; \frac{z}{3} \;+\;
 \frac{(1 - 12 z)^{3/2} - 1}{54}.
\end{equation}
The radius of convergence is exactly $\rho = 1/12 = 1/C_{W_3}^{W\text{-line}}$;
the nearest singularity is a branch point at $z = 1/12$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
From the Poisson-bracket recursion
\eqref{eq:w3-wline-recursion}, write
$n a_n = 3 \sum_{\substack{j + k = n+1 \\ 2 \le j \le k}}
 w(j, k) \, j k \, a_j a_k$ for $n \ge 3$
($w = 1/2$ if $j = k$, $w = 1$ otherwise), with $a_2 = 1$.
Converting the unordered-with-weight sum to an ordered sum over
$j, k \ge 2$ (each $j \ne k$ pair counted twice, each $j = k$ pair
counted once) gives
\[
 n a_n \;=\; \tfrac{3}{2}
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = n+1 \\ 2 \le j, k}}
 j k \, a_j a_k, \qquad n \ge 3.
\]
Multiplying both sides by $z^{n-1}$ and summing over $n \ge 3$,
the left-hand side is
$\sum_{n \ge 3} n a_n z^{n-1} = F'(z) - 2 a_2 z = F'(z) - 2 z$,
while the right-hand side is
$\tfrac{3}{2} \bigl( \sum_{j \ge 2} j a_j z^{j-1} \bigr)^2
 = \tfrac{3}{2} F'(z)^2$.
So $F'(z)$ satisfies the algebraic relation
\[
 \tfrac{3}{2} F'(z)^2 - F'(z) + 2 z \;=\; 0.
\]
Solving the quadratic for $F'$, with branch chosen by
$F'(0) = 0$, yields~\eqref{eq:w3-wline-gf-derivative}.
Integrating from $0$ to $z$ with the substitution $u = 1 - 12 t$ gives
$F(z) = z/3 - (1/3) \int_0^z \sqrt{1 - 12 t} \, dt =
 z/3 + \bigl[(1 - 12 z)^{3/2} - 1\bigr]/54$,
establishing~\eqref{eq:w3-wline-gf-integrated}. The radius of
convergence follows from the branch point at $z = 1/12$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[\label{cor:w3-wline-self-consistency}
Riccati self-consistency at the radius of convergence]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
Evaluation of the generating function derivative at the radius
$z = 1/12$ gives the sharp identity
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-wline-self-consistency}
 F'(1/12)
 \;=\; \sum_{n \ge 2} n \, a_n \cdot 12^{\,1-n}
 \;=\; \frac{1}{3}.
\end{equation}
Explicitly: the infinite sum
$\sum_{n \ge 2} n a_n / 12^{n-1}$ converges absolutely and equals $1/3$.
Numerical verification: the partial sum through $N = 300$ reaches
$0.32246$, with residual $1/3 - 0.32246 \approx 0.01087$, matching
the Stirling tail
$\sum_{n > N} n a_n 12^{1-n} \sim 1/(3 \sqrt{\pi N})$
to four significant figures.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Set $z = 1/12$ in~\eqref{eq:w3-wline-gf-derivative}:
$F'(1/12) = (1 - \sqrt{0})/3 = 1/3$.
The power-series representation
$F'(z) = \sum_{n \ge 2} n a_n z^{n-1}$ at $z = 1/12$ gives
the stated sum. Absolute convergence follows from
$n a_n 12^{1-n}\sim (6\sqrt{\pi})^{-1}n^{-3/2}$, and the continuous
extension of $F'$ to $z=1/12$ identifies the sum with the boundary
value. The Stirling tail verification is by
direct substitution of the asymptotic
$a_n \sim 12^n / (72 \sqrt{\pi} n^{5/2})$ into the tail
$\sum_{n > N} n a_n / 12^{n-1}
 \sim \sum_{n > N} 12 / (72 \sqrt{\pi} n^{3/2})
 = (1/6\sqrt{\pi}) \sum_{n > N} n^{-3/2}
 \sim (1/3\sqrt{\pi}) N^{-1/2}$,
evaluated against the computed partial sum at $N = 300$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:w3-wline-catalan-identity}
The $W$-line as a Catalan-number sequence in disguise]
The generating-function closed form
\eqref{eq:w3-wline-gf-derivative} exhibits the $W_3$ $W$-line
integer sequence as a rescaled Catalan-type sequence. Using
$(1 - \sqrt{1 - 4u})/2 = \sum_{m \ge 0} C_m u^{m+1}$ (standard Catalan
identity with $C_m = \binom{2m}{m}/(m+1)$) evaluated at $u = 3 z$:
\[
 F'(z) \;=\; \frac{1 - \sqrt{1 - 12 z}}{3}
 \;=\; \frac{2}{3} \cdot \frac{1 - \sqrt{1 - 4 \cdot 3 z}}{2}
 \;=\; 2 \sum_{m \ge 0} C_m \, 3^m \, z^{m+1}.
\]
Thus $n a_n = [z^{n-1}] F'(z) = 2 \cdot C_{n-2} \cdot 3^{n-2}$, so
\[
 a_n \;=\; \frac{2 \cdot C_{n-2} \cdot 3^{n-2}}{n}
 \;=\; \frac{2 \cdot 3^{n-2}}{n (n-1)} \binom{2n-4}{n-2},
\]
reproducing~\eqref{eq:w3-wline-central-binomial}. The exponential
base $C_{W_3}^{W\text{-line}} = 12 = 4 \cdot 3$ decomposes as
\emph{(Catalan base $4$)} $\times$ \emph{(weight $s = 3$)}; the
Catalan base belongs to this square-root model (branch point of
$\sqrt{1 - 4u}$ at $u = 1/4$); the weight $s = 3$ is the propagator
prefactor. Under the Catalan-type Riccati hypotheses recorded in
Remark~\ref{rem:riccati-template-hypotheses}, the model equation is
\[
 F_s'(z) = \frac{1-\sqrt{1-4sz}}{s},
\]
and the resulting conditional base is $C_s=4s$. At $s=3$, the proved
$W_3$ $W$-line gives $C_3=12$. This does not include the Virasoro
$T$-line, and it does not assert the higher-spin $W^{(s)}$ lanes of
principal $W_N$.
The crucial difference: the $W_3$ $W$-line enjoys
\emph{$Z_2$ parity}: $W \to -W$ forces odd-depth shadows to
vanish, so only even arities $r = 2m$ carry; reindexing $m = r/2$
turns the original bar-depth bracket index $j + k = r + 2$
(with $j, k$ even) into $j' + k' = m + 1$ on the halved index,
and $j' = k' = 2$ is allowed (original $j = k = 4$), so the
seed $a_2 = 1$ enters the recursion from the first non-trivial
step. The Virasoro $T$-line has no such parity: both even
and odd arities carry, and the original $j + k = r + 2$ index
excludes $j = 2$ at every depth (since $k = r$ is never yet
computed). The $T$-line integer sequence
$A_r = 8 (-6)^{r-4}/r$ is therefore generated by a
\emph{different} recurrence (effectively $j \ge 3$,
$j + k = r + 2$) producing $C_\Vir^T = 6$, not
$C = 4 \cdot 2 = 8$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:linear-vs-quadratic-asymptotic-recurrence}
Linear vs quadratic asymptotic recurrence: the deeper
structural dichotomy]
The true structural difference between Virasoro $T$-line and
$W_3$ $W$-line asymptotics lies not just in the $Z_2$ parity, but
in how the \emph{leading-$c$} projection interacts with the
quadratic shadow recurrence.

Both families satisfy a quadratic shadow recursion on the
full rational coefficients $S_r(c)$:
\[
 r \, c \, S_r \;=\; -\sum_{\substack{j+k = r+2 \\ j \le k}}
 w(j, k) \, j \, k \, S_j(c) \, S_k(c).
\]
The recursion is quadratic in $S$, with a $1/c$ prefactor from
the propagator $P = 2/c$ (on $T$-line) or $P = 3/c$ (on $W$-line).

\emph{Virasoro $T$-line}: the different $S_j(c)$ have different
$c$-scalings: $S_3 = 2 \sim c^0$,
$\widehat S_r^{\rm wt} \sim c^{-(r-2)}$ for
$r \ge 4$. Under the scaling $A_r := \lim_{c \to \infty}
c^{r-2}\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}$ (for $r \ge 4$), only the pair
$(j, k) = (3, r-1)$
contributes at leading $c$ (other pairs are higher-order in
$1/c$). This \emph{cascade of $c$-orders collapses the quadratic
recursion to a LINEAR recurrence}
\[
 A_r \;=\; -\frac{6 (r-1)}{r} A_{r-1},
 \qquad r \ge 5,
\]
with two seeds $A_3 = A_4 = 2$. Linear recurrence yields pure
geometric growth $A_r = 8 (-6)^{r-4}/r$, and the generating
function has a logarithmic term (polynomial plus $\log(1+6 z)$).

\emph{$W_3$ $W$-line}: the integer sequence $a_m := |N_{2m}| /
2560^{m-1}$ is defined \emph{after} factoring out all
$c$-dependence. No cascade of $c$-orders: all pairs contribute at
the same order. The quadratic shadow recursion preserves its
quadratic character on $(a_m)$,
\[
 m a_m \;=\; \tfrac{3}{2} \sum_{\substack{j + k = m+1 \\ j, k \ge 2}}
 w(j, k) \, j \, k \, a_j \, a_k,
\]
giving Catalan-type growth
$a_m \sim 12^m / (72 \sqrt{\pi} \cdot m^{5/2})$
and an algebraic closed form (polynomial plus $(1-12 z)^{3/2}$).

\emph{Distilled distinction}: the $Z_2$ parity (Remark~(H1)) allows
the \emph{integer} sequence to be defined (by halving the arity
and normalising $c$-powers); the resulting recurrence remains
\emph{quadratic}, giving algebraic GF and Catalan-type
$m^{-5/2}$ prefactor. Absence of parity forces leading-$c$
extraction to route through a \emph{linear} recurrence on
$A_r$ (leading scaling index), giving transcendental GF and
$r^{-1}$ prefactor. Both end at finite exponential base ($6$
or $12$), but the sub-exponential power-law differs by two orders
of magnitude ($r^{-1}$ vs $m^{-5/2}$).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:cross-vol-three-invariants-W3}
Cross-volume: three distinct $W_3$ shadow-tower invariants]
The $W_3$ shadow tower carries three \emph{distinct} asymptotic
invariants, catalogued in the Vol~II cross-volume remark
	\texttt{rem:beta-A-W3-wline-integer-sequence}
	in the Vol~II climax comparison:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
 \item $C_{W_3}^{T\text{-line}} = 6$: shadow-exponential base
 of the Vol~I leading-$c$ projection $A_r$ on the $T$-line;
 the $T$-line dominance value
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-class-M-C-is-6}).
 \item $\beta_{W_3} = 10$: the Vol~II Banach-completion
 sum-of-channels bound, closed form
 $\beta_N = 12 (H_N - 1) = \sum_{s=2}^{N} 12/s$ (Vol~II
 \texttt{thm:beta-N-closed-form-proved-all-N}); at $N = 3$
 decomposes as $12/2 + 12/3 = 6 + 4 = 10$.
 \item $C_{W_3}^{W\text{-line}} = 12$: the $c$-independent
 integer-sequence base of the $W$-line
 (Theorem~\ref{thm:w3-wline-exponential-base}), equal to the
 Riccati model value $4 s$ at $s = 3$.
\end{enumerate}
These are three different objects measuring three different
quantities; there is no contradiction in their distinct values.
The Vol~II $\beta_N$ formula is the proved closed form
for the sum-of-channels Banach rate; the Vol~I $C$ is the
asymptotic of the leading-$c$ projection on the fixed $T$-line;
the $W$-line integer base $C = 12$ is a third invariant,
established here.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:riccati-template-hypotheses}
Hypotheses for the \(C = 4s\) Riccati model]
The $C_s = 4 s$ structural formula from
Remark~\ref{rem:w3-wline-catalan-identity} applies under the
following hypotheses on a generator lane:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(H\arabic*)]
 \item \emph{$Z_2$ parity} (generator $\to -$generator) forcing
 odd-depth shadows on the lane to vanish.
 \item Hessian propagator $P = s / c$ on the lane, for some
 lane weight parameter $s \in \mathbb{Z}_{\ge 2}$.
 \item Seed $a_2 = 1$ (suitably normalised curvature).
 \item Weight-$4$ OPE structure constant producing $a_3$ from
 $a_2^2$ via the quadratic recursion.
\end{enumerate}
Under (H1)--(H4), the generating function $F(z) = \sum_{m \ge 2}
a_m z^m$ satisfies
$\tfrac{s}{2} F'(z)^2 - F'(z) + 2 z = 0$, whence
$F'(z) = (1 - \sqrt{1 - 4 s z}) / s$ and $C = 4 s$. The
$W_3$ $W$-line satisfies (H1)--(H4) with $s = 3$. The
Virasoro $T$-line fails (H1). Whether higher-spin $W^{(s)}$
lanes in principal $W_N$ satisfy (H1)--(H4) for $s \ge 4$ is
open: parity, Hessian normalisation, and the quartic seed must be
checked from the Fateev--Lukyanov/Hornfeck OPE data case by case.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:w3-wline-doubling-interpretation}
The doubling $12 = 2 \cdot 6$: structural origin]
The factor-of-two between $C_{W_3}^{W\text{-line}} = 12$ and
$C_{W_3}^{T\text{-line}} = 6$ admits a structural decomposition.
The $W$-line has seed data $a_2 = 1$, $a_3 = 2$ (from the $W\!W$
OPE structure constant $2T/(z-w)^4$), with recursion kernel
\eqref{eq:w3-wline-recursion} carrying explicit prefactor
$3/n$ rather than $2/n$ (reflecting the $W$-line Hessian
$P_W = 3/c$ versus $P_T = 2/c$). The central-binomial closed
form~\eqref{eq:w3-wline-central-binomial}
shows that the $W$-line integer growth carries an extra factor of
$2$ per bar-depth relative to the $T$-line: the
$T$-line Riccati has $A_r \sim 8 (-6)^{r-4}/r$, so
$|A_{r+1}/A_r| \to 6$; the $W$-line ratio
$a_{n+1}/a_n = 6(2n-3)/(n+1) \to 12$ picks up the factor $2$ via the
$(2n-3)$ numerator (Pochhammer-shifted combinatorial weight) against
the $(n+1)$ denominator (versus the $r/(r+1) \to 1$ damping on
$T$-line).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:w3-wline-decomposition-is-circular}
The ``$3/2 \times 4/3 = 2$'' decomposition is numerical]
The doubling $2 = (3/2)\cdot(4/3)$ can be written with
$3/2=P_W/P_T$ (Hessian-propagator ratio) and $4/3$ as a kernel
factor. This decomposition is numerical: it
factorises the two proved bases
$C_{W_3}^{W\text{-line}}/C_\Vir^T=12/6$. It does \emph{not}
provide an independent derivation of a higher-spin formula.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:w3-wline-higher-spin-prediction}
Open mathematical condition for higher-spin $W^{(s)}$ lanes]
Only two lane bases are proved in this chapter:
\[
 C_\Vir^T=6,\qquad C_{W_3}^{W\text{-line}}=12.
\]
They come from different recursions. The Virasoro $T$-line has no
$Z_2$ parity reduction and its leading-$c$ projection is linear.
The $W_3$ $W$-line has parity, the halved index
$j+k=n+1$, and the quadratic Catalan recurrence
\eqref{eq:w3-wline-recursion}. Therefore the pair $(6,12)$ is not
a two-point interpolation problem.

For a principal $W_N$ lane generated by $W^{(s)}$ with $s\ge4$, the
conditional formula $C_s=4s$ is valid only if (H1)--(H4) of
Remark~\ref{rem:riccati-template-hypotheses} are proved for that
lane. The $W_4$ stage-$4$ packet shows that this condition has
substantive content. The stage-$4$ residual set has
$29$ entries; the top-pole cut leaves $7$; parity removes
$(4,4;3;0,5)$; the exact identity packet has the six entries
\[
(3,3;4;0,2),\quad (4,4;4;0,4),\quad
(3,4;3;0,4),\quad (3,4;4;0,3),\quad
(4,4;2;0,6),\quad (3,4;2;0,5).
\]
These split as four higher-spin channels and two Virasoro-target
identities, with principal Drinfeld--Sokolov values
$C^{\mathrm{DS}}_{4,4;2;0,6}=2$ and
$C^{\mathrm{DS}}_{3,4;2;0,5}=0$
(\texttt{compute/lib/w4\_stage4\_coefficients.py},
\texttt{test\_w4\_stage4\_coefficients.py}). This six-entry packet
is a finite OPE identity packet. It is not the quartic contact
polynomial, not a scalar Hochschild coefficient, and not a physical
bulk reconstruction datum.

The $W_4$ quartic contact packet has different semantics: the
weight-$4$ exchange space has two orthogonal quasi-primaries,
$\Lambda={:}TT{:}-(3/10)\partial^2T$ with norm
$c(5c+22)/10$ and the primary $W_4$ with norm $c/4$
(\texttt{compute/lib/w4\_multivariable\_shadow.py}). Thus the
reduced quartic splits into $\Lambda$-mediated and $W_4$-mediated
channels; for instance $Q_{3434}=4C_{34,W}^{2}/c$ has no
$(5c+22)^{-1}$ pole. The uniform Zamolodchikov filtration that
works on the Virasoro and $W_3$ $T$-lines is therefore broken by
$W_4$ exchange. No formula for
$C_{W_N}^{W^{(s)}\text{-line}}$ at $s\ge4$, and in particular no
$C_4=16$ assertion, is made here.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:w3-wline-koszul-duality-partner}
Koszul-dual conductor and the normalised $W$-line sequence]
In the Fateev--Lukyanov free-field convention (where the
classical-limit self-dual fixed point lies at $c = 2$, i.e.\ $2(N-1)$
at $N = 3$), the $W_3$ Koszul involution is $c \mapsto 4 - c$ with
symmetric-point conductor $K_3^{\mathrm{FL}} := c + (4 - c) = 4 =
2(N-1)$; this is the classical-limit conductor, distinct from the
Trinity conductor $K^{\mathrm{trin}}(W_3) = c + c^! = 100$ and from
the scalar-complementarity $\kappa(W_3) + \kappa(W_3^!) = 250/3$
(Arakawa convention; for $W_3$ specifically, NOT Vir where
$\kappa + \kappa^! = 13$ at self-dual $c = 13$). The statement ``$c \mapsto 4 - c$ at
$K_3 = 4$'' is convention-specific: it captures the free-field
symmetric point and is NOT the trace-form conductor. Under $c \mapsto 4 - c$, the $W$-line integer sequence
$a_n$ is \emph{invariant} (since $a_n$ is independent of $c$ after
normalising out $2560^{n-1}/[c^{2m-3}(5c+22)^{3(m-1)}]$), so the
normalised shadow-exponential base $C = 12$ is unchanged by this
free-field involution. This invariance is only a statement about the
normalised integer sequence. It does not identify the
Fateev--Lukyanov conductor with the trace-form conductor, and it does
not turn the numerical factorisation $12/6=(3/2)(4/3)$ into a
derivation of any higher-spin base.
\end{remark}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Motivic scope}
\label{sec:sth-motivic}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{proposition}[\label{prop:sth-virasoro-rational-through-8}No
motivic period enters Virasoro through weight 8]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
