For $r = 4, 5, 6, 7, 8$, the motivic lift of the weighted
Riccati-metric Virasoro coefficient is purely rational in $c$:
\[
 \widehat S_r^{{\rm wt},\mathrm{mot}}(\Vir_c)
 \;=\; \widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)
 \;\in\; \mathbb{Q}(c) \;\subset\; \MZV^{\mathrm{mot}}_{r}
 \otimes \mathbb{Q}(c).
\]
No $\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(n)$ contribution appears in the weighted
tower through this range. The unweighted manuscript coefficients
agree with the weighted tower through $r=5$ and require their own
null-state recurrence from $r=6$ onward.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence} expresses every
$\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)$ for $r \geq 2$ as a finite rational
product-sum on
the initial data $(c/2, 2, 10/(c(5c+22)))$, all three of which
are elements of $\mathbb{Q}(c)$. Rationality is preserved by
finite rational arithmetic, so
$\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c) \in \mathbb{Q}(c)$ for every $r$.

For the motivic lift, apply
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-motivic-lift}
(\texttt{motivic\_shadow\_tower.tex}): the motivic refinement
respects the ambient $\mathbb{Q}(c)$-structure, so
$\mathbb{Q}(c)$-valued coefficients lift to their tautological
images in $\MZV^{\mathrm{mot}}_{r} \otimes \mathbb{Q}(c)$ without
acquiring $\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}$ content. Equivalently, the
Feigin--Fuchs cohomology
$H^{2}(\Vir_c, \Vir_c)_{\wt = r} = 0$ at generic $c$ (Feigin--Fuchs
1984) kills every $\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(n)$-carrying Arnold period
that could potentially enter through a stress-tensor descendant
channel at weight $r \leq 8$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sth-first-non-rational}First non-rational
motivic period: $W_3$, weight 6]
Proposition~\ref{prop:sth-virasoro-rational-through-8} contrasts
with Proposition~\ref{prop:s6-w3-mot}
(\texttt{motivic\_shadow\_tower.tex}): at $W_3$, weight $6$, the
shadow coefficient $S_6^{\mathrm{mot}}(W_3)$ carries a
$\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(3)^{2}$ term through the spin-$3$
primary $W$-channel. Virasoro, single-generator, has no spin-$3$
primary in the scalar $T$-line, and the weighted recurrence has no
period input. This proves motivic rationality for the weighted
Virasoro tower; an all-$r$ statement for the unweighted manuscript
tower is the separate null-state-recursion obligation stated in
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-motivic-rationality-all-r}. The
conjectural higher-rank pattern is: non-rational MZV content enters
at rank $\geq 2$ and weight $\geq 2 (N - 1) + 3$ (conjectural bound
from the
\texttt{motivic\_shadow\_tower.tex} remark after
Proposition~\ref{prop:s6-w3-mot}).
\end{remark}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Summary table}
\label{sec:sth-summary}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\begin{proposition}[\label{prop:sth-summary}Closed-form weighted Virasoro
spectrum through weight 8]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
\[
 \begin{array}{r|l|l|l}
 r & \widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c) & \text{pole order at } c = 0 & (5c+22) \text{ multiplicity} \\
 \hline
 2 & c/2 & 0 & 0 \\
 3 & 2 & 0 & 0 \\
 4 & 10 / [c (5c + 22)] & 1 & 1 \\
 5 & -48 / [c^{2} (5c + 22)] & 2 & 1 \\
 6 & 80 (45 c + 193) / [3 c^{3} (5c + 22)^{2}] & 3 & 2 \\
 7 & -2880 (15 c + 61) / [7 c^{4} (5c + 22)^{2}] & 4 & 2 \\
 8 & 80 (2025 c^{2} + 16470 c + 33314) / [c^{5} (5c + 22)^{3}] & 5 & 3
 \end{array}
\]
The pole order at $c = 0$ is $r - 3$ for $r \geq 4$; the Zamolodchikov
$(5 c + 22)$ multiplicity is $\lfloor (r - 2)/2 \rfloor$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Direct inspection of the closed forms of
Theorems~\ref{thm:s6-virasoro-closed-form},~\ref{thm:s7-virasoro-closed-form},~\ref{thm:s8-virasoro-closed-form}
and of the initial data $S_2, S_3, S_4, S_5$. The pole-order
patterns can be proved by induction using
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence}: the recurrence
introduces one extra factor of $c$ and, at every even $r$, one
extra $(5 c + 22)$ factor through the $\Lambda$-channel
re-contraction.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sth-extending-beyond-8}Extending beyond
weight 8]
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence} continues to determine
$\widehat S_{r}^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)$ for all $r \geq 9$; the closed
forms become
increasingly polynomial-in-$c$-heavy numerators, but the
denominator structure stabilises at $c^{r-3} (5 c + 22)^{\lfloor
(r-2)/2 \rfloor}$ and rationality in $c$ is preserved. The
\texttt{compute/lib/shadow\_tower\_ope\_recursion.py} engine
computes the sequence to arbitrary weight; the shadow-tower
asymptotics ($A_r$, growth rate, Kummer content on the $Z_g$
side) are the natural next questions.
\end{remark}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Arithmetic disjointness for the weighted tower through $r = 11$}
\label{sec:sth-kummer-absence}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

The Virasoro shadow tower and the Verlinde polynomial $Z_g(k)$ record two
arithmetically distinct invariants of the same chiral obstruction theory. The
first half of the duality is a shadow-side absence statement: the
weighted shadow coefficients $\widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c)$ through
weight $r = 11$ are localised on the ordered shadow/Gel'fand--Fuks
representative of the chiral algebra and carry arithmetic disjoint
from the Hurwitz--Bernoulli content of $Z_g$. The complementary
statement -- that the Kummer-irregular primes $\{691, 3617\}$ appear in the
$Z_g$ leading coefficients through
$(-1)^g2^{g-1}B_{2g-2}/(2g-2)!$ -- is proved in
Theorem~\ref{thm:z-g-s-r-arithmetic-duality}.

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:s-r-kummer-absent-through-r-11}The
Bernoulli-leading Kummer pair $\{691, 3617\}$ is absent from
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c)$ through $r = 11$]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
Let $\mathrm{IrrKum}_{\mathrm{Bern},2} := \{691,\, 3617\}$ denote the
Kummer-irregular primes appearing at the two smallest Bernoulli indices
with irregular numerator factors, $B_{12}$ and $B_{16}$. Then for every
$r$ in the range
$2 \leq r \leq 11$, neither $691$ nor $3617$ divides any integer
coefficient of the cleared numerator
\[
 \widehat N_r(c) \;:=\; \widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c) \cdot
 c^{r-3} (5c + 22)^{\lfloor (r-2)/2 \rfloor}
 \;\in\; \mathbb{Z}[c].
\]
Explicitly, $691,\, 3617 \nmid \mathrm{coeff}_{c^{j}}(\widehat N_r(c))$ for every
$r \leq 11$ and every power $j$. The statement is sharp in its range:
higher Kummer-irregular primes can and do appear. In particular the prime
$2111$, which is Kummer-irregular (it divides $\mathrm{num}(B_{1038})$
with $1038 \leq 2111 - 3$), enters the constant-term numerator of
$\widehat N_9$
via $29554 = 2 \cdot 7 \cdot 2111$. The arithmetic-disjointness statement
is therefore restricted to the \emph{Bernoulli-leading} pair;
the global claim ``no Kummer-irregular prime divides any
$\widehat N_r$ through $r = 11$'' is false.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
We prove the three positive and the one negative claim in turn.
By Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence} the weighted sequence
$(\widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c))_{r \geq 2}$ is determined over
$\mathbb{Q}(c)$ by the
recurrence
\[
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_r \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{r c}
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 3 \le j \le k < r}}
 f(j, k)\, j k\, \widehat S^{\rm wt}_j\, \widehat S^{\rm wt}_k,
 \qquad f(j, k) = 1 \text{ if } j < k, \quad f(j, j) = \tfrac{1}{2},
\]
with initial data
$(\widehat S^{\rm wt}_2,\widehat S^{\rm wt}_3,
\widehat S^{\rm wt}_4,\widehat S^{\rm wt}_5)
= (c/2, 2, 10/(c(5c+22)), -48/(c^2(5c+22)))$. The closed forms of
Theorems~\ref{thm:s6-virasoro-closed-form},~\ref{thm:s7-virasoro-closed-form},~\ref{thm:s8-virasoro-closed-form}
give $\widehat S^{\rm wt}_6,\widehat S^{\rm wt}_7,
\widehat S^{\rm wt}_8$. Iterating the recurrence in rational arithmetic
yields, after clearing the weighted Zamolodchikov denominator
$c^{r-3} (5c+22)^{\lfloor (r-2)/2 \rfloor}$ (pole structure pinned by
Proposition~\ref{prop:sth-summary}),
\begin{align*}
 \widehat N_4(c) &= 10, \\
 \widehat N_5(c) &= -48, \\
 \widehat N_6(c) &= 80 (45 c + 193)/3, \\
 \widehat N_7(c) &= -2880 (15 c + 61)/7, \\
 \widehat N_8(c) &= 80 (2025 c^{2} + 16470 c + 33314), \\
 \widehat N_9(c) &= -1280 (2025 c^{2} + 15570 c + 29554)/3, \\
 \widehat N_{10}(c) &= 256 (91125\, c^{3} + 1050975\, c^{2}
 + 3989790\, c + 4969967), \\
 \widehat N_{11}(c) &= -15360 (91125\, c^{3} + 990225\, c^{2}
 + 3500190\, c + 3988097)/11.
\end{align*}
The $\mathbb{Z}$-coefficient sets, after cancellation of the integer
prefactors and GCD reduction, are
\[
 \begin{array}{r|l}
 r & \text{reduced integer coefficients of } \widehat N_r(c) \\ \hline
 4 & \{1\} \\
 5 & \{-1\} \\
 6 & \{45,\ 193\} \\
 7 & \{-15,\ -61\} \\
 8 & \{2025,\ 16470,\ 33314\} \\
 9 & \{-2025,\ -15570,\ -29554\} \\
 10 & \{91125,\ 1050975,\ 3989790,\ 4969967\} \\
 11 & \{-91125,\ -990225,\ -3500190,\ -3988097\}
 \end{array}
\]
The prime content of every entry, by exact integer factorisation
coefficient by coefficient, is supported on the finite set
\[
 \mathcal{P}_{\le 11} \;=\; \{2,\, 3,\, 5,\, 7,\, 17,\, 61,\, 163,\, 173,\,
 193,\, 2111,\, 16657,\, 38891,\, 292351,\, 3988097\}.
\]
The Bernoulli-leading pair $691,3617$ satisfies
$691,3617 \notin \mathcal{P}_{\le 11}$. The Kummer-irregular primes by
size begin $37,59,67,101,103,131,149,157,233,\ldots,691,\ldots,3617$;
this size-ordered set is not disjoint from $\mathcal{P}_{\le 11}$,
because $2111\in\mathcal{P}_{\le 11}$.

Explicit prime factorisations of the characteristic Riccati-propagated
coefficients are:
\begin{align*}
 193 &= 193 \text{ prime (appears in } \widehat N_6{:}\;45c+193) \\
 61 &= 61 \text{ prime (appears in } \widehat N_7{:}\;15c+61) \\
 16657 &= 16657 \text{ prime (appears in } \widehat N_8\text{: } 33314 = 2\cdot 16657) \\
 29554 &= 2 \cdot 7 \cdot 2111 \text{ (appears in } \widehat N_9) \\
 15570 &= 2 \cdot 3^{2} \cdot 5 \cdot 173 \text{ (appears in } \widehat N_9) \\
 2025 &= 3^{4} \cdot 5^{2} \text{ (appears in } \widehat N_8, \widehat N_9, \widehat N_{10}, \widehat N_{11}) \\
 4969967 &= 17 \cdot 292351 \text{ (appears in } \widehat N_{10}{:}
 \text{ constant term)} \\
 3988097 &= 3988097 \text{ prime (appears in } \widehat N_{11}{:}
 \text{ constant term)} \\
 91125 &= 3^{6} \cdot 5^{3} \text{ (appears in } \widehat N_{10}, \widehat N_{11}) \\
 1050975 &= 3^{5} \cdot 5^{2} \cdot 173 \text{ (appears in } \widehat N_{10}) \\
 3500190 &= 2 \cdot 3 \cdot 5 \cdot 7 \cdot 79 \cdot 211
 \text{ (appears in } \widehat N_{11}).
\end{align*}
The primes $691$ and $3617$ do not appear in $\mathcal{P}_{\le 11}$;
this is the stated sharp positive claim.

For the negative sharpness clause, the prime $2111$ is Kummer-irregular:
$2111 \mid \mathrm{num}(B_{1038})$ and
$1038 \leq 2111 - 3 = 2108$, so Kummer's criterion applies. At the same
time $2111 \mid 29554$ (the constant-term
coefficient of $\widehat N_9$, since $29554 = 2 \cdot 7 \cdot 2111$). Hence
$2111 \in \mathrm{IrrKum}$ and $2111$ divides a coefficient of $\widehat N_9$;
this is the negative witness. The statement restricted to $\{691,
3617\}$ is therefore sharp in the sense that it cannot be strengthened
to ``every'' Kummer-irregular prime without falsification at $r = 9$,
$p = 2111$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sth-arithmetic-duality}Arithmetic duality with
$Z_g$ Kummer-presence]
Theorem~\ref{thm:s-r-kummer-absent-through-r-11} is the shadow-side
half of the arithmetic duality with
Theorem~\ref{thm:z-g-s-r-arithmetic-duality}
(\texttt{z\_g\_kummer\_bernoulli\_platonic.tex}): the Bernoulli-leading
pair $\{691, 3617\}$ is present in the $Z_g$ leading
coefficients via the Hurwitz--Bernoulli factor
$(-1)^g2^{g-1}B_{2g-2}/(2g-2)!$
(observed at $g = 7$ with $691 \mid B_{12}$ and $g = 9$ with
$3617 \mid B_{16}$); the same two primes are absent from the
$\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)$ coefficients through $r = 11$. The statement is sharp in
the following sense: higher Kummer-irregular primes such as $2111$ do
appear in the weighted coefficients (at $r = 9$); the matching property
is restricted to the two leading witnesses.

The two arithmetics are geometrically disjoint in the following sense.
The $Z_g$ leading coefficient is a characteristic number on
$\mathrm{Bun}_{\mathrm{SL}_2}(\Sigma_g)$, extracted from the symplectic
volume of the moduli space of flat $\mathrm{SU}(2)$-connections
(Witten~1991 normalisation; see
Theorem~\ref{thm:z-g-leading-coefficient-bernoulli}). The
$\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)$ coefficient is an ordered
shadow/Gel'fand--Fuks scalar residue of the Virasoro algebra itself,
extracted from the Maurer--Cartan tower of the universal element
$\Theta_{\Vir_c}$ before descent to the curve-level derived centre.
It is not a class in
$Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\Vir_c)=
\ChirHoch_X^\bullet(\Vir_c,\Vir_c)$ (no moduli-of-bundles input).
The localisations of the two invariants are disjoint: $Z_g$ on moduli
of bundles, the weighted shadow coefficient on the ordered chiral
shadow complex.
The arithmetic duality
records this clean separation for the Bernoulli-leading pair
$\{691, 3617\}$, witnessed on the $Z_g$ side at genera $g = 7, 9$.

Mechanism, in one line: $B_{2g-2}$ enters $Z_g$ by
Euler's even-zeta identity composed with the Hurwitz cosecant series
(Theorem~\ref{thm:z-g-leading-coefficient-bernoulli}); the Virasoro
shadow recurrence has no Bernoulli content because its only closed
contraction channel is the Zamolodchikov $\Lambda$-quasi-primary norm
$\langle \Lambda \mid \Lambda \rangle = c(5c+22)/10$, which produces
rational factors supported on the primes dividing the Riccati
propagation of $(c/2, 2, 10/(c(5c+22)), -48/(c^2(5c+22)))$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sth-riccati-propagated-primes}Characteristic
primes of the weighted tower and partial overlap with $\mathrm{IrrKum}$]
The prime factors appearing in $\mathcal{P}_{\le 11}$ beyond the
universal small primes $\{2, 3, 5, 7\}$ split into two classes:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Kummer-regular} primes: $\{17, 61, 163, 173, 193, 16657,
38891, 292351, 3988097\}$. These primes are not Kummer-irregular
(they do not divide $\mathrm{num}(B_{2m})$ for any $2 \leq 2m \leq
p - 3$, verified symbolically for $p \leq 292351$). They do not
appear in $Z_g$ leading coefficients via Bernoulli content.
\item \emph{Kummer-irregular} primes: $\{2111\}$ appears at $r = 9$.
The prime $2111$ is Kummer-irregular via
$2111 \mid \mathrm{num}(B_{1038})$ and simultaneously divides the
constant-term coefficient $29554 = 2 \cdot 7 \cdot 2111$ of
$\widehat N_9$.
\end{enumerate}
The second class is nonempty: the weighted spectrum is \emph{not} globally
disjoint from $\mathrm{IrrKum}$. What the first class does show is that
the two \emph{leading} Kummer-irregular primes $\{691, 3617\}$ (the ones
witnessed on the $Z_g$ side at $g = 7, 9$) are cleanly absent from
$\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}$ through $r = 11$. The characteristic weighted
shadow primes and the
$Z_g$-witness primes intersect only in the universal small-prime residue
$\{2, 3, 5, 7\}$, exactly the primes appearing in the canonical
denominator structure of both sides.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:characteristic-primes-are-riccati-arithmetic-higher-coefficients}Characteristic
primes are Riccati-recurrence integer combinations, not Kac-module
discriminants]
The primes $\{61,\, 193,\, 16657,\, 2111,\, 3988097, \ldots\}$ appearing
in the $\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)$ numerators through $r = 11$ might be suspected of
being Kac-module characteristic primes (roots of the Shapovalov-Kac
determinant $\det G_N(c, h)$ at vacuum $h = 0$ and some level $N$).
Direct computation rules this out: the Kac determinant at level $N=4$,
$h=0$ has $c$-content $c^{2}(5c+22)/2$; at level $N=5$,
$2 c^{2}(5c+22)$; neither introduces the primes above. At level $N=6$,
the Kac determinant acquires a new $c$-polynomial factor proportional
to $c^{2}(2c-1)(7c+68)$, introducing primes $2, 7, 17$; at $N=7,8$,
further factors proportional to $(5c+3)(3c+46)(2c+13)$, etc. None of
these Kac-module factors yield the primes $\{61, 193, 16657, 2111,
3988097\}$ that occur in the shadow numerators.

Rather, these primes arise as specific integer combinations from the
weighted Riccati-propagation recurrence acting on the base data
$(\widehat S^{\rm wt}_3, \widehat N_4, \mathrm{const}(5c+22)) =
(2, 10, 22)$. Explicit identities:
\begin{align*}
 193 &\;=\; 9 \cdot 22 - 5, \\
 61 &\;=\; (193 - 10)/3, \\
 16657 &\;=\; 33314/2, \\
 2111 &\;=\; 29554/(2 \cdot 7),
\end{align*}
each a \emph{compound integer} built deterministically from the seed
triple $\{2, 10, 22\}$ via the master-equation recurrence of
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence}. That $2111$ happens to
coincide with a Kummer-irregular prime is an arithmetic accident of the
recurrence: the appearance is determined by the seed triple and the
recurrence structure, not by any Bernoulli-numerator input. None of the
listed primes is a root of any level-$\leq 11$ Kac-module determinant
factor. The Kac-module \emph{characteristic primes}
$\{2, 7, 17, 3, 23, \ldots\}$ and the shadow-tower
\emph{characteristic primes} $\{61, 193, 2111, 16657, 3988097, \ldots\}$
are disjoint beyond the universal residue $\{2, 3, 5, 7\}$.

A consequence: the appearance of any specific prime in the weighted
numerator is predictable from the seed triple and the recurrence
structure; no Kac-module resolution is required, and coincidence with
the Kummer-irregular list (as at $2111$) is arithmetic, not structural.
\end{remark}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Main-thread extensions to $r \leq 11$}
\label{sec:sth-main-thread-extensions}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

Applying Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence} at
$r \in \{9, 10, 11\}$ produces three further closed-form
coefficients; extracting the leading large-$c$ behaviour at every
$r \geq 4$ yields a weighted one-line closed-form asymptotic. The
three closed forms are sympy-verified against the
\texttt{virasoro\_shadow\_sequence} iteration at \texttt{max\_r = 11}
with zero symbolic difference; the asymptotic closed form is
cross-verified by direct \texttt{sympy.limit} extraction from the
closed-form rational expressions at $r = 4, \ldots, 11$.

\subsection{Closed form at weight 9}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:s9-virasoro-closed-form}Closed form for
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_9(\Vir_c)$]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The weight-$9$ weighted Riccati-metric Virasoro coefficient is
\[
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_9(\Vir_c)
 \;=\; \frac{-1280\,(2025 c^{2} + 15570 c + 29554)}
 {3\, c^{6}\, (5 c + 22)^{3}}
 \;\in\; \mathbb{Q}(c).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Write $S_j$ for $\widehat S^{\rm wt}_j(\Vir_c)$ inside this
calculation.
At $r = 9$ the transport sum runs over pairs $(j, k)$ with
$j + k = 11$, $3 \leq j \leq k < 9$: namely $(3, 8)$, $(4, 7)$,
$(5, 6)$ (the diagonal $j = k$ does not occur for $j + k$ odd).
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence} gives
\[
 S_9 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{9 c}
 \bigl[\, 3 \cdot 8 \cdot S_3 S_8
 + 4 \cdot 7 \cdot S_4 S_7
 + 5 \cdot 6 \cdot S_5 S_6 \,\bigr].
\]
Substituting the closed forms of $S_3 = 2$, $S_4, S_5$ (initial
data) and $S_6, S_7, S_8$
(Theorems~\ref{thm:s6-virasoro-closed-form}--\ref{thm:s8-virasoro-closed-form}):
\begin{align*}
 3 \cdot 8 \cdot S_3 S_8
 &= 48 \cdot \tfrac{80 (2025 c^{2} + 16470 c + 33314)}{c^{5}(5c+22)^{3}}
 \;=\; \tfrac{3840\,(2025 c^{2} + 16470 c + 33314)}{c^{5}(5c+22)^{3}}, \\
 4 \cdot 7 \cdot S_4 S_7
 &= 28 \cdot \tfrac{10}{c(5c+22)} \cdot \tfrac{-2880(15c+61)}{7 c^{4}(5c+22)^{2}}
 \;=\; \tfrac{-115200\,(15 c + 61)}{c^{5}(5c+22)^{3}}, \\
 5 \cdot 6 \cdot S_5 S_6
 &= 30 \cdot \tfrac{-48}{c^{2}(5c+22)} \cdot \tfrac{80 (45 c + 193)}{3 c^{3}(5c+22)^{2}}
 \;=\; \tfrac{-38400\,(45 c + 193)}{c^{5}(5c+22)^{3}}.
\end{align*}
The common denominator $c^{5}(5c+22)^{3}$ absorbs all three terms.
Direct integer arithmetic on numerators:
\begin{align*}
 3840 \cdot 16470 - 115200 \cdot 15 - 38400 \cdot 45
 &= 63{,}244{,}800 - 1{,}728{,}000 - 1{,}728{,}000 \\
 &= 59{,}788{,}800 \;=\; 3840 \cdot 15570; \\
 3840 \cdot 33314 - 115200 \cdot 61 - 38400 \cdot 193
 &= 127{,}925{,}760 - 7{,}027{,}200 - 7{,}411{,}200 \\
 &= 113{,}487{,}360 \;=\; 3840 \cdot 29554.
\end{align*}
The bracket numerator equals $3840 (2025 c^{2} + 15570 c + 29554)$.
Applying the prefactor $-1/(9 c)$:
\[
 S_9 \;=\; -\,\frac{3840\,(2025 c^{2} + 15570 c + 29554)}
 {9 c \cdot c^{5} (5c+22)^{3}}
 \;=\; \frac{-1280\,(2025 c^{2} + 15570 c + 29554)}{3\, c^{6}(5c+22)^{3}},
\]
where $3840/9 = 1280/3$. The quadratic numerator has discriminant
$15570^{2} - 4 \cdot 2025 \cdot 29554 = 3{,}037{,}500 =
2^{2} \cdot 3^{5} \cdot 5^{5}$, with square root $450 \sqrt{15}$
irrational, so $2025 c^{2} + 15570 c + 29554$ is
$\mathbb{Q}$-irreducible.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Closed form at weight 10}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:s10-virasoro-closed-form}Closed form for
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_{10}(\Vir_c)$]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The weight-$10$ weighted Riccati-metric Virasoro coefficient is
\[
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_{10}(\Vir_c)
 \;=\; \frac{256\,(91125 c^{3} + 1050975 c^{2} + 3989790 c + 4969967)}
 {c^{7}\, (5 c + 22)^{4}}
 \;\in\; \mathbb{Q}(c).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Write $S_j$ for $\widehat S^{\rm wt}_j(\Vir_c)$ inside this
calculation.
At $r = 10$ the transport sum runs over pairs $(j, k)$ with
$j + k = 12$, $3 \leq j \leq k < 10$: namely $(3, 9)$, $(4, 8)$,
$(5, 7)$, and the diagonal $(6, 6)$ with $f(6, 6) = \tfrac{1}{2}$.
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence} gives
\[
 S_{10} \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{10 c}
 \bigl[\, 3 \cdot 9 \cdot S_3 S_9
 + 4 \cdot 8 \cdot S_4 S_8
 + 5 \cdot 7 \cdot S_5 S_7
 + \tfrac{1}{2} \cdot 6 \cdot 6 \cdot S_6^{2} \,\bigr].
\]
Substituting the closed forms of $S_3$ through $S_9$: each product
has its own canonical $c$-exponent and $(5c+22)$-exponent; after
promotion to the common denominator $c^{7}(5c+22)^{4}$ via the
appropriate cofactors ($(5c+22), (5c+22)^{2}, (5c+22)^{1},
(5c+22)^{0}$ respectively, together with $c, c, c^{2}, c$),
integer arithmetic on the resulting cubic numerator yields
$91125 c^{3} + 1050975 c^{2} + 3989790 c + 4969967$, with total
prefactor $-2560/10 = -256$; the intermediate minus sign combines
to give
\[
 S_{10} \;=\; \frac{256\,(91125 c^{3} + 1050975 c^{2}
 + 3989790 c + 4969967)}{c^{7} (5c+22)^{4}}.
\]
The symbolic arithmetic is implemented at
\texttt{compute/lib/shadow\_tower\_higher\_vir.py::s10\_virasoro}
and cross-verified against
\texttt{virasoro\_shadow\_sequence(c, max\_r = 10)[10]} with
\texttt{sp.simplify} returning zero. The leading numerator
coefficient $91125 = 3^{6} \cdot 5^{3}$ is $\{3, 5\}$-smooth; the
subleading $1050975 = 3^{3} \cdot 5^{2} \cdot 1557$; the constant
term $4969967$ is prime, lying outside $\mathrm{IrrKum}$ through
$p \leq 10^{4}$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Closed form at weight 11}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:s11-virasoro-closed-form}Closed form for
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_{11}(\Vir_c)$]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The weight-$11$ weighted Riccati-metric Virasoro coefficient is
\[
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_{11}(\Vir_c)
 \;=\; \frac{-15360\,(91125 c^{3} + 990225 c^{2} + 3500190 c
 + 3988097)}
 {11\, c^{8}\, (5 c + 22)^{4}}
 \;\in\; \mathbb{Q}(c).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Write $S_j$ for $\widehat S^{\rm wt}_j(\Vir_c)$ inside this
calculation.
At $r = 11$ the transport sum runs over pairs $(j, k)$ with
$j + k = 13$, $3 \leq j \leq k < 11$: namely $(3, 10)$, $(4, 9)$,
$(5, 8)$, $(6, 7)$ (the diagonal is absent for $j + k$ odd).
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence} gives
\[
 S_{11} \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{11 c}
 \bigl[\, 30\, S_3 S_{10} + 36\, S_4 S_9 + 40\, S_5 S_8
 + 42\, S_6 S_7 \,\bigr].
\]
Substituting the closed forms of $S_3$ through $S_{10}$ and
reducing to the common denominator $c^{8}(5c+22)^{4}$ produces the
cubic numerator $91125 c^{3} + 990225 c^{2} + 3500190 c + 3988097$
with overall prefactor $-15360 / 11$. Symbolic arithmetic is
implemented at \texttt{compute/lib/shadow\_tower\_higher\_vir.py}
in the \texttt{virasoro\_shadow\_sequence} engine at
\texttt{max\_r = 11}; \texttt{sp.simplify(seq[11] - s11\_claimed)}
is identically zero. The cubic constant term $3988097$ is prime
(verified by \texttt{sympy.isprime}), and lies outside
$\mathrm{IrrKum}$ through $p \leq 10^{4}$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Closed-form asymptotic}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:shadow-tower-asymptotic-closed-form}Closed
form for the leading asymptotic]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For every $r \geq 4$, the large-$c$ leading coefficient
$A_r := \lim_{c \to \infty} c^{r - 2}
\widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c)$ has closed form
\[
 \widehat S^{\rm wt}_r(\Vir_c)
 \;=\; \frac{A_r}{c^{r - 2}} \;+\; O(c^{-(r - 1)}),
 \qquad A_r \;=\; \frac{8\,(-6)^{r - 4}}{r}.
\]
Equivalently the sequence obeys the recurrence
\[
 A_r \;=\; -\,\frac{6 (r - 1)}{r}\, A_{r - 1},
 \qquad A_4 \;=\; 2,
\]
with explicit values $A_4 = 2$, $A_5 = -48/5$, $A_6 = 48$,
$A_7 = -1728/7$, $A_8 = 1296$, $A_9 = -6912$, $A_{10} = 186624/5$,
$A_{11} = -2239488/11$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Write $S_j$ for $\widehat S^{\rm wt}_j(\Vir_c)$ inside this proof.
\emph{Step 1: leading contribution comes from the $(j, k) = (3, r - 1)$
pair.} In the master-equation recurrence
\[
 S_r \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{r c}
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 3 \le j \le k < r}}
 f(j, k)\, j k\, S_j S_k,
\]
each summand's $c$-exponent at infinity is
$\mathrm{ord}_{c, \infty}(S_j) + \mathrm{ord}_{c, \infty}(S_k) =
-(j - 2) - (k - 2) = -(r - 2)$ for $j, k \geq 4$ (using
$\mathrm{ord}_{c, \infty}(S_j) = -(j - 2)$ for $j \geq 4$), while
the unique pair with $j = 3$ has
$\mathrm{ord}_{c, \infty}(S_3) + \mathrm{ord}_{c, \infty}(S_{r - 1})
= 0 - (r - 3) = -(r - 3)$. Dividing by $-r c$ yields
$\mathrm{ord}_{c, \infty} = -(r - 2)$ for the $(3, r - 1)$ summand
and $\mathrm{ord}_{c, \infty} = -(r - 1)$ for every $(j, k)$ with
$j \geq 4$. Hence only the $(3, r - 1)$ pair contributes to the
leading $c^{-(r - 2)}$ coefficient $A_r$.

\emph{Step 2: extract $A_r$.} The $(3, r - 1)$ summand has weight
$3 \cdot (r - 1) \cdot S_3 \cdot S_{r - 1}$. At leading order
$S_{r - 1} = A_{r - 1} / c^{r - 3}$ and $S_3 = 2$. Dividing by
$-r c$ and matching the $c^{-(r - 2)}$ coefficient:
\[
 A_r \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{r} \cdot 3 (r - 1) \cdot 2 \cdot A_{r - 1}
 \;=\; -\,\frac{6 (r - 1)}{r}\, A_{r - 1}.
\]

\emph{Step 3: solve the recurrence.} Telescoping from $r = 4$:
\[
 A_r \;=\; A_4 \cdot \prod_{j = 5}^{r} \Bigl(-\,\frac{6 (j - 1)}{j}\Bigr)
 \;=\; A_4 \cdot (-6)^{r - 4} \cdot \prod_{j = 5}^{r} \frac{j - 1}{j}
 \;=\; 2 \cdot (-6)^{r - 4} \cdot \frac{4}{r}
 \;=\; \frac{8 (-6)^{r - 4}}{r},
\]
using $A_4 = 2$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:sth-leading-asymp}) and the
telescoping $\prod_{j = 5}^{r} (j - 1)/j = 4/r$.

\emph{Step 4: numerical check.} The closed form gives
$A_4 = 8 \cdot 1/4 = 2$; $A_5 = 8 \cdot (-6)/5 = -48/5$;
$A_6 = 8 \cdot 36/6 = 48$; $A_7 = 8 \cdot (-216)/7 = -1728/7$;
$A_8 = 8 \cdot 1296/8 = 1296$; $A_9 = 8 \cdot (-7776)/9 = -6912$;
$A_{10} = 8 \cdot 46656/10 = 186624/5$;
$A_{11} = 8 \cdot (-279936)/11 = -2239488/11$. Each value is
independently confirmed by
\texttt{sp.limit(seq[r] * c**(r - 2), c, sp.oo)} run on the
sequence from \texttt{virasoro\_shadow\_sequence(c, max\_r = 11)}
(eight-fold agreement, zero symbolic difference).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[\label{cor:virasoro-23-smoothness}Every leading
numerator is $\{2, 3\}$-smooth]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For every $r \geq 4$, $r \cdot A_r = 8 \cdot (-6)^{r - 4}$ is a
pure $\{2, 3\}$-smooth signed integer, and the denominator of $A_r$
in lowest terms over $\mathbb{Q}$ equals $r$ stripped of its
$\{2, 3\}$-smooth part:
$\mathrm{denom}(A_r) = r / \gcd(r,\, 2^{\infty} 3^{\infty})$. No
prime $\geq 5$ other than divisors of $r$ appears in $A_r$; in
particular no Kummer-irregular prime (e.g.\ $691, 3617$) appears in
any $A_r$ through $r = 11$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-asymptotic-closed-form},
$r \cdot A_r = 8 \cdot (-6)^{r - 4} = (-1)^{r - 4}
\cdot 2^{r - 1} \cdot 3^{r - 4}$, purely $\{2, 3\}$-smooth with
sign. In lowest terms $A_r = \varepsilon_r \cdot 2^{r - 1}
\cdot 3^{r - 4}/r$, so the denominator is $r$ after cancelling its
$\{2, 3\}$-smooth part. Numerator primes are in $\{2, 3\}$ only;
primes $\geq 5$ appear in $A_r$ only as residual denominator
contributions from $\{2, 3\}$-rough divisors of $r$ (e.g.
$5 \mid \mathrm{denom}(A_5)$, $7 \mid \mathrm{denom}(A_7)$,
$5 \mid \mathrm{denom}(A_{10})$, $11 \mid \mathrm{denom}(A_{11})$).

Kummer-irregular primes ordered by size begin at $37$. Hence for
$r \leq 11$, no Kummer-irregular prime can divide $r$, and none appears
in the $\{2, 3\}$-smooth numerator. The claim holds through $r = 11$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[\label{cor:virasoro-motivic-purity-r-leq-11}Motivic
purity through weight 11 (SPECIAL CASE of
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-motivic-rationality-all-r})]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For $r \in \{2, 3, \ldots, 11\}$ the motivic lift of the weighted
Riccati-metric Virasoro coefficient is purely rational in $c$:
\[
 \widehat S_r^{{\rm wt},\mathrm{mot}}(\Vir_c)
 \;=\; \widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c) \;\in\; \mathbb{Q}(c)
 \;\subset\; \MZV^{\mathrm{mot}}_{r} \otimes \mathbb{Q}(c),
\]
with no multiple-zeta contribution $\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(n)$ at any
weight in the weighted tower in this range.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Immediate specialisation of
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-motivic-rationality-all-r}
(\texttt{motivic\_shadow\_tower.tex}):
$\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c) \in \mathbb{Q}(c)$ for every
$r \ge 2$ unconditionally, by the master-equation recurrence preserving
$\mathbb{Q}(c)$-rationality at each step. The range
$r \le 11$ is the finite subset with explicit closed-form
verification via
Theorems~\ref{thm:s9-virasoro-closed-form},
\ref{thm:s10-virasoro-closed-form},
\ref{thm:s11-virasoro-closed-form}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:motivic-purity-all-r-supersession}%
All-$r$ motivic purity]
The all-$r$ Virasoro motivic rationality of
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-motivic-rationality-all-r}
strictly contains the $r \le 11$ scope of
Corollary~\ref{cor:virasoro-motivic-purity-r-leq-11}: the
$\mathbb{Q}(c)$-rationality of $\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)$ holds
for every $r \ge 2$ without the finite-range restriction. The finite
range $r\le 11$ remains useful because the coefficients are written
out explicitly and are used by the arithmetic-duality statements
(\texttt{z\_g\_kummer\_bernoulli\_platonic.tex},
\texttt{higher\_kummer\_arithmetic\_duality\_platonic.tex}).

For every family in the standard class-M landscape for which
Theorem~\ref{thm:motivic-shadow-full-class-m} applies (Virasoro,
$W_N$ for any $N$, BP, $W_\infty$, irrational coset), the shadow tower is
$\mathbb{Q}(c)$-rational at every $r \ge 2$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:motivic-shadow-full-class-m}).
The $E_1$-chiral residue structure of the recurrence forces
$\mathbb{Q}(c)$-rationality at every step; depth-2 MZV would
require $E_2$-associator structure absent from the shadow tower
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-depth-1-rationality}).
\end{remark}

\subsection{Subleading asymptotic and characteristic-prime layer}
\label{subsec:subleading-asymptotic}

The leading coefficient $A_r$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-asymptotic-closed-form} is
$\{2, 3\}$-smooth with a denominator tail from primes dividing $r$.
The \emph{subleading} coefficient
\[
 B_r \;:=\; \lim_{c \to \infty} c \Bigl(
 c^{r - 2}\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c) - A_r \Bigr)
\]
is the next term in the Laurent expansion of
$\Phi_r(c) := c^{r - 2}\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)$ at
$c = \infty$:
\[
 \Phi_r(c) \;=\; A_r \;+\; \frac{B_r}{c} \;+\; \frac{\Gamma_r}{c^2}
 \;+\; O(c^{-3}).
\]
The following theorem gives the exact closed form for $B_r$.

\begin{lemma}[\label{lem:subleading-combinatorial-identity}Combinatorial
identity for the subleading source]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For every integer $r \geq 5$,
\[
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 4 \le j \le k \le r - 2}} f(j, k)
 \;=\; \frac{r - 5}{2},
\]
where $f(j, k) = 1$ if $j < k$ and $f(j, k) = 1/2$ if $j = k$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The constraints $4 \le j \le k$ and $j + k = r + 2$ force
$k = r + 2 - j \le r - 2$, i.e.\ $j \ge 4$, and $j \le (r + 2)/2$.

\emph{Case $r$ odd.} Then $j + k = r + 2$ is odd, so $j \neq k$ and
every summand has $f = 1$. The admissible range is
$4 \le j \le (r + 1)/2$, containing $(r + 1)/2 - 4 + 1 = (r - 5)/2$
integers. The sum equals $(r - 5)/2$.

\emph{Case $r$ even.} The midpoint $j = k = (r + 2)/2$ is attained;
its contribution is $f = 1/2$. The off-diagonal range
$4 \le j \le r/2$ contributes $(r - 6)/2$ unit summands (each with
$f = 1$). The total is $(r - 6)/2 + 1/2 = (r - 5)/2$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:shadow-tower-subleading-closed-form}Closed
form for the subleading asymptotic]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For every $r \geq 4$, the subleading coefficient admits the
two-term closed form
\[
 B_r \;=\; -\,A_r \left[ \frac{22}{5} + \frac{(r - 4)(r - 5)}{18} \right]
 \;=\; -\,\frac{4 \, (-6)^{r - 4} \, (5 r^{2} - 45 r + 496)}{45\, r}.
\]
The first factor $22/5$ is the geometric-series contribution from
the universal denominator factor $5 c + 22$; the second factor
$(r - 4)(r - 5)/18$ is the \emph{Riccati-source contribution}
generated by the cross-pairs $(j, k)$ with $j, k \geq 4$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1: recursive decomposition of $B_r$.} Substituting
$\Phi_r = c^{r - 2}\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}$ into the
master-equation recurrence, writing $S_j$ for
$\widehat S_j^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)$ in this calculation,
$S_r = -(1 / r c) \sum_{j + k = r + 2,\, 3 \le j \le k < r}
f(j, k)\, j k\, S_j S_k$ and using the identity $j + k = r + 2$ to
cancel the shared $c^{4 - j - k} = c^{2 - r}$ factors yields the
\emph{rescaled recurrence}
\[
 r\, \Phi_r\, c \;=\; -\,\sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 3 \le j \le k < r}}
 f(j, k)\, j k\, \Phi_j \Phi_k,
\]
or equivalently $\Phi_r = -(1 / r c) \sum f(j, k) j k \Phi_j \Phi_k$.
The factor $\Phi_3 = 2 c$ has \emph{negative} order at $c = \infty$
(order $-1$ as a Laurent monomial in $u := 1/c$), whereas every
$\Phi_j$ with $j \geq 4$ has order $0$. Splitting the index set
according to whether $j = 3$ or $j \geq 4$:
\begin{align*}
 \Phi_r
 &= -\,\frac{6 (r - 1)}{r} \Phi_{r - 1}
 \;-\; \frac{1}{r c}
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 4 \le j \le k \le r - 2}}
 f(j, k)\, j k\, \Phi_j \Phi_k.
\end{align*}
Here the $(3, r - 1)$ contribution simplifies via $\Phi_3 = 2 c$:
$-(1 / r c) \cdot 3 (r - 1) \cdot (2 c) \cdot \Phi_{r - 1}
 = -6 (r - 1) / r \cdot \Phi_{r - 1}$.

\emph{Step 2: Laurent-coefficient matching.} Write
$\Phi_r = A_r + B_r / c + \Gamma_r / c^2 + \cdots$ for
$r \geq 4$. Matching the $c^0$ coefficient reproduces the leading
recurrence $A_r = -6 (r - 1) A_{r - 1} / r$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-asymptotic-closed-form}. Matching the
$c^{-1}$ coefficient gives
\[
 B_r \;=\; -\,\frac{6 (r - 1)}{r} B_{r - 1}
 \;-\; \frac{1}{r}
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 4 \le j \le k \le r - 2}}
 f(j, k)\, j k\, A_j A_k.
\]
Define the \emph{source term}
$\sigma_r := (1/r) \sum_{j + k = r + 2,\, 4 \le j \le k \le r - 2}
f(j, k) j k A_j A_k$.

\emph{Step 3: source-to-leading identity.} Using the closed form
$A_r = 8 (-6)^{r - 4} / r$,
\[
 j k \, A_j A_k \;=\; 64 \cdot (-6)^{j + k - 8} \;=\; 64 \cdot (-6)^{r - 6}
\]
is independent of the partition $(j, k)$ of $r + 2 - 4 - 4 = r - 6$.
Therefore
\[
 \sigma_r \;=\; \frac{64 \cdot (-6)^{r - 6}}{r}
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 4 \le j \le k \le r - 2}} f(j, k)
 \;=\; \frac{64 \cdot (-6)^{r - 6}}{r} \cdot \frac{r - 5}{2}
\]
by Lemma~\ref{lem:subleading-combinatorial-identity}. Dividing by
$A_r$:
\[
 \frac{\sigma_r}{A_r}
 \;=\; \frac{32 \, (-6)^{r - 6} (r - 5) / r}{8 \, (-6)^{r - 4} / r}
 \;=\; \frac{4 (r - 5)}{(-6)^{2}}
 \;=\; \frac{r - 5}{9}.
\]
Thus $\sigma_r / A_r = (r - 5) / 9$ for every $r \geq 5$ (with
$\sigma_5 = 0$ since the index set is empty).

\emph{Step 4: variation of parameters.} The homogeneous recurrence
$A_r = -6 (r - 1) A_{r - 1} / r$ admits $A_r$ as its unique
solution up to scaling. Writing $B_r = A_r \cdot \phi_r$ and
substituting into the inhomogeneous recurrence of Step 2:
\[
 A_r \phi_r \;=\; -\,\frac{6 (r - 1)}{r} A_{r - 1} \phi_{r - 1}
 \;-\; \sigma_r
 \;=\; A_r \phi_{r - 1} \;-\; \sigma_r,
\]
so $\phi_r - \phi_{r - 1} = -\sigma_r / A_r = -(r - 5) / 9$ by
Step 3. Telescoping from the base value $\phi_4 = B_4 / A_4$
(computed below):
\[
 \phi_r \;=\; \phi_4 \;-\; \sum_{s = 5}^{r} \frac{s - 5}{9}
 \;=\; \phi_4 \;-\; \frac{(r - 4)(r - 5)}{18}.
\]

\emph{Step 5: base case.} At $r = 4$, $S_4 = 10 / [c (5 c + 22)]$ so
$\Phi_4 = c^2 S_4 = 10 c / (5 c + 22) = 2 / (1 + 22 / (5 c))$.
Expanding geometrically:
\[
 \Phi_4(c) \;=\; 2 \sum_{k \geq 0} \left( -\,\frac{22}{5 c} \right)^{k}
 \;=\; 2 \;-\; \frac{44}{5 c} \;+\; \frac{968}{25 c^{2}} \;-\; \cdots,
\]
giving $A_4 = 2$ and $B_4 = -44/5$, whence $\phi_4 = -22/5$.

\emph{Step 6: closed form.} Combining Steps 4--5,
$\phi_r = -22/5 - (r - 4)(r - 5) / 18$, and
$B_r = A_r \phi_r$. Rewriting with common denominator $90$:
\[
 B_r \;=\; -\,\frac{A_r}{90} \bigl[ 396 + 5 (r - 4)(r - 5) \bigr]
 \;=\; -\,\frac{A_r}{90} (5 r^{2} - 45 r + 496).
\]
Substituting $A_r = 8 (-6)^{r - 4} / r$ yields
$B_r = -4 (-6)^{r - 4} (5 r^{2} - 45 r + 496) / (45 r)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[\label{cor:subleading-characteristic-primes}Riccati-
arithmetic primes of the subleading layer]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The \emph{subleading polynomial} $q(r) := 5 r^{2} - 45 r + 496$ has
discriminant $\Delta = 45^{2} - 4 \cdot 5 \cdot 496 = -7895 < 0$;
therefore $q(r) \geq 1579/4 > 0$ for every real $r$, attained at
$r = 9/2$. The prime factorizations of $q(r)$ control the
\emph{new} primes appearing in $B_r$ beyond those of $A_r$:
\[
 q(4) = 2^{2} \cdot 3^{2} \cdot 11, \quad
 q(5) = 2^{2} \cdot 3^{2} \cdot 11, \quad
 q(6) = 2 \cdot 7 \cdot 29, \quad
 q(7) = 2 \cdot 3 \cdot 71,
\]
\[
 q(8) = 2^{3} \cdot 3 \cdot 19, \quad
 q(9) = 2^{4} \cdot 31, \quad
 q(10) = 2 \cdot 3 \cdot 7 \cdot 13, \quad
 q(11) = 2 \cdot 3 \cdot 101.
\]
Among these primes, only $101$ is Kummer-irregular by size, with
$101 \mid \mathrm{num}(B_{68})$. None of the displayed primes belongs
to the Bernoulli-leading pair $\{691,3617\}$. In particular, the
sharpness caveat of
Theorem~\ref{thm:s-r-kummer-absent-through-r-11} (stating that the
two \emph{Bernoulli-leading} Kummer witnesses $\{691, 3617\}$ are
absent from $S_r$ as rational function through $r = 11$) extends to
the entire subleading asymptotic layer through $r = 11$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The discriminant computation is elementary. Substituting
$r = 4,5,\ldots,11$ into $q(r)$ gives the displayed factorisations.
The primes $\{7,11,13,19,29,31\}$ are below the first
Kummer-irregular prime by size, namely $37$. The prime $71$ is regular:
no numerator $\mathrm{num}(B_{2m})$ with $2 \leq 2m \leq 68$ is
divisible by $71$. The prime $101$ is Kummer-irregular via
$101\mid\mathrm{num}(B_{68})$. Thus the only Kummer emergence in
$q(r)$ through $r=11$ is the single prime $101$ at $r=11$. The two
\emph{Bernoulli-leading} Kummer-irregular primes $\{691, 3617\}$
(smallest by Bernoulli index, $691 \mid B_{12}$ and $3617 \mid
B_{16}$) are absent from $q(r)$ for every $r \le 11$. See
Remark~\ref{rem:subleading-kummer-correction} for the
Bernoulli-leading vs size-leading distinction.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Sub-subleading asymptotic: the Tier-3 closed form and the
emergence of the Kummer-irregular prime $691$}
\label{subsec:sub-subleading-asymptotic}

The leading and subleading coefficients, $A_r$ and $B_r$, were
$\{2,3\}$-smooth modulo a divisor-of-$r$ tail and a two-term
Zamolodchikov-Riccati factorisation, respectively. The
\emph{sub-subleading} coefficient
\[
 \Gamma_r \;:=\; \lim_{c \to \infty} c^{2}
 \bigl( c^{r - 2}\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c) - A_r - B_r / c \bigr)
\]
is the next Laurent coefficient of
$\Phi_r(c) := c^{r-2}\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)$ at
$c = \infty$. The theorem below
gives its exact closed form and explains why the Kummer-irregular prime
$691$ first emerges at $r = 8$.

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:shadow-tower-sub-subleading-closed-form-inline}%
Closed form for the sub-subleading asymptotic]
\ClaimStatusProvedElsewhere
For every $r \geq 4$, the sub-subleading coefficient admits the
three-term closed form
\[
 \frac{\Gamma_r}{A_r} \;=\; \frac{484}{25}
 \;+\; \frac{22}{45}\,(r - 4)(r - 5)
 \;+\; \frac{(r - 4)(r - 5)(r - 6)(r - 7)}{972}.
\]
The first term is the geometric-square $(-22/5)^{2} = 484/25$
inherited from the base case. The second term is the mixing
contribution from the Zamolodchikov norm factor. The third term is
the pure Riccati-source correction generated by cross-pair
$(A_j B_k + B_j A_k)$ summation.
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[Attribution]
The canonical inscription of this theorem, with the full variation-
of-parameters derivation and the dedicated Kummer-$691$ dissection,
is Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-sub-subleading-closed-form} in
the sub-subleading platonic chapter. The six-step proof body below
is retained as a self-contained alternative route via the cubic
combinatorial identity (Lemma~\ref{lem:sub-subleading-cubic-identity});
it is not independent of the canonical proof, and the label
\texttt{thm:shadow-tower-sub-subleading-closed-form} resolves to the
canonical site. The corollaries
\ref{cor:kummer-emergence-at-r-8} and
\ref{cor:tier-3-characteristic-primes} are stated here (unique
labels) because they carry the explicit $r = 8$ arithmetic and the
Tier-3 prime-content table through $r = 11$.
\end{remark}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1: sub-subleading recurrence.} Expanding
$\Phi_r = A_r + B_r / c + \Gamma_r / c^{2} + O(c^{-3})$ in the
rescaled Riccati recurrence
$r c \Phi_r = -\sum_{j + k = r + 2,\, 3 \le j \le k < r}
f(j, k)\, j k\, \Phi_j \Phi_k$ (from
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-subleading-closed-form}, Step~1),
and matching the $c^{0}$ coefficient (which on the left-hand side
is $\Gamma_r$ due to the multiplication by $c$), yields
\[
 \Gamma_r \;=\; -\,\frac{6 (r - 1)}{r}\, \Gamma_{r - 1}
 \;-\; \frac{1}{r}
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 4 \le j \le k \le r - 2}}
 f(j, k)\, j k\, \bigl( A_j B_k + B_j A_k \bigr).
\]
The $\Phi_3 \Phi_{r-1}$ term contributes $-6(r-1)/r \cdot \Gamma_{r-1}$
via $\Phi_3 = 2 c$ (the same homogeneous propagation structure as
in Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-asymptotic-closed-form} and
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-subleading-closed-form}).

\emph{Step 2: source-term closed form.} Using
$A_j B_k + B_j A_k = -A_j A_k \bigl[ 44/5 + ((j-4)(j-5) +
(k-4)(k-5))/18 \bigr]$ and the partition-invariance identity
$j k \cdot A_j A_k = 64 \cdot (-6)^{r - 6}$ (from the proof of
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-subleading-closed-form}):
\begin{align*}
 \sigma_r^{\Gamma}
 &= -\,64 \cdot (-6)^{r-6} \left[ \frac{22(r-5)}{5}
 \;+\; \frac{1}{18}
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 4 \le j \le k \le r-2}}
 f(j, k) P_{jk} \right]
\end{align*}
where $P_{jk} := (j-4)(j-5) + (k-4)(k-5)$ and the combinatorial
identity of
Lemma~\ref{lem:subleading-combinatorial-identity} gives
$\sum f(j, k) = (r-5)/2$.

\emph{Step 3: cubic combinatorial identity for $P_{jk}$.}
\begin{lemma}[\label{lem:sub-subleading-cubic-identity}
Cubic combinatorial identity]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For every integer $r \geq 5$,
$\sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 4 \le j \le k \le r-2}}
f(j, k)\, P_{jk} = (r-5)(r-6)(r-7)/3$.
\end{lemma}
\noindent \emph{Proof of Lemma.} By symmetry under the
involution $(j, k) \leftrightarrow (k, j)$, the sum reduces to
$2 \sum_i f_i \cdot i(i-1)$ where $i = j - 4$ ranges from $0$ to
$\lfloor (r-6)/2 \rfloor$. Summing the cubic polynomial values at
$r = 6, 7, \ldots, 12$ yields the sequence
$0, 0, 2, 8, 20, 40, 70$ whose third differences are constant $=2$;
polynomial interpolation gives $(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)/3$. \qedlem

\emph{Step 4: source-to-leading ratio for $\Gamma$.} Dividing
$\sigma_r^{\Gamma}$ by $A_r = 288 \cdot (-6)^{r-6} / r$:
\[
 \frac{\sigma_r^{\Gamma}}{A_r}
 \;=\; -\,\frac{2 r}{9}\, (r-5)
 \left[ \frac{22}{5} + \frac{(r-6)(r-7)}{54} \right].
\]

\emph{Step 5: variation-of-parameters telescoping.} Writing
$\Gamma_r = A_r \cdot \gamma_r$ and substituting:
$\gamma_r = \gamma_{r-1} - (1/r) \cdot \sigma_r^{\Gamma}/A_r$, so
\[
 \gamma_r \;-\; \gamma_{r-1}
 \;=\; \frac{2}{9} (r-5)
 \left[ \frac{22}{5} + \frac{(r-6)(r-7)}{54} \right].
\]
The base case $\gamma_4 = (-22/5)^{2} = 484/25$ follows from
direct geometric expansion of
$\Phi_4 = 10 c/(5 c + 22) = 2 (1 - 22/(5c) + (22/(5c))^{2} - \cdots)$.

\emph{Step 6: telescoping sums.} Summing from $s = 5$ to $r$:
the linear term gives $(22/45) (r-4)(r-5)$ via the triangular
identity $\sum_{s=5}^{r} (s - 5) = (r-4)(r-5)/2$; the cubic term
gives $(r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)/972$ via
$\sum_{s=5}^{r} (s-5)(s-6)(s-7) = (r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)/4$ (the
standard identity
$\sum_{t = 0}^{N} t(t-1)(t-2) = (N+1) N (N-1) (N-2)/4$ evaluated at
$N = r - 5$).

Combining with $\gamma_4 = 484/25$ yields the claim.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[\label{cor:kummer-emergence-at-r-8}Emergence of the
Kummer-irregular prime $691$ at $\Gamma_{8}$]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
At $r = 8$ the sub-subleading coefficient factorises as
\[
 \frac{\Gamma_{8}}{A_{8}} \;=\; \frac{484}{25}
 + \frac{264}{45} + \frac{24}{972}
 \;=\; \frac{39204 + 11880 + 50}{2025}
 \;=\; \frac{51134}{2025}
 \;=\; \frac{2 \cdot 37 \cdot 691}{3^{4} \cdot 5^{2}}.
\]
Hence $\Gamma_{8} = A_{8} \cdot 51134 / 2025 = 1296 \cdot 51134 /
2025 = 2^{5} \cdot 37 \cdot 691 / 5^{2}$. The prime $691$ is the
\emph{first} Kummer-irregular prime (i.e.\ $691 \mid
\mathrm{num}(B_{12})$) and its emergence at $r = 8$ is the sharp
lower boundary of the Kummer-irregular regime in the Laurent
asymptotic stratification of $\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Direct evaluation:
$(r-4)(r-5) = 12$, $(r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7) = 24$ at $r = 8$. Therefore
$\Gamma_{8}/A_{8} = 484/25 + 22 \cdot 12 / 45 + 24/972 = 484/25 +
264/45 + 2/81$. Common denominator $2025 = 3^{4} \cdot 5^{2}$:
$484 \cdot 81 + 264 \cdot 45 + 2 \cdot 25 = 39204 + 11880 + 50 =
51134$. Integer factorisation $51134 = 2 \cdot 37 \cdot 691$
(verified symbolically in
\texttt{compute/tests/test\_sub\_subleading\_asymptotic.py}).
The combinatorial sum $39204 + 11880 + 50 = 51134$ channels the
prime $691$ through the Tier-3 closed form.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:gamma-not-beta-squared}Sub-subleading $\neq$
subleading squared]
The naive guess
$\Gamma_r / A_r \stackrel{?}{=} (B_r / A_r)^{2} = \beta_r^{2}$
\emph{fails}. The exact discrepancy is
\[
 \frac{\Gamma_r}{A_r} \;-\; \beta_r^{2}
 \;=\; \frac{(r-4)(r-5) \bigl[ (r-6)(r-7) - 3(r-4)(r-5) \bigr]}
 {972}
 \;=\; -\,\frac{(r-4)(r-5)(2 r^{2} - 14 r + 18)}{972}.
\]
At $r = 8$ this discrepancy equals $-34/81$. The non-vanishing of
this correction is the Riccati-source signature: the quadratic
source $\sigma_r^{(\mathrm{quadratic})}$ generated by $B_j B_k$
products at $r \geq 6$ cross-interacts with the linear source
$\sigma_r^{(\mathrm{linear})}$ generated by $A_j B_k + B_j A_k$,
producing a genuinely new Laurent coefficient not obtainable from
Tier-1 and Tier-2 data alone.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[\label{cor:tier-3-characteristic-primes}Tier-3 prime
content through $r = 11$]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The numerator primes of $\gamma_r := \Gamma_r / A_r$ in lowest
terms for $r = 4, \ldots, 11$ are:
\[\begin{array}{c|c}
 r & \text{numerator primes of } \gamma_r \\
 \hline
 4 & \{2, 11\} \\
 5 & \{2, 11\} \\
 6 & \{2, 11, 13\} \\
 7 & \{2, 11, 19\} \\
 8 & \{2, 37, \mathbf{691}\} \\
 9 & \{2, 13, 43, 53\} \\
 10 & \{2, 13, 19, 47\} \\
 11 & \{2, 29, 1423\}
\end{array}\]
The prime $691$ appears uniquely at $r = 8$; it is the \emph{only}
Kummer-irregular prime in the set $\{691, 3617\}$ that emerges in
the Tier-3 layer through $r = 11$. The second leading
Kummer-irregular prime $3617$ does not appear in any
$\Gamma_r / A_r$ for $r \leq 11$.
\end{corollary}

\subsection{Sub-sub-subleading asymptotic: Tier 4 and the Riccati-
source signature}
\label{subsec:tier-4-asymptotic}

The Laurent stratification extends one further tier down, to
the sub-sub-subleading coefficient
\[
 \Delta_r \;:=\; \lim_{c \to \infty} c^{3}
 \bigl( c^{r - 2}\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)
 - A_r - B_r / c - \Gamma_r / c^{2} \bigr).
\]
This is the first tier where the $B_j B_k$ cross-term (subleading
squared) enters the recurrence: Tier 3 recovers the purely linear
$(A_j B_k + B_j A_k)$ source, while Tier 4 introduces the quadratic
$B_j B_k$ self-coupling.

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:shadow-tower-tier-4-closed-form}Closed
form for the Tier-4 sub-sub-subleading asymptotic]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For every $r \geq 4$, the sub-sub-subleading coefficient admits the
four-term closed form
\[
 \frac{\Delta_r}{A_r}
 \;=\; -\,\frac{10648}{125}
 \;-\; \frac{242}{75}\,(r-4)(r-5)
 \;-\; \frac{11}{810}\,(r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)
 \;-\; \frac{(r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)(r-8)(r-9)}{104976}.
\]
The first term is the geometric-cube base $-\,(-22/5)^{3} =
-10648/125$ inherited from $\Phi_{4}(c) = 10 c/(5 c + 22)$. The
three $(r-4)(r-5)$ polynomial corrections are iterated Riccati
source contributions at successive Tier depths.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{Step 1: Tier-4 recurrence.} Matching the $c^{-1}$ coefficient
on the left-hand side of $r c \Phi_r = -\sum f(j,k) j k \Phi_j \Phi_k$
yields
\[
 \Delta_r \;=\; -\,\frac{6(r-1)}{r}\,\Delta_{r-1}
 \;-\; \frac{1}{r} \sigma_r^{\Delta},
\]
where the Tier-4 source
\[
 \sigma_r^{\Delta} \;=\;
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 4 \le j \le k \le r-2}}
 f(j, k)\, j k\, \bigl( A_j \Gamma_k + B_j B_k + \Gamma_j A_k \bigr).
\]
The novel $B_j B_k$ contribution makes this the first tier carrying
the quadratic Riccati-source self-coupling.

\emph{Step 2: source decomposition.} Using
$\Gamma_k / A_k = \gamma_k$ and $B_j B_k = A_j A_k \cdot (22/5 +
(j-4)(j-5)/18)(22/5 + (k-4)(k-5)/18)$, the source $\sigma_r^{\Delta}$
decomposes as
\[
 \frac{\sigma_r^{\Delta}}{A_r} \;=\;
 \frac{64 r}{288}\,\bigl[
 \underbrace{(968/25) (r-5)/2}_{\gamma\text{-sum at }m=0}
 + \underbrace{(22/45) (r-5)(r-6)(r-7)/3}_{\gamma\text{-sum at }m=2}
 + \underbrace{(1/972) \Sigma_Q}_{\gamma\text{-sum at }m=4}
 \]
 \[
 + (22/5)^{2} (r-5)/2
 + \underbrace{(22/90) (r-5)(r-6)(r-7)/3}_{\text{cross}}
 + (1/324) \Sigma_R
 \bigr]
\]
where $\Sigma_Q := \sum f(j,k) Q_{jk}$ with
$Q_{jk} = (j-4)(j-5)(j-6)(j-7) + (k-4)(k-5)(k-6)(k-7)$, and
$\Sigma_R := \sum f(j,k) R_{jk}$ with
$R_{jk} = (j-4)(j-5)(k-4)(k-5)$.

\emph{Step 3: quintic combinatorial identities
(\label{lem:quintic-identities}).}

\begin{lemma}[\label{lem:quintic-combinatorial}Quintic combinatorial
identities]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For every $r \geq 5$:
\[
 \Sigma_Q \;:=\; \sum_{\substack{j+k=r+2 \\ 4 \le j \le k \le r-2}}
 f(j,k) Q_{jk} \;=\; \frac{(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)(r-8)(r-9)}{5},
\]
\[
 \Sigma_R \;:=\; \sum_{\substack{j+k=r+2 \\ 4 \le j \le k \le r-2}}
 f(j,k) R_{jk} \;=\; \frac{(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)(r-8)(r-9)}{60}.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By symmetry $(j,k) \leftrightarrow (k,j)$,
$\Sigma_Q = 2 \sum f_i i(i-1)(i-2)(i-3)$ with $i = j-4$; polynomial
interpolation on values $0,0,0,0,24,144,504,1344$ at $r = 6,\ldots,13$
gives constant fifth differences equal to $2$ and the unique degree-5
interpolant $(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)(r-8)(r-9)/5$. Similarly
$\Sigma_R$ interpolates to $(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)(r-8)(r-9)/60$; the
coefficient ratio $12$ between the two sums reflects
$Q_{jk}/R_{jk} \sim 12$ averaged over the index set.
\end{proof}

\emph{Step 4: source-to-leading ratio for $\Delta$.} The $\Sigma_Q$
and $\Sigma_R$ contributions combine at the quintic level:
\[
 \frac{1}{972} \cdot \frac{1}{5} + \frac{1}{324} \cdot \frac{1}{60}
 \;=\; \frac{1}{4860} + \frac{1}{19440}
 \;=\; \frac{4 + 1}{19440}
 \;=\; \frac{1}{3888}.
\]
Using also the identity $968/25 + (22/5)^2 = 1452/25$ at $m = 0$ and
$22/45 + 22/90 = 11/15$ at $m = 2$:
\[
 \frac{\sigma_r^{\Delta}}{A_r}
 \;=\; \frac{2 r}{9}\, (r-5)
 \left[ \frac{726}{25}
 + \frac{11}{45} (r-6)(r-7)
 + \frac{1}{3888} (r-6)(r-7)(r-8)(r-9) \right].
\]

\emph{Step 5: variation-of-parameters telescoping.} Writing
$\Delta_r = A_r \delta_r$:
\[
 \delta_r - \delta_{r-1} \;=\; -\,\frac{2}{9} (r-5)
 \left[ \frac{726}{25}
 + \frac{11}{45} (r-6)(r-7)
 + \frac{1}{3888} (r-6)(r-7)(r-8)(r-9) \right].
\]
Base case $\delta_4 = -\,(22/5)^{3} = -10648/125$ from direct
geometric expansion of $\Phi_4 = 10 c/(5 c + 22)$ at third order in
$1/c$.

\emph{Step 6: telescoping sums.} Three identities are used:
\begin{align*}
 \sum_{s=5}^{r} (s-5) &= (r-4)(r-5)/2, \\
 \sum_{s=5}^{r} (s-5)(s-6)(s-7) &= (r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)/4, \\
 \sum_{s=5}^{r} (s-5)(s-6)(s-7)(s-8)(s-9) &=
 (r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)(r-8)(r-9)/6.
\end{align*}
Applying these to the three polynomial terms in Step 5 and
simplifying:
\begin{align*}
 \delta_r + (22/5)^{3}
 &= -\,(2/9)(726/25) \cdot (r-4)(r-5)/2
 \;-\; (2/9)(11/45) (r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)/4 \\
 &\quad\;-\; (2/9)(1/3888) (r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)(r-8)(r-9)/6 \\
 &= -\,(242/75)(r-4)(r-5)
 \;-\; (11/810) (r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7) \\
 &\quad\;-\; (1/104976) (r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)(r-8)(r-9).
\end{align*}
This is the claimed closed form.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Four-tier arithmetic database: Kummer-irregularity is
Laurent-depth controlled, not absent}
\label{subsec:four-tier-arithmetic-database}

The arithmetic duality
Theorem~\ref{thm:z-g-s-r-arithmetic-duality}
(\texttt{z\_g\_kummer\_bernoulli\_platonic.tex}) was stated for the
\emph{two Bernoulli-leading} Kummer-irregular primes
$\{691, 3617\}$: these are the primes dividing
$\mathrm{num}(B_{12})$ and $\mathrm{num}(B_{16})$ respectively, the
two smallest Bernoulli indices admitting Kummer-irregular divisors.
The stratification refines by tabulating the full Kummer-irregular
emergence pattern in each Laurent Tier through $r = 15$.

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:kummer-laurent-depth-controlled}%
Laurent-depth-controlled Kummer emergence]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
Let $\mathrm{IrrKum}_{\mathrm{size}}$ denote the set of
Kummer-irregular primes ordered by size:
$\mathrm{IrrKum}_{\mathrm{size}} = \{37, 59, 67, 101, 103, 131,
149, 157, 233, 257, 263, 271, 283, 293, \ldots, 691, \ldots, 3617,
\ldots\}$ (OEIS A000928). For Virasoro shadow-tower coefficient
numerators in each Laurent Tier $k \in \{1, 2, 3, 4\}$ of
$\Phi_r = c^{r-2}\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)$ at large $c$, the following
emergence table is exact through $r = 15$:

\[\begin{array}{c|l}
 \text{Tier} & \text{Kummer-irregular primes appearing, with } r \text{ of emergence} \\
 \hline
 1 (A_r) & \emptyset \text{ (no Kummer-irregular prime through } r \leq 15\text{)} \\
 2 (B_r) & \{101 \text{ at } r = 11\} \\
 3 (\Gamma_r) & \{37 \text{ at } r = 8,\, 691 \text{ at } r = 8,\, 811 \text{ at } r = 13\} \\
 4 (\Delta_r) & \{37 \text{ at } r = 11,\, 283 \text{ at } r = 13\}
\end{array}\]

In particular: the prime $691$ emerges \emph{uniquely} at $(r, k) =
(8, 3)$; the prime $3617$ does not appear in any Tier through
$r = 15$; but the smaller Kummer-irregular primes $\{37, 101, 283,
811\}$ do appear at specific $(r, k)$ coordinates.

The arithmetic duality
Theorem~\ref{thm:z-g-s-r-arithmetic-duality}, stated for
$\{691, 3617\}$, has exactly this scope: these two primes follow
the Bernoulli-index hierarchy
$691 \mid B_{12}$, $3617 \mid B_{16}$, and are absent from all
Tiers through $r = 15$ except the unique $691$-sighting at Tier~3,
$r = 8$. Smaller Kummer-irregular primes (37, 59, 67, 101, ...)
have different Bernoulli witnesses (e.g., $37 \mid B_{32}$,
$101 \mid B_{68}$) and follow their own emergence patterns in the
Virasoro Laurent stratification.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Direct enumeration via the closed forms
$A_r = 8(-6)^{r-4}/r$,
$B_r / A_r = -\,(22/5) - (r-4)(r-5)/18$,
$\Gamma_r / A_r = 484/25 + (22/45)(r-4)(r-5) +
(r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)/972$, and
$\Delta_r / A_r = -\,(22/5)^{3} - (242/75)(r-4)(r-5) -
(11/810)(r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7) -
(1/104976)(r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)(r-8)(r-9)$.
Each is evaluated at $r = 4, 5, \ldots, 15$; integer numerator in
lowest terms is factored; resulting prime set is intersected with
$\mathrm{IrrKum}_{\mathrm{size}}$. The table is the exact output of
this enumeration (verified symbolically in
\texttt{compute/tests/test\_four\_tier\_kummer\_database.py}).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:kummer-witness-verification-20260417}%
Bernoulli-numerator verification of Kummer witnesses]
The Kummer-irregular labels used in the Laurent-tier table are fixed by
explicit Bernoulli-numerator witnesses:

\emph{Kummer-irregular} (Bernoulli witness):
\[
 37 \mid B_{32},\quad
 101 \mid B_{68},\quad
 283 \mid B_{20},\quad
 691 \mid B_{12},\quad
 811 \mid B_{544},\quad
 13297 \mid B_{1438},\quad
 3617 \mid B_{16}.
\]

\emph{Kummer-regular in the checked range}:
\[
 23 \; (B_{2m}, 2m \leq 20,\; \text{no witness}),\quad
 43 \; (2m \leq 40,\; \text{no witness}),\quad
 419 \; (2m \leq 416,\; \text{no witness}),\quad
 1423 \; (2m \leq 1420,\; \text{no witness}).
\]

\emph{The prime $3067$.} The prime $3067$ has no Bernoulli witness in
$B_{2m}$ for $2m \leq 2000$. Under the Kummer criterion
$p \mid \mathrm{num}(B_{2k})$ for some $2 \leq 2k \leq p - 3$, this
covers the regime $2m \leq 2000 < 3064 = p - 3$; extension to
$2m \leq 3064$ exceeds the current symbolic-computation cost budget
but the failure through $B_{2000}$ makes Kummer-regularity the honest
label at available verification depth. The prime $3067$ still appears
in the $\Gamma_{12}$ numerator as a Riccati-arithmetic characteristic
prime, not as Kummer-arithmetic.

The Tier~3 emergence table of
Theorem~\ref{thm:kummer-laurent-depth-controlled} retains three
entries $\{37, 691, 811\}$; the four-tier emergence statement is
otherwise unchanged. The arithmetic-duality theorem
for the Bernoulli-leading pair $\{691, 3617\}$ is unaffected by the
$3067$ computation: both leading primes are verified Kummer-irregular and
the absence / presence pattern on $S_r$ vs $Z_g$ holds at the stated
scope.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:subleading-kummer-correction}
Bernoulli-leading and size-leading Kummer orderings]
The subleading-polynomial primes
$\{7, 11, 13, 19, 29, 31, 71, 101\}$ through $r = 11$ avoid the two
\emph{Bernoulli-leading} Kummer-irregular primes $\{691, 3617\}$.
They do not avoid the Kummer-irregular primes ordered by size:
$37$ is first by size, followed by $59,67,101,103,\ldots$, and
$101$ appears in
\[
 q(11)=606=2\cdot3\cdot101,\qquad 101\mid B_{68}.
\]
Thus the subleading layer separates two orderings. It is disjoint
from the Bernoulli-leading pair through $r\le11$, but it contains
the size-ordered Kummer witness $101$ at $r=11$.

The full Kummer-Laurent emergence pattern is the content of
Theorem~\ref{thm:kummer-laurent-depth-controlled}.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[\label{cor:bernoulli-leading-duality-sharpness}%
Sharpness of the Bernoulli-leading arithmetic duality]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The two Bernoulli-leading Kummer-irregular primes
$\{691, 3617\}$ satisfy:
\begin{itemize}
\item $691$ appears on $Z_g$ at the leading Bernoulli asymptotic
 for $g = 7$ (via $B_{12}$) and is absent from $S_r$ through
 $r = 15$ \emph{except} at Tier~3, $r = 8$, where it appears in
 the combined sum $39204 + 11880 + 50 = 51134 = 2 \cdot 37 \cdot 691$.
\item $3617$ appears on $Z_g$ at the leading Bernoulli asymptotic
 for $g = 9$ (via $B_{16}$) and is absent from every $S_r$ tier
 through $r = 15$.
\end{itemize}
Therefore the arithmetic duality
Theorem~\ref{thm:z-g-s-r-arithmetic-duality} is \emph{sharp} at
Bernoulli index $12$ with a single Tier-3 exception, and
unconditional at Bernoulli index $16$ through $r = 15$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The first assertion is the explicit factorisation
$51134=2\cdot37\cdot691$ in Tier~3 at $r=8$, together with the
absence computation for the remaining tiers through $r=15$. The
second assertion is the corresponding divisibility check for
$3617\mid B_{16}$ and no occurrence in the displayed $S_r$ tiers
through $r=15$. These are the two boundary cases in
Theorem~\ref{thm:z-g-s-r-arithmetic-duality}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:four-tier-pattern}Four-tier Laurent
stratification pattern]
Combining Theorems \ref{thm:shadow-tower-asymptotic-closed-form},
\ref{thm:shadow-tower-subleading-closed-form},
\ref{thm:shadow-tower-sub-subleading-closed-form}, and
\ref{thm:shadow-tower-tier-4-closed-form}, the four-tier Laurent
stratification of the Virasoro shadow tower at $c = \infty$ has a
remarkable structural pattern:
\[\begin{array}{c|l|l}
 \text{Tier} & \text{coefficient} & \text{closed-form structure} \\
 \hline
 1 & A_r & \tau^{0}, \text{ universal } \{2,3\}\text{-smooth} \\
 2 & B_r / A_r & -\tau - (r-4)(r-5)/18 \\
 3 & \Gamma_r / A_r & \tau^{2} + (\tau/?) (r-4)(r-5) + (r-4)(r-5)(r-6)(r-7)/972 \\
 4 & \Delta_r / A_r & -\tau^{3} - (?) (r-4)(r-5) - (?) (r-4)\cdots(r-7) - (?)(r-4)\cdots(r-9)
\end{array}\]
where $\tau = 22/5$. Each Tier $k$ has exactly $k$ terms (at
polynomial degrees $0, 2, 4, \ldots, 2(k-1)$ in $(r-4)(r-5)\ldots
(r-4-(2m-1))$ for $m = 0, 1, \ldots, k-1$), and the signs alternate
$+, -, +, -, \ldots$ per Tier. This regularity is consistent with an
all-tier closed form
\[
 \text{Tier-}k(r) / A_r \;=\; (-1)^{k+1}\sum_{m=0}^{k-1}
 c^{(k)}_m \cdot \prod_{\ell=0}^{2m-1}(r - 4 - \ell),
\]
with explicit rational coefficients $c^{(k)}_m$ determined by
nested telescoping of the Tier-$k$ combinatorial identities. The
Tier-5 and above closed forms are an open forward extension,
accessible via the same variation-of-parameters technique applied
to the higher partial differences of $A_j B_k + B_j A_k + \Gamma_j A_k
+ A_j \Gamma_k + B_j B_k + \ldots$ (Tier-$k$ source).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:three-tier-arithmetic-picture}Three-tier
arithmetic of the Virasoro shadow tower]
Combining
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-asymptotic-closed-form},
Corollary~\ref{cor:virasoro-23-smoothness},
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-subleading-closed-form},
Corollary~\ref{cor:subleading-characteristic-primes},
Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-sub-subleading-closed-form},
Corollary~\ref{cor:kummer-emergence-at-r-8}, and
Corollary~\ref{cor:tier-3-characteristic-primes}, the Virasoro
weighted shadow $\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)$ stratifies at
$c = \infty$ into three
arithmetic tiers:
\begin{description}
\item[Tier~1 (leading, $A_r$).] Universal $\{2, 3\}$-smooth
 integers modulo residual $\{5, 7, 11, \ldots\}$-contribution from
 divisors of $r$. Arithmetic content: the sign alternation of
 $(-6)^{r - 4}$ and the inverse harmonic normalization $1/r$.
\item[Tier~2 (subleading, $B_r$).] Two-term factorization
 $-A_r \cdot [22/5 + (r - 4)(r - 5)/18]$. The first summand
 records the Zamolodchikov quasi-primary norm
 $\langle \Lambda_4 | \Lambda_4 \rangle = c (5 c + 22)/10$
 (the factor $22/5 = 22/5$); the second summand is the
 \emph{Riccati-specific} contribution $(r - 4)(r - 5)/18$
 generated by the cross-pair cohomological sum. Characteristic
 primes come from $q(r) = 5 r^{2} - 45 r + 496$; the prime
 sequence $\{11, 7, 29, 71, 19, 31, 13, 101, \ldots\}$ is
 Riccati-arithmetic, not Kummer-Bernoulli.
\item[Tier~3 (sub-subleading and beyond, $\Gamma_r, \Delta_r, \ldots$).]
 Higher Laurent coefficients mix the two tiers and introduce
 Kummer-Bernoulli content beginning at
 $\Gamma_{8} = 2^{5} \cdot 37 \cdot 691 / 5^{2}$, where the first
 Kummer-irregular prime $691$ appears. This is the \emph{sharp
 boundary} of the Kummer absence: absent from $S_r$ as rational
 function and from the first two Laurent layers, but present in
 the full expansion at the sub-subleading level.
\end{description}
The three-tier picture separates the universal classical limit
(Tier~1), the Zamolodchikov representation-theoretic arithmetic
(Tier~2), and the Kummer-Bernoulli content inherited from the
Hurwitz-formal cotangent of $\mathrm{Bun}_{\SL_{2}}(\Sigma_{g})$
(Tier~3). The arithmetic duality
Theorem~\ref{thm:z-g-s-r-arithmetic-duality} is refined by this
stratification: the two Bernoulli-leading Kummer witnesses
$\{691, 3617\}$ are absent from \emph{all three tiers} of $S_r$
through $r = 11$ except the unique sighting of $691$ in
$\Gamma_{8}$, and are present on $Z_g$ already at the leading
Bernoulli asymptotic via $B_{12}$ and $B_{16}$.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[\label{lem:floor-parity-subadditive}Parity subadditivity
of the floor]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For integers $a, b \geq 1$,
\[
 \left\lfloor \tfrac{a}{2} \right\rfloor
 + \left\lfloor \tfrac{b}{2} \right\rfloor
 \;\le\;
 \left\lfloor \tfrac{a + b}{2} \right\rfloor,
\]
with equality unless both $a$ and $b$ are odd.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Write $a = 2 p + \alpha$ and $b = 2 q + \beta$ with
$p, q \in \mathbb{Z}_{\geq 0}$ and $\alpha, \beta \in \{0, 1\}$. Then
$\lfloor a/2 \rfloor = p$ and $\lfloor b/2 \rfloor = q$, and
$\lfloor (a + b)/2 \rfloor = p + q + \lfloor (\alpha + \beta)/2 \rfloor$.
The defect
$\lfloor (a + b)/2 \rfloor - \lfloor a/2 \rfloor - \lfloor b/2 \rfloor
 = \lfloor (\alpha + \beta)/2 \rfloor \in \{0, 0, 1\}$
according as $(\alpha, \beta) \in
\{(0, 0), (0, 1), (1, 0), (1, 1)\}$. The defect is $0$ except when
$\alpha = \beta = 1$, in which case it equals $1$. Equivalently,
equality holds unless both $a$ and $b$ are odd.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[\label{cor:floor-shift-j-plus-k}Floor shift on the
index set of the shadow recurrence]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For integers $j, k$ with $j + k = r + 2$, $3 \leq j \leq k$ and
$r \geq 4$,
\[
 \left\lfloor \tfrac{j - 2}{2} \right\rfloor
 + \left\lfloor \tfrac{k - 2}{2} \right\rfloor
 \;\le\;
 \left\lfloor \tfrac{r - 2}{2} \right\rfloor,
\]
with equality unless $j$ and $k$ are both odd.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:floor-parity-subadditive} with $a = j - 2$ and
$b = k - 2$ (so $a, b \geq 1$ since $j, k \geq 3$); then
$a + b = j + k - 4 = r - 2$. Both-odd for $(a, b)$ corresponds to
both-odd for $(j, k)$ by parity shift of $2$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:s-r-rational-denominator-pattern}Rational
denominator pattern for the weighted Virasoro shadow tower]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For every integer $r \geq 4$, the weighted Virasoro shadow coefficient
$\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c) \in \mathbb{Q}(c)$ admits a
presentation with denominator
dividing
\[
 D_r(c) \;:=\; c^{\,r - 3}\,
 (5 c + 22)^{\lfloor (r - 2)/2 \rfloor}.
\]
Equivalently, the polynomial
$\widehat N_r(c) := \widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)\, D_r(c) \in
\mathbb{Q}(c)$ is a
polynomial in $c$. The bound $D_r(c)$ is saturated (no common factor
of $c$ or $5c + 22$ divides both $\widehat N_r$ and $D_r$) through $r = 11$ by
the explicit closed forms of
Theorems~\ref{thm:s6-virasoro-closed-form}--\ref{thm:s11-virasoro-closed-form}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By strong induction on $r \geq 4$, using the Virasoro shadow
recurrence of Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence}.

\medskip
\noindent \emph{Base.} At $r = 4$,
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_4 = 10 / (c (5 c + 22)) = 10 / D_4(c)$ since
$D_4(c) = c^{1} (5 c + 22)^{\lfloor 2/2 \rfloor} = c (5 c + 22)$;
the denominator divides $D_4(c)$. At $r = 5$,
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_5 = - 48 / (c^{2} (5 c + 22)) = -48 / D_5(c)$ since
$D_5(c) = c^{2} (5 c + 22)^{\lfloor 3/2 \rfloor} = c^{2} (5 c + 22)$;
the denominator divides $D_5(c)$.

\medskip
\noindent \emph{Inductive step.} Fix $r \geq 6$ and assume the
conclusion for all $r' \in \{4, 5, \dots, r - 1\}$. By
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence},
\begin{equation} \label{eq:sr-induction-recurrence}
 \widehat S_r^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)
 \;=\; -\,\frac{1}{r c}
 \sum_{\substack{j + k = r + 2 \\ 3 \le j \le k < r}}
 f(j, k)\, j k\, \widehat S_j^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)\,
 \widehat S_k^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c),
\end{equation}
with $f(j, k) \in \{1, \tfrac{1}{2}\}$. Every index $j, k$ on the
right-hand side satisfies $3 \leq j \leq k \leq r - 1$, so
$\widehat S_j^{\rm wt}, \widehat S_k^{\rm wt}$ fall under the
inductive hypothesis:
$\widehat S_j^{\rm wt}$ has denominator dividing $D_j(c) = c^{\,j - 3} (5 c + 22)^{\lfloor (j - 2)/2 \rfloor}$
and similarly for $S_k$.

The product $\widehat S_j^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)\widehat S_k^{\rm wt}(\Vir_c)$ has denominator dividing
\begin{align}
 D_j(c) \cdot D_k(c)
 &\;=\; c^{\,(j - 3) + (k - 3)}\,
 (5 c + 22)^{\lfloor (j - 2)/2 \rfloor
 + \lfloor (k - 2)/2 \rfloor}
 \notag \\
 &\;=\; c^{\,r - 4}\,
 (5 c + 22)^{\lfloor (j - 2)/2 \rfloor
 + \lfloor (k - 2)/2 \rfloor}, \label{eq:sr-induction-productdenom}
\end{align}
using $j + k = r + 2$ in the $c$-exponent. By
Corollary~\ref{cor:floor-shift-j-plus-k} the $(5 c + 22)$-exponent
satisfies
\[
 \lfloor (j - 2)/2 \rfloor + \lfloor (k - 2)/2 \rfloor
 \;\le\;
 \lfloor (r - 2)/2 \rfloor,
\]
so the product denominator $D_j(c) D_k(c)$ divides
$c^{\,r - 4} (5 c + 22)^{\lfloor (r - 2)/2 \rfloor}$.

Each summand
$f(j, k)\, j k\, \widehat S_j^{\rm wt}\widehat S_k^{\rm wt}$ in
\eqref{eq:sr-induction-recurrence} is a rational multiple of
$\widehat S_j^{\rm wt}\widehat S_k^{\rm wt}$, so its denominator
divides the same bound. The finite sum
of summands therefore has denominator dividing
$c^{\,r - 4} (5 c + 22)^{\lfloor (r - 2)/2 \rfloor}$. Multiplying by
the overall prefactor $-1/(r c)$ multiplies the denominator by $c$
(and a rational constant, which does not affect polynomial divisibility
over $\mathbb{Q}(c)$), yielding
\[
 \mathrm{denom}(\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}) \;\mathrm{divides}\;
 c^{\,r - 4 + 1}\,
 (5 c + 22)^{\lfloor (r - 2)/2 \rfloor}
 \;=\;
 c^{\,r - 3}\,
 (5 c + 22)^{\lfloor (r - 2)/2 \rfloor}
 \;=\; D_r(c),
\]
which closes the induction.

\medskip
\noindent \emph{Saturation through $r = 11$.} The denominators of
Theorems~\ref{thm:s6-virasoro-closed-form}--\ref{thm:s11-virasoro-closed-form}
(after cancelling rational constants) are respectively
$c^{3}(5c+22)^{2}$, $c^{4}(5c+22)^{2}$, $c^{5}(5c+22)^{3}$,
$c^{6}(5c+22)^{3}$, $c^{7}(5c+22)^{4}$, $c^{8}(5c+22)^{4}$, matching
$D_6, D_7, \ldots, D_{11}$ exactly. No accidental cancellation
between numerator and denominator occurs through $r = 11$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:sr-denominator-sharpness}Sharpness via the
diagonal and near-diagonal pair]
The upper bound of
Theorem~\ref{thm:s-r-rational-denominator-pattern} is realised
(before the overall $1/(r c)$) by the pair $(j, k) \in
\{((r+2)/2, (r+2)/2)\}$ when $r$ is even (the diagonal summand with
$f(j, j) = 1/2$) and by $(j, k) = ((r+1)/2, (r+3)/2)$ when $r$ is odd
(the near-diagonal summand). In both cases
$\lfloor (j - 2)/2 \rfloor + \lfloor (k - 2)/2 \rfloor
 = \lfloor (r - 2)/2 \rfloor$
by Corollary~\ref{cor:floor-shift-j-plus-k} (equality case: $j, k$ not
both odd). The off-diagonal both-odd pairs such as $(j, k) = (3, r - 1)$
with $r - 1$ odd contribute denominators strictly smaller in the
$(5 c + 22)$ exponent and embed without resistance into the dominant
bound. Saturation of $D_r(c)$ in $\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}$ therefore
reduces to absence of
numerator-denominator cancellation, a finite rational check discharged
through $r = 11$ in the tests.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:denominator-pattern-correction}
Denominator pattern: $c^{r - 3}$, not $c^{r - 2}$]
The weighted Virasoro shadow denominator is
\[
 \mathrm{denom}(\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}) \;=\; c^{r - 3}
 \cdot (5 c + 22)^{\lfloor (r - 2)/2 \rfloor},
 \qquad r \geq 4,
\]
with $c$-exponent $r - 3$, one less than the large-$c$ asymptotic
order. The numerator at each weight carries total $c$-degree
$\lceil (r - 2)/2 \rceil - 1$ (zero at $r = 4, 5$; linear at
$r = 6, 7$; quadratic at $r = 8, 9$; cubic at $r = 10, 11$), so
the large-$c$ order is
$\mathrm{ord}_{c, \infty}(\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}) = -(r - 2)$
consistently. Explicit check through $r = 11$: the denominators of
Theorems~\ref{thm:s6-virasoro-closed-form}--\ref{thm:s11-virasoro-closed-form}
are $c^{3}(5c+22)^{2},\ c^{4}(5c+22)^{2},\ c^{5}(5c+22)^{3},\
c^{6}(5c+22)^{3},\ c^{7}(5c+22)^{4},\ c^{8}(5c+22)^{4}$, matching
$r - 3 \in \{3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8\}$ respectively.

The $(5c + 22)^{\lfloor (r - 2)/2 \rfloor}$ factor is
\emph{Riccati-propagated} from the weight-$4$ Zamolodchikov norm
$\langle \Lambda \mid \Lambda \rangle = c (5c + 22)/10$, not
independently generated at each even weight. Direct Kac-determinant
verification: $\det G_{N = 4,\, h = 0}(\Vir_c) \propto
c^{2}(5c + 22)/2$ and $\det G_{N = 5,\, h = 0}(\Vir_c) \propto
2 c^{2} (5c + 22)$ (both carrying the same $(5c + 22)$ factor).
Higher levels $N \geq 6$ introduce different $c$-polynomial
Kac-determinant factors, which do not appear in any
$\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}$ through $r = 11$. The $(5c + 22)$
multiplicity in $\widehat S_r^{\rm wt}$ is therefore
inherited from a single Riccati-propagation chain (weight-$4$
Zamolodchikov norm iterated through the recurrence), not from
weight-$r$ Kac-module data. No new weight-$r$ Shapovalov norm is
needed through $r = 11$.
\end{remark}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section*{Epilogue}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

The Virasoro shadow tower is closed in a concrete sense through
weight $11$: every coefficient is a specific rational function of
$c$ with a structurally transparent denominator
$c^{r-3} (5c + 22)^{\lfloor (r-2)/2 \rfloor}$; every leading
asymptotic is pinned by the closed-form recurrence
$A_r = 8 (-6)^{r - 4}/r$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-tower-asymptotic-closed-form}); every
weighted coefficient through $r = 8$ is verified against two disjoint derivation
chains (MC master-equation recurrence and Riccati $\sqrt{Q_L}$
Taylor expansion) at four distinct central charges. The
$\widehat S^{\rm wt}_8 = 4144720/19683$ at $c = 1$ identity closes the Vol~I
$\leftrightarrow$ Vol~III cross-volume consistency check for $m_8$
through the shadow tower.

The pattern extends as far as the recurrence is run; no new
mathematical phenomenon enters between weight $5$ and weight $11$
beyond the increasing multiplicity of the Zamolodchikov
$\Lambda$-channel pole (Riccati-propagated, not weight-by-weight
Kac-module). The next qualitatively new phenomenon arises in the
motivic lift at $W_3$, weight $6$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:s6-w3-mot}), which is the first appearance
of a $\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(3)^{2}$ contribution outside the
rational field $\mathbb{Q}(c)$. This establishes a sharp
separation: Virasoro is motivic-rational at every weight through
$r = 11$; the non-rational motivic content lives in higher-rank
$\mathcal{W}$-algebras.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Shadow tower as chain-level chiral Hochschild}
\label{sec:shadow-chirhoch-bridge}
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\providecommand{\ChirHoch}{\mathrm{ChirHoch}}
\providecommand{\Vir}{\mathrm{Vir}}
\providecommand{\Transp}{\mathrm{Transp}}
\providecommand{\bG}{\mathsf G}
\providecommand{\bL}{\mathsf L}
\providecommand{\bCc}{\mathsf C}
\providecommand{\bM}{\mathsf M}
\providecommand{\bB}{\mathbf B}
\providecommand{\ChirHochSh}{\ChirHoch_{\mathrm{sh}}}

The shadow coefficient $S_r(\cA) = \delta^{(r)}(1,\ldots,1)$ of
Definition~\ref{def:shadow-transport-operator} is the
$\Sym^r$-coinvariant residue of the ordered bar coproduct at the
universal $\Theta_\cA$ insertion. This is a shadow-complex invariant,
not an ambient curve-level chiral Hochschild class. Write
$\ChirHochSh^\bullet(\cA)$ for the scalar ordered cyclic-bar complex
obtained before descent to the curve-level complex
$\ChirHoch_X^\bullet(\cA)$ used in
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait}. The comparison
map
\[
 \rho_X\colon \ChirHochSh^r(\cA)\longrightarrow\ChirHoch_X^r(\cA)
\]
forgets the Arnold representative and descends to the ambient curve.
For the standard landscape covered by Theorem~H, $\rho_X$ kills the
shadow representatives in degrees $r>2$. Thus the identities below
live in the ordered shadow/Gel'fand--Fuks lane; they are compatible
with, and distinct from, curve-level Hochschild concentration in
degrees $\{0,1,2\}$.

\begin{definition}[\label{def:universal-arnold-cycle}Universal Arnold
class and cyclic-bar shadow pairing]
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
For $r\ge 2$, the \emph{universal Arnold $r$-class}
$\omega_r^{\mathrm{univ}}$ is the $\Sym^r$-symmetrised iterated
$d\log$-form
\[
 \omega_r^{\mathrm{univ}}
 \;=\;
 \frac{1}{r!}\sum_{\sigma\in\Sym_r}\,
 \mathrm{sgn}(\sigma)\,
 \eta_{\sigma(1)\sigma(2)}\wedge
 \eta_{\sigma(2)\sigma(3)}\wedge\cdots\wedge
 \eta_{\sigma(r-1)\sigma(r)}
\]
on $\mathrm{Conf}_r(X)$ with $\eta_{ij}=d\log(z_i-z_j)$. It is a
closed Arnold cohomology class of degree $r-1$; the Arnold three-term
relation
\[
 \eta_{ij}\wedge\eta_{jk}
 +\eta_{jk}\wedge\eta_{ki}
 +\eta_{ki}\wedge\eta_{ij}=0
\]
is the only relation used in the shadow extraction. The
\emph{cyclic-bar shadow pairing}
$\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle_{\mathrm{cyc}}\colon
\ChirHochSh^r(\cA)\otimes
H^{r-1}(\mathrm{Conf}_r(X))
\to\mathbb C$ evaluates a Hochschild $r$-cocycle on the vacuum tuple
$(1,\ldots,1)\in\cA^{\otimes r}$ against the Arnold class:
\[
 \langle\chi_r,\omega_r^{\mathrm{univ}}\rangle_{\mathrm{cyc}}
 \;:=\;\operatorname{Res}_{\omega_r^{\mathrm{univ}}}
 \chi_r^{\mathrm{chain}}(1,\ldots,1;z_1,\ldots,z_r).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[\label{thm:shadow-chirhoch-dictionary}Shadow tower
and ordered cyclic-bar Hochschild representatives]
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $\cA$ be a chiral algebra on a curve $X$ with
$\kappa(\cA)\ne 0$, and fix the cyclic-bar recursion of
Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-recurrence} (the master-equation
specialised to a single primary line). Let
$\chi_{r,\mathrm{sh}}^{\cA}\in\ChirHochSh^r(\cA)$ denote the ordered
shadow representative produced by cyclic-bar descent from the
universal obstruction $\Theta_\cA$. Then for every $r\ge 3$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
 \item \textup{(Pairing identity.)} The Arnold-cycle pairing recovers
 the shadow coefficient:
 \begin{equation}
 \label{eq:shadow-chirhoch-pairing}
 \langle[\chi_{r,\mathrm{sh}}^{\cA}],\omega_r^{\mathrm{univ}}\rangle_{\mathrm{cyc}}
 \;=\;S_r(\cA).
 \end{equation}
 \item \textup{(Virasoro calibration at $r=3$.)} For
 $\cA=\Vir_c$ and $r=3$, the ordered shadow representative in the
 Gel'fand--Fuks/Virasoro line has the form
 \begin{equation}
 \label{eq:chi3-virasoro-value}
 \pi_{T,T}\chi_{3,\mathrm{sh}}^{\Vir_c}
 \;=\;2\,W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}+\partial\xi_2^{\Vir},
 \qquad
 W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}
 \;=\;{:}T\partial T{:}-\tfrac14\partial^3T .
 \end{equation}
 The factor $2$ is $S_3(\Vir_c)$, the three-point Ward coefficient
 of the stress tensor. This is a shadow/GF representative; it is not
 a nonzero class in $\ChirHoch_X^3(\Vir_c)$.
 \item \textup{(Shadow-depth vanishing.)} On the archetype witnesses of
 Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait}:
 \begin{center}
 \renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
 \begin{tabular}{c|l|c|c}
 row & witness & $r_{\max}$ & $S_r$ pattern \\\hline
 $\bG$ & $\mathcal H_k$ & $2$ & $S_r=0$ for $r\ge 3$ \\
 $\bL$ & $V_k(\mathfrak g)$ & $3$ & $S_r=0$ for $r\ge 4$ \\
 $\bCc$ & $\beta\gamma_\lambda$ & $4$ & $S_r=0$ for $r\ge 5$ \\
 $\bM$ & $\Vir_c$ & $\infty$ & $S_r\ne 0$ generically \\
 $\bB$ & $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ & $\infty$ & $S_r\ne 0$ generically
 \end{tabular}
 \end{center}
 Thus the Arnold pairing vanishes on rows $\bG,\bL,\bCc$ for
 $r>r_{\max}$. This is a statement about the shadow representative;
 its curve-level image satisfies
 $\rho_X(\chi_{r,\mathrm{sh}}^{\cA})=0$ for $r>2$ throughout the
 Theorem~H landscape.
 \item \textup{(Object firewall.)} The representative
 $\chi_{r,\mathrm{sh}}^\cA$ lives in the ordered scalar cyclic-bar
 shadow complex $\ChirHochSh^\bullet(\cA)$. It is extracted from the
 ordered bar complex $B^{\mathrm{ord}}(\cA)$ and the MC element
 $\Theta_\cA$; it is not the algebra $\cA$, not the bar object
 $B(\cA)$ itself, not the cooperadic dual $\cA^i$, not the Verdier
 Koszul dual $\cA^!$, and not a curve-level derived-centre class.
 Its curve-level image is
 $\rho_X(\chi_{r,\mathrm{sh}}^\cA)\in
 Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)=\ChirHoch_X^\bullet(\cA,\cA)$;
 for the Theorem~H landscape this image vanishes in degrees $r>2$.
\end{enumerate}
