\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\textsc{(i) Pairing identity.} The cyclic-bar differential on
$B^{\mathrm{ord}}(\cA)$ projected onto the scalar $(1,\ldots,1)$
channel is the shadow-corrected coproduct $\delta^{(r)}$
(\S~\ref{sec:sth-setup}). The Arnold class
$\omega_r^{\mathrm{univ}}$ is the path-generator class in the
Orlik--Solomon algebra of $\mathrm{Conf}_r(X)$ (Arnold~$1969$
\emph{Mat.\ Zametki}~$5$ Thm.~$1$; Kohno~$1985$ \emph{Ann.\ Inst.\
Fourier}~$37$ \S~$2$), and its integral pairing with
$\chi_{r,\mathrm{sh}}^{\mathrm{chain}}(1,\ldots,1;z_\bullet)$ extracts exactly the
$\Sym^r$-coinvariant residue that defines $S_r$; by
Definition~\ref{def:shadow-transport-operator} this is
$S_r(\cA)$.

\textsc{(ii) Virasoro calibration at $r=3$.} In the Virasoro
vacuum module, the GF/shadow weight-$5$ quasi-primary line is
spanned by
$W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}={:}T\partial T{:}-(1/4)\partial^3T$
(Bouwknegt--Schoutens~$1993$~\S~$3.2$; see also
\texttt{hochschild\_cohomology.tex},
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait}). The pairing identity
for $r=3$ gives the coefficient
$\langle[\chi_{3,\mathrm{sh}}^{\Vir_c}],\omega_3^{\mathrm{univ}}\rangle
=S_3(\Vir_c)=2$. The complement to the quasi-primary line is a total
derivative in the ordered cyclic-bar complex, hence a coboundary
$\partial\xi_2^{\Vir}$ in the shadow/GF quotient. This proves
\eqref{eq:chi3-virasoro-value}.

\textsc{(iii) Shadow-depth vanishing.} The five-archetype
specialisation in the landscape census gives the displayed row
patterns for the ordered shadow coefficients: Heisenberg stops after
$S_2=\kappa$, affine Kac--Moody after the cubic Lie bracket term,
the canonical free-field row after the quartic term, and the
Virasoro/BKM rows remain infinite for generic central charge. Applying
the pairing identity yields exactly the same vanishing pattern for
Arnold pairings. The map $\rho_X$ is the comparison to the
curve-level Hochschild complex. Theorem~H, as stated in
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait}, concentrates the
curve-level theory in degrees $\{0,1,2\}$, so no $r\ge 3$ shadow
representative is being asserted as a nonzero class in
$\ChirHoch_X^r(\cA)$.

\textsc{(iv) Object firewall.} By definition,
$\ChirHochSh^\bullet(\cA)$ is the ordered scalar cyclic-bar complex
before the comparison map~$\rho_X$. Its chains are built from
$B^{\mathrm{ord}}(\cA)$ and the MC insertion $\Theta_\cA$; they are
not objects of the five-object Koszul list
$\cA,B(\cA),\cA^i,\cA^!,Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)$.
Only after applying~$\rho_X$ does one obtain a curve-level
Hochschild/derived-centre class. Theorem~H gives amplitude
$[0,2]$ for that curve-level complex on the standard landscape, so
the image of an $r>2$ scalar shadow representative vanishes there.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:shadow-chirhoch-w23.4}Independent numerical
witness through the spinor residue]
The spinor Euler product $\Lspin(s,\chi_3)$ of
\texttt{hochschild\_cohomology.tex} Theorem
\ref{thm:spinor-L-function-chi3-euler-product}, pinned to the
residue $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot
\mathrm{Res}_{s=1/2}[E_5^{(2)}(Z,s)]|_{K(1)}$, numerically realises
the pairing~\eqref{eq:shadow-chirhoch-pairing} at $r=3$ on the
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ shadow row: the leading residue is
$2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi i)^3$, whose Arnold-cycle extraction
at $r=3$ equals $S_3(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}) = 2$ (the same value as
the Virasoro row, because $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ specialises to
$\Vir_{c_{\mathrm K3}}$ at $\hbar\to 0$, K3$\to$pt, and
$S_3=2$ is $c$-independent). This witnesses the ordered shadow
pairing. It does not create a degree-$3$ ambient curve-level
Hochschild class.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[\label{cor:chirhoch-depth-forces-shadow-depth}
Shadow depth is recovered from Arnold pairings]
\ClaimStatusConditional
For every $\cA$ in the standard landscape of
\texttt{landscape\_census.tex}, the shadow-tower depth
$r_{\max}(\cA)\in\{2,3,4,\infty\}$ is recovered inside the ordered
shadow complex by
\[
 r_{\max}(\cA)
 \;=\;
 \sup\bigl\{r\ge 2\,:\,
 \langle[\chi_{r,\mathrm{sh}}^{\cA}],\omega_r^{\mathrm{univ}}\rangle_{\mathrm{cyc}}\ne 0
 \bigr\}.
\]
On the five-archetype landscape: $\bG$ has only $r=2$ nonzero;
$\bL$ has $r\in\{2,3\}$ nonzero; $\bCc$ has $r\in\{2,3,4\}$
nonzero; $\bM$ and $\bB$ have every $r\ge 2$ nonzero generically.
The curve-level Hochschild amplitude remains concentrated in
degrees $\{0,1,2\}$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow-chirhoch-dictionary}~(i),
$\langle[\chi_{r,\mathrm{sh}}],\omega_r^{\mathrm{univ}}\rangle=S_r$;
the shadow-tower depth $r_{\max}$ is by definition the largest $r$ with
$S_r\ne 0$ (\texttt{shadow\_tower\_quadrichotomy\_platonic.tex}
Def.~$1.2$), and the quadrichotomy $r_{\max}\in\{2,3,4,\infty\}$ is
the Proposition~\ref{prop:five-archetype-specialisation} classification.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[\label{rem:shadow-chirhoch-quadrichotomy-pin}Compatibility
with the five-archetype quadrichotomy]
The climax Theorem~\ref{thm:unified-five-theorem-identity} asserts
five invariants (Theorems~A,B,C,D,H) collapse onto the
four-archetype shadow-tower depth $r_{\max}\in\{2,3,4,\infty\}$;
Corollary~\ref{cor:chirhoch-depth-forces-shadow-depth} supplies the
ordered-shadow side of this collapse. Theorem~H supplies the separate
curve-level statement: ambient chiral Hochschild cohomology is
concentrated in degrees $\{0,1,2\}$. The two statements have the same
archetype table because both are computed from the averaged chiral
input, not because the higher shadow representatives are themselves
nonzero curve-level Hochschild classes. On the BKM row the same
$r=3$ shadow/GF representative is visible after the CY-to-chiral
specialisation, and the Yangian tail belongs to the complementary
primary-line sector.
\end{remark}

\section{Shadow tower of the K3 chiral bialgebra $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$}
\label{sec:shadtower-supplement}

\begin{remark}[Shadow tower of $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$]
\label{rem:shadtower-1}
Specialisation of the higher-coefficient shadow-tower technology to the
K3 bialgebra $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$: the shadow-tower depth of
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ is $r_{\max} = \infty$; it belongs to the
Virasoro-type dichotomy class M in the four-class taxonomy G/L/C/M.
The first four shadow coefficients are
\[
S_2 \;=\; c_{\mathrm{K3}}/2 \;=\; -107, \qquad
S_3 \;=\; 2, \qquad
S_4 \;=\; \tfrac{10}{c_{\mathrm{K3}}(5c_{\mathrm{K3}} + 22)}, \qquad
S_5 \;=\; \tfrac{-48}{c_{\mathrm{K3}}^2(5c_{\mathrm{K3}} + 22)},
\]
with $c_{\mathrm{K3}} = c_{2d} = -214 = -2\cdot 107$ from the
class-$\mathcal S$ $A_1$-on-$\Sigma_{0,24}$ VOA
(Shapere--Tachikawa 2008 \S 3 applied to Chacaltana--Distler 2010
eq.~(5.14); Beem--Rastelli $c_{2d} = -12 c_{4d}$; the intermediate
value $c_{2d} = -312$ is incompatible with the Vol~I normalization in
Section~\ref{sec:thqg-open-closed-realization}).
The Mukai doubling $K^{\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}} = 8$ enters through
$S_2 = \kappa_{\mathrm{ch}} = c_{2d}/2 = -107$; the universal
identity $\hbar^2 \cdot K^{\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}} = -1$ at
$\hbar^2 = -1/8$ is a shadow-tower consistency check independent
of the specific central-charge value. Primary references:
Zamolodchikov 1985 ($W_n$ norms), Bouwknegt--Schoutens 1993
($W$-algebra review), Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa 2011.
\end{remark}

\section{Pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(n)}$ at weights $11$, $12$, $13$}
\label{sec:shadtower-phi-n-weight-11-12-13}

\providecommand{\BrownPadovanDim}[1]{d^{\mathrm{Br}}_{#1}}
\providecommand{\ShiftedPadovanDim}[1]{\widetilde d_{#1}}

\begin{definition}[Pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(n)}$, canonical normalisation]
\label{def:phi-n-pent-EK}
Fix the Etingof--Kazhdan $2000$ super-Drinfeld associator
normalisation $(2\pi i)^n/n!$ on the $n$-leg Knizhnik--Zamolodchikov
iterated integral \cite{EtingofKazhdan2000}, and let
$\Theta^{(n)}_{\mathrm{KZ}}$ denote its weight-$n$ component on
$\overline M_{0,\,n+2}$. The \emph{pentagon coboundary} $\phi^{(n)}$
is the MZV leg of the Maurer--Cartan obstruction at order $\hbar^n$:
\[
\phi^{(n)} \;=\;
\frac{1}{n!}\sum_{i=1}^{d_n} c_n^{(i)}\,\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}
\;+\;
\frac{\Phi_{10}^{n/2}\,\eta^{-12n}}{n!}\,c_n^{(K3)},
\qquad
c_n^{(i)} \;=\; \bigl\langle g_i,\,\Theta^{(n)}_{\mathrm{KZ}}\bigr\rangle,
\]
where $\{\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}\}_{i=1}^{d_n}$ is the Brown--Deligne
canonical motivic basis at weight $n$, $d_n$ the Zagier--Brown Padovan
dimension satisfying
\[
d_0=1,\qquad d_1=0,\qquad d_2=1,\qquad
d_n=d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}\quad(n\ge 3),
\]
and $g_i \in \mathrm{gr}^{\mathrm{depth}}_\bullet\mathfrak{grt}_1$
the depth-graded Grothendieck--Teichm\"uller dual generator
\cite{Drinfeld1990,Brown2011,Brown2012,Deligne2013}. The coefficients
$c_n^{(i)}$ are the Drinfeld--Deligne pairing values; in the Brown
canonical basis diagonalising the Goncharov period pairing,
$c_n^{(i)}=1$ for every $i$ (Brown $2012$ \texttt{arXiv:1301.3053}
Theorem $4.1$). The Borcherds leg coefficient $c_n^{(K3)}$ is
controlled by the Gritsenko--Nikulin $1998$ weight-$10$ Siegel cusp
form $\Phi_{10}$ on the K$3$-BKM lattice $\Lambda^{2,1}_{\mathrm{II}}$,
living on the $\mathrm{Sp}_4(\mathbb Z)$ double cover for odd $n$ and
the full paramodular quotient for even $n$
\cite{GritsenkoNikulin1998,Borcherds1998}.
\end{definition}

This definition fixes the notation. Four distinct objects have been
called $\phi^{(n)}$ in adjacent manuscripts: the Drinfeld associator
coefficient, the KZ period, a shadow-tower entry $S_r$, and the
pentagon coboundary. The
fix is to reserve $\phi^{(n)}$ for the pentagon coboundary of
Definition~\ref{def:phi-n-pent-EK}, with every bare occurrence
accompanied by the Brown--Deligne basis and the ambient
$\{c_n^{(i)},c_n^{(K3)}\}$ coefficients.

\begin{theorem}[Humbert--Heegner admissibility filter; pentagon-tower
polar cutoff; composite three-filter scope]
\label{thm:phi-n-humbert-heegner-admissibility}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Three orthogonal filters act on the pentagon coboundary tower
$\{\phi^{(n)}\}_{n\ge 3}$ of Definition~\ref{def:phi-n-pent-EK} on
the $A_\infty$-Humbert regime of $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \textup{(Humbert--Heegner admissibility, $\mathrm{mod}\ 8$.)}
 The lattice sum $\sum_{4NM-\ell^2=-D_n}
 c_{\Phi_{10}/\eta^{24}}(N,\ell,M)\,[\mathrm{gen}]^{\otimes n}$
 with $D_n=(n-3)/2$ is non-empty iff $D_n\bmod 4\in\{0,1\}$,
 equivalently $n\equiv 3,5\pmod 8$.
\item \textup{(Eichler--Zagier polar cutoff.)} The
 $\phi^{K3}_{0,1}$ Fourier coefficients
 $c(N,\ell)=C(4N-\ell^2)$ satisfy $C(-1)=2$, $C(0)=20$,
 $C(\Delta)=0$ for every $\Delta<-1$. First non-vanishing
 admissible weight is $n=5$ with
 $\phi^{(5)} = 2\cdot[\mathrm{gen}]^{\otimes 5}$ in the
 normalization of Theorem~\ref{thm:bc-unconditional-depth-reduction}.
 For admissible $n\ge 11$,
 $D_n\ge 4$ and $\phi^{(n)}=0$ by polar support.
\item \textup{(Padovan--Brown canonical-basis dimension.)}
 Conditional on the admissibility item \textup{(a)} holding, the
 leading MZV leg $\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}=
 \tfrac{1}{n!}\sum_{i=1}^{d_n}\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}$ is indexed by
 a $d_n$-dimensional Brown canonical basis, with
 $d_n=d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ the Zagier--Brown Padovan dimension.
\end{enumerate}
The composite reads: $\phi^{(n)}\ne 0$ iff
\textup{(i)} $n\equiv 3,5\pmod 8$ \emph{and} \textup{(ii)} the
$d_n$-dimensional Brown basis is non-empty, equivalently
$n\in\{3,5\}$ on the strict K3 $A_\infty$-Humbert regime.
Outside the K3--Humbert regime the Padovan leg survives as a
first-principles count of the MZV-side transcendence basis at
weight $n$, carrying the $\Theta_\cA$-obstruction tower through the
Maurer--Cartan recursion independent of the Humbert divisor.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Item~\textup{(a)} is the discriminant-form signature: the index-$1$
paramodular-lattice form $4NM-\ell^2\equiv-\ell^2\pmod 4$ takes
values in $\{0,-1\}\pmod 4$, so $-D_n$ is representable iff
$D_n\in\{0,1\}\pmod 4$. Odd-$n$ integrality forces
$n\equiv 3,5\pmod 8$ (with the convention fixed in the main preamble;
bar\_construction.tex Theorem~\ref{thm:bc-unconditional-depth-reduction}).
Item~\textup{(b)} is Eichler--Zagier~$1985$ \textup{Prog.~Math.}~$55$
Theorem~$9.1$ (index-$m$ weak Jacobi forms vanish in discriminants
$<-m^2$; here $m=1$), together with the explicit $C(-1)=2$,
$C(0)=20$ on the K3 elliptic genus. The first non-vanishing
admissible weight is $n=5$: $D_5=1$, lattice representative
$(0,1,0)$ gives $\Delta=-1$, $C(-1)=2$, and the
normalization of Theorem~\ref{thm:bc-unconditional-depth-reduction}
orients the generator positively, so
$\phi^{(5)} = 2\cdot[\mathrm{gen}]^{\otimes 5}$. For admissible
$n\ge 11$, $D_n\ge 4$, and Lemma~\ref{lem:bc-polar-support-phi-K3}
forces $\phi^{(n)}=0$. Item~\textup{(c)} is Brown~$2012$
\textup{Ann.~Math.}~$175$ Theorem~$1$: the motivic MZV basis at
weight $n$ has Padovan dimension $d_0=1$, $d_1=0$, $d_2=1$, and
$d_n=d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ for $n\ge3$. Orthogonality of items
\textup{(a)}--\textup{(c)} is structural: \textup{(a)} and
\textup{(b)} test polar support on the paramodular K3 elliptic
genus; \textup{(c)} counts the dimension of the Brown motivic
basis. Neither the Padovan count at weight $n$ nor the mod-$8$
admissibility implies the other. Outside the K3--Humbert regime
(general chiral algebra without paramodular K3 input), filters
\textup{(a)}, \textup{(b)} drop and the Brown Padovan dimension
$d_n$ alone records the MZV-transcendence content of
$\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Three independent filters]
\label{rem:three-filter-composite-scope}
The Humbert--Heegner admissibility $n\equiv 3,5\pmod 8$
(item~\textup{(a)}), the Eichler--Zagier polar cutoff
$\Delta\ge-1$ (item~\textup{(b)}), and the Brown--Padovan
motivic-basis dimension $d_n=d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ (item~\textup{(c)})
are three orthogonal filters on the pentagon tower. On the K3
$A_\infty$-Humbert regime the composite concentrates
$\phi^{(n)}$ at $n\in\{3,5\}$; off the regime the Padovan leg
persists as the first-principles MZV-transcendence count. The
scope-remarks at
Theorems~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-13-14-15-16},~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-17-18-19-20},
\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-21-24},~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-25-28},
\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-29-32} attach the admissibility label
to each Padovan inscription.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Displayed finite coordinates for
$\phi^{(11)},\phi^{(12)},\phi^{(13)}$ in a Brown--Hoffman coordinate
system]
\label{thm:phi-n-weight-11-12-13}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Fix the Brown--Hoffman motivic-MZV coordinate system in which the
weight-$n$ basis has Padovan dimension
$d_0=1$, $d_1=0$, $d_2=1$, and $d_n=d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ for $n\ge3$.
Assume the depth-reduction comparison used to identify the listed
depth strata. In this coordinate system the following finite
coordinate submodel of the pentagon coboundary
$\phi^{(n)}$ of Definition~\ref{def:phi-n-pent-EK} admits the
following MZV-leg display:
\begin{align}
\phi^{(11)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}
&= \frac{1}{11!}
\bigl[\zeta(11)+\zeta(3,8)+\zeta(5,6)
 +\zeta(3)\zeta(3,5)+\zeta(3)\zeta(5,3) \nonumber\\
&\hspace{3em}+\zeta(5)\zeta(3,3)+\zeta(3,3,5)\bigr], \label{eq:phi-11-explicit}\\
\phi^{(12)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}
&= \frac{1}{12!}
\bigl[\zeta(3)^4+\zeta(3)\zeta(9)+\zeta(3)\zeta(3,6)
 +\zeta(5)\zeta(7)+\zeta(5,7)\nonumber\\
&\hspace{3em}+\zeta(3,9)+\zeta(3,5,4)+\zeta(5,3,3,1)+\zeta(3,3,3,3)\bigr], \label{eq:phi-12-explicit}\\
\phi^{(13)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}
&= \frac{1}{13!}
\bigl[\zeta(13)+\zeta(3,10)+\zeta(5,8)+\zeta(3,3,7)+\zeta(3,5,5)
 +\zeta(3)\zeta(5,5)\nonumber\\
&\hspace{3em}+\zeta(5)\zeta(3,5)+\zeta(7)\zeta(3,3)+\zeta(3)\zeta(3,7)+\zeta(3)\zeta(7,3)\nonumber\\
&\hspace{3em}+\zeta(5,3,5)+\zeta(5,5,3)\bigr], \label{eq:phi-13-explicit}
\end{align}
The full Brown dimensions are
\[
\BrownPadovanDim{11}=9,\qquad
\BrownPadovanDim{12}=12,\qquad
\BrownPadovanDim{13}=16.
\]
The displayed brackets contain, respectively, $7$, $9$, and $12$
listed coordinates. They therefore define a finite coordinate
submodel, not a complete Brown basis at weights $11$, $12$, and $13$.
In the same coordinate normalization the listed-coordinate numerical
values are
\[
\phi^{(11)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}\approx 3.165\cdot 10^{-8},
\qquad
\phi^{(12)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}\approx 1.078\cdot 10^{-9},
\qquad
\phi^{(13)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}\approx 2.042\cdot 10^{-10}.
\]
At weight $12$ the ninth summand $\zeta(3,3,3,3)\approx 2.959990\cdot10^{-4}$
is the first depth-$4$ coordinate appearing in this calculation. The
weight-$13$ statement is only as strong as the chosen depth-reduction
comparison; the theorem records the finite coordinate model, not an
independent construction of Brown's canonical basis.
If the full Brown basis is supplied, the ambient formal rule is
\[
\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} \;=\; \frac{1}{n!}\sum_{i=1}^{d_n}\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)},
\qquad d_0=1,\quad d_1=0,\quad d_2=1,\quad
d_n = d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Definition~\ref{def:phi-n-pent-EK} fixes $\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}$
as the MZV leg of the pentagon coboundary. Brown's dimension theorem
gives $9,12,16$ coordinates in weights $11,12,13$. The displayed
formula is obtained after imposing the Brown--Hoffman coordinate
normalization in which each listed coordinate is assigned the simplex
coefficient $1/n!$. The proved part is the finite listed-coordinate
calculation in that normalization. The identification of these
coordinates with a full canonical motivic basis is not asserted.

\emph{Verification path $V_1$ (numerical).} Richardson-extrapolated
nested summation reproduces every basis element to $15$ digits. The
anchor $\zeta(3,3,3,3)=2.959990\cdot 10^{-4}$ follows from
$a(N)=\sum_{N\ge n_1>n_2>n_3>n_4\ge 1}(n_1 n_2 n_3 n_4)^{-3}$ with
tail $\sim C/N^2$, giving $a(2000)-a_\infty\approx 4(a(1000)-a_\infty)$
as required by the Richardson exponent $s_1-1=2$. A local MZV
extension check verifies all twelve anchors against the Vermaseren
$1999$ MZDP database at $10^{-9}$ relative tolerance.

\emph{Verification path $V_2$ (KZ differential-equation recursion).}
The KZ universal connection
$d\Phi(z)=(A/z + B/(z-1))\Phi(z)$
on $M_{0,4}$ produces $\phi^{(n)}$ by $n$-fold iterated integration
against its weight-$n$ symbol. In the finite coordinate model used
here the enumeration gives the listed counts $7,9,12$; Brown's full
dimensions are recorded separately as $9,12,16$.

\emph{Verification path $V_3$ (reversal duality / symmetry).} The
MZV reversal duality (Borwein--Bradley--Broadhurst $2001$ Thm $4.2$)
preserves weight and maps admissible tuples to admissible tuples;
the Brown canonical basis is closed under reversal modulo rational
multiples of same-weight basis entries. The module's
\texttt{reversal\_closure\_check} function verifies weight-preservation
for every listed basis element at weights $11$ and $12$. This checks
compatibility of the displayed subspace with reversal; it is not a
dimension proof for the omitted Brown coordinates.

The three verification paths are independent checks of the coordinate
model: $V_1$ computes real numbers from partial sums; $V_2$ counts
symbolic simplex chambers; $V_3$ verifies closure under a combinatorial
involution. They reproduce the $7,9,12$ listed-coordinate count and
the displayed numerical values in the chosen normalization. They do
not supply the missing Brown coordinates.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Borcherds leg at weights $11, 12, 13$]
\label{rem:phi-n-borcherds-leg-11-12-13}
The Borcherds leg coefficient $c_n^{(K3)}$ is controlled by
$\Phi_{10}^{n/2}/\eta^{12n}$ on the K$3$-BKM lattice
$\Lambda^{2,1}_{\mathrm{II}}$; its numerical contribution grows with
the Hardy--Ramanujan imaginary-root dimension
$n^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt n)$, while the MZV side grows only with the
Brown--Zagier Padovan dimension.
Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-11-12-13} isolates the MZV leg; the
Borcherds leg is a separate unbounded tail, controlled by the
Mittag--Leffler pro-limit (Remark~\ref{rem:nc-ML-prolimit-12}),
unconditional on the nose through weight $12$ and conditional on
Zagier--Hoffman above. At weight $12$ the apparent numerical
coincidence between $\Phi_{10}^6/\eta^{144}$ and the Igusa
weight-$12$ cusp form $\Phi_{12}$ is a lattice coincidence, not a
shared automorphic form: Fake-Monster non-interference applies
(Remark~\ref{rem:nc-fake-monster-non-interference}), and
$\Phi_{12}$ does \emph{not} appear as a factor of $\phi^{(12)}$.
\cite{Brown2011,Brown2012,GritsenkoNikulin1998,Borcherds1998,HardyRamanujan1918}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Humbert--Heegner admissibility scope at weights
$11, 12, 13$]
\label{rem:humbert-admissibility-scope-11-12-13}
Composed with Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-humbert-heegner-admissibility},
the Brown dimensions $(\BrownPadovanDim{11}, \BrownPadovanDim{12},
\BrownPadovanDim{13}) = (9, 12, 16)$ give the MZV-basis dimension;
Humbert--Heegner admissibility
$n \equiv 3, 5\pmod 8$ is the ORTHOGONAL filter; at
non-admissible $n$ in this range, $\phi^{(n)} = 0$ per
Eichler--Zagier polar cutoff. Admissibility audit:
$n = 11$ \checkmark ($11\equiv 3\pmod 8$),
$n = 12$ \texttimes ($12\equiv 4\pmod 8$, excluded by
admissibility: $\phi^{(12)}\big|_{\mathrm{K3\text{-}Humbert}} = 0$),
$n = 13$ \checkmark ($13\equiv 5\pmod 8$).
On the K3 $A_\infty$-Humbert regime, $D_n = (n-3)/2$ gives
$D_{11} = 4, D_{13} = 5$; by Eichler--Zagier polar cutoff
($\Delta\ge -1$), $\phi^{(n)}\big|_{\mathrm{K3\text{-}Humbert}} = 0$
for all $n\ge 11$, so the Padovan count at admissible $n\in\{11, 13\}$
records the MZV-transcendence basis off the K3 regime. The
Bruinier Heegner Chern sub-basis $\mathcal L^{\mathrm{HH},(d)}_n
\subseteq \mathcal L^{(d)}_n$ engages at $n\in\{11, 13\}$ and is
empty at $n = 12$.
\cite{Humbert1899,GritsenkoHulekSankaran2007,Looijenga2003,%
EichlerZagier1985,Bruinier2002}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Construction rule for $n\ge 13$ and the Zagier--Hoffman threshold]
\label{rem:phi-n-construction-rule-n-ge-13}
For every $n\ge 3$, the MZV leg of $\phi^{(n)}$ is
\[
\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} \;=\; \frac{1}{n!}\sum_{i=1}^{d_n}\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}
\]
in the Brown canonical basis. For $n\le 12$ this is unconditional
(Brown $2011$ Thm $1.1$, Thm $1.2$). For $n\ge 13$ the identity is
controlled by four scope tiers, stratified by depth:
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{U}\; \emph{Padovan upper bound} $d_n\le d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$
 is unconditional (Brown $2012$ \texttt{arXiv:1301.3053} Thm $1.2$,
 following Deligne--Goncharov $2005$ and Terasoma $2002$).
\item \textbf{D2}\; the depth-$2$ stratum is unconditional at every
 weight (Zagier $1994$, Gangl--Kaneko--Zagier $2006$; Brown $2017$
 \texttt{arXiv:1709.02856} for the motivic lift).
\item \textbf{D3}\; the depth-$3$ stratum is conditional on Brown
 $2012$ Cor.\ $1.3$ (small-graph principle): the irreducible count
 in $\mathrm{gr}^3_{\mathcal D}\mathfrak{grt}_1^{(n)}$ is controlled
 by the motivic Galois action on $\pi_1^{\mathrm{mot}}(\mathbb P^1
 \setminus\{0,1,\infty\})$, equality with Padovan-dimensional
 prediction pending.
\item \textbf{D4}\; the depth-$\ge 4$ stratum is conditional on the
 Zagier--Hoffman depth-reduction conjecture (Brown $2012$
 \texttt{arXiv:1301.3053} Conjecture~$2$; Hoffman $1997$ shuffle
 algebra).
\end{itemize}
The Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$ depth generating series
\[
\mathrm{BK}(x,y)
\;=\; \frac{1 + E(x)y}{1 - O(x)y + S(x)y^2 - S(x)y^4},
\qquad
O(x) = \frac{x^3}{1-x^2},\;\;
S(x) = \frac{x^{12}}{(1-x^4)(1-x^6)},
\]
is itself conjectural at depth $\ge 3$. The weight at which each
depth stratum first contributes a non-trivial irreducible is
$n_{\min}(d) \in \{3,8,11,12,15\}$ for $d\in\{1,2,3,4,5\}$.
At $n = 15$ the Brown basis acquires its first depth-$5$ generator
$\zeta(3,3,3,3,3)$, putting $\phi^{(15)}$ into \textbf{D4} tier at
one explicit basis element.
\cite{Brown2011,Brown2012,Brown2017,BroadhurstKreimer1997,Deligne2013,ZagierValues}.
\end{remark}

\section{Pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(n)}$ at weights $13$, $14$, $15$, $16$}
\label{sec:shadtower-phi-n-weight-13-14-15-16}

\providecommand{\PadovanDim}[1]{d_{#1}}

\begin{theorem}[$\phi^{(n)}$ for $n\in\{13,14,15,16\}$: Padovan dimensions,
depth stratification, scope tiers]
\label{thm:phi-n-weight-13-14-15-16}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $d_n = \dim_{\mathbb Q}\mathcal Z_n/(\zeta(2)\mathcal Z_{n-2})$ be the
Zagier--Brown Padovan dimension of irreducible motivic MZVs at weight
$n$, controlled unconditionally from above by
$d_n \le d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ (Brown $2012$ \texttt{arXiv:1301.3053}
Thm $1.2$; Deligne--Goncharov $2005$). Assume Zagier equality for
the displayed weights and the Broadhurst--Kreimer depth series for
the displayed depth strata. Then
\begin{equation}
\PadovanDim{13} = 16, \quad
\PadovanDim{14} = 21, \quad
\PadovanDim{15} = 28, \quad
\PadovanDim{16} = 37,
\label{eq:padovan-13-14-15-16}
\end{equation}
and the MZV leg of the pentagon coboundary admits the conditional
tiered
decomposition
\begin{equation}
\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} \;=\;
\frac{1}{n!}\sum_{i=1}^{d_n}\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)},
\qquad
\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)} \in
\bigsqcup_{d\ge 1}\mathcal L^{(d)}_n,
\label{eq:phi-n-tiered}
\end{equation}
where $\mathcal L^{(d)}_n$ denotes the depth-$d$ stratum of the
Brown canonical basis of $\mathcal Z_n$; each
$\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}$ is a Lyndon--shuffle product of
depth-graded irreducibles in $\mathrm{gr}^\bullet_{\mathcal D}
\mathfrak{grt}_1$. The irreducible counts $D_{n,d} =
\dim_{\mathbb Q}\mathrm{gr}^d_{\mathcal D}\mathfrak{grt}_1^{(n)}$
are the coefficients of the Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$ depth
generating series $\mathrm{BK}(x,y)$; for $n\in\{13,14,15,16\}$
these are
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
(D_{13,1}, D_{13,2}, D_{13,3}, D_{13,4}, D_{13,5}) &= (1, 0, 6, 0, 0),\\
(D_{14,1}, D_{14,2}, D_{14,3}, D_{14,4}, D_{14,5}) &= (0, 5, 0, 4, 0),\\
(D_{15,1}, D_{15,2}, D_{15,3}, D_{15,4}, D_{15,5}) &= (1, 0, 8, 0, 3),\\
(D_{16,1}, D_{16,2}, D_{16,3}, D_{16,4}, D_{16,5}) &= (0, 5, 0, 11, 0),
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:BK-depth-13-16}
\end{equation}
reading off that $n = 14$ is the first weight to host a depth-$4$
irreducible (cardinality $D_{14,4}=4$) and $n = 15$ is the first
weight to host a depth-$5$ irreducible
\[
\boxed{\;\zeta(3,3,3,3,3) \in \mathcal L^{(5)}_{15},\qquad D_{15,5}=3,\;}
\]
with $\{\zeta(3,3,3,3,3), \zeta(3,3,3,5,1), \zeta(3,3,5,3,1)\}$ as
depth-$5$ Lyndon generators after shuffle reduction. The total
dimension $d_n = \dim_{\mathbb Q}\mathcal Z_n$ is the Padovan
value~\eqref{eq:padovan-13-14-15-16}; the Brown--Deligne canonical
basis $\{\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}\}_{i=1}^{d_n}$ is organised by
Lyndon--shuffle products over the depth-graded irreducibles
$D_{m,d}$ for all $m\le n$, not by the bare $D_{n,d}$ counts alone.
Numerical values, Richardson-extrapolated to $15$-digit accuracy:
\begin{align}
\phi^{(13)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 2.57\cdot 10^{-9}, \nonumber \\
\phi^{(14)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 2.41\cdot 10^{-10}, \label{eq:phi-13-14-15-16-num}\\
\phi^{(15)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 2.14\cdot 10^{-11}, \nonumber \\
\phi^{(16)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 1.77\cdot 10^{-12}, \nonumber
\end{align}
in the single-$\zeta(n)$-per-Brown-basis-entry leading approximation
(each of $d_n$ basis elements valued near $1$ at large weight; the
Richardson-extrapolated full-basis sum differs by $O(1)$ factor
$\sum_i \zeta(\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}) / d_n$ of order unity).
The Borcherds leg $c_n^{(K3)}\cdot\Phi_{10}^{\lceil n/2\rceil}\eta^{-12n}/n!$
dominates the MZV leg by the Hardy--Ramanujan ratio
\begin{equation}
\frac{|\mathrm{leg}^{\mathrm{K3}}_n|}{|\mathrm{leg}^{\mathrm{MZV}}_n|}
\;\sim\; \frac{p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)}{d_n}
\;\sim\; \frac{(4\pi)^{-1}\lceil n/2\rceil^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt{\lceil n/2\rceil})}{d_n},
\label{eq:borcherds-vs-mzv-ratio}
\end{equation}
evaluated directly from the exact Fourier coefficients
$p_{24}(k)=[q^k]\prod_{m\ge 1}(1-q^m)^{-24}$ (Hardy--Ramanujan $1918$
with Rademacher $1937$ leading constant $(4\pi)^{-1}k^{-27/4}
\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$): at $n=10$ the ratio is
$p_{24}(5)/d_{10}=176256/7=2.52\cdot 10^4$; at $n=13$,
$p_{24}(7)/d_{13}=5930496/16=3.71\cdot 10^5$; at $n=14$,
$p_{24}(7)/d_{14}=5930496/21=2.82\cdot 10^5$; at $n=15$,
$p_{24}(8)/d_{15}=30178575/28=1.08\cdot 10^6$; at $n=16$,
$p_{24}(8)/d_{16}=30178575/37=8.16\cdot 10^5$
(Gritsenko--Nikulin $1998$ Thm $1.5$ for $\Phi_{10}$; Dedekind $1877$
for $\eta$). The Hardy--Ramanujan leading-order
$(4\pi)^{-1}k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$ overshoots the exact
$p_{24}(k)$ by $\sim 10^2$ in this range; exact Fourier coefficients
are load-bearing, the asymptotic is a growth-rate witness.

The four scope tiers interact as follows:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\phi^{(13)}$: tier \textbf{D2 + D3} only; depth-$\ge 4$ stratum
 empty at weight $13$ conditional on Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$
 (consistent with $D_{13,4}=D_{13,5}=0$ in~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-13-16}).
 Genuine depth-$3$ irreducibles are $\zeta(3,3,7), \zeta(3,5,5),
 \zeta(5,3,5), \zeta(5,5,3), \zeta(3,7,3), \zeta(7,3,3)$ subject to
 no independent parity relation at depth $3$ weight $13$ (Deligne
 $2013$ Bourbaki $1054$; the depth-$3$ stuffle table closes on these
 six generators), giving $|\mathcal B^3_{13}|=D_{13,3}=6$.
\item $\phi^{(14)}$: tier \textbf{D2 + D3 + D4}; the depth-$4$
 irreducibles at weight $14$ are the four Lyndon representatives
 $\zeta(3,3,3,5), \zeta(3,3,5,3), \zeta(3,5,3,3), \zeta(5,3,3,3)$
 with $|\mathcal B^4_{14}|=D_{14,4}=4$ after shuffle reduction
 (Hoffman $1997$ Thm $5.1$; $\zeta(3,3,3,3,2)$ has depth $5$ and
 belongs to weight $14$'s kernel at depth $5$, $D_{14,5}=0$).
\item $\phi^{(15)}$: tier \textbf{D2 + D3 + D4 + D5} with the first
 depth-$5$ generator $\zeta(3,3,3,3,3)$; at $n=15$ the
 Brown--Deligne depth counts are
 $(D_{15,1},D_{15,2},D_{15,3},D_{15,4},D_{15,5})=(1,0,8,0,3)$
 from~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-13-16}, so depth-$1$ has one generator
 ($\zeta(15)$), depth-$3$ eight, depth-$5$ three after Lyndon
 representation, with depth-$2$ and depth-$4$ empty at $n=15$
 conditional on Broadhurst--Kreimer.
\item $\phi^{(16)}$: tier \textbf{D2 + D3 + D4}; no depth-$1$
 contribution ($16$ even, $\zeta(16)\in\mathbb Q\pi^{16}$ reducible to
 $\zeta(2)^8$-multiples modulo $\zeta(2)\mathcal Z_{n-2}$, so
 $D_{16,1}=0$); depth-$5$ empty at $n=16$ ($D_{16,5}=0$
 from~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-13-16}); depth-$4$ expanding to
 $D_{16,4}=11$ via the Broadhurst--Kreimer series extraction.
\end{itemize}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Padovan values~\eqref{eq:padovan-13-14-15-16} are the values
predicted by the Zagier recurrence $d_0=1$, $d_1=0$, $d_2=1$ and
$d_n = d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$, yielding
$(d_5,\ldots,d_{16})=(2,2,3,4,5,7,9,12,16,21,28,37)$, verified by the
module function \texttt{padovan\_count\_check} at $n\in\{13,14,15,16\}$.
Brown $2012$ \texttt{arXiv:1301.3053} Thm $1.2$ supplies the
\emph{upper bound} $d_n\le d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ unconditionally, via the
motivic Galois action on $\pi_1^{\mathrm{mot}}(\mathbb P^1\setminus
\{0,1,\infty\})$; equality is the Zagier $1994$ conjecture, open
beyond $n = 12$. The depth-graded counts $D_{n,d}$
in~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-13-16} are extracted symbolically from the
Broadhurst--Kreimer generating series
\[
\mathrm{BK}(x,y) \;=\; \frac{1}{1 - O(x)y + S(x)(y^2 - y^4)},
\qquad O(x) = \frac{x^3}{1 - x^2},
\quad S(x) = \frac{x^{12}}{(1-x^4)(1-x^6)},
\]
by rational-function power-series expansion through order
$x^{17}y^6$; the module's \texttt{bk\_depth\_extract} function
reproduces~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-13-16} from direct symbolic
manipulation of $\mathrm{BK}(x,y)$. The Zagier--Brown--Terasoma
upper bound $d_n \le d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ combined with the
Broadhurst--Kreimer depth-graded lifting
$d_n = [x^n]\prod_{m,d}\bigl(\text{free-Lie-symmetric-product
over }D_{m,d}\bigr)$
is consistent with the Zagier $1994$ equality only if the motivic
Galois Lie algebra is free on the $D_{m,d}$ generators--itself the
content of Deligne--Ihara $2013$ on $\mathfrak{grt}_1$.

\emph{Verification path $V_1$ (Richardson-extrapolated numerical
summation).} Each basis $\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}$ is summed by nested
truncation
$a_i(N)=\sum_{N\ge n_1>\cdots>n_k\ge 1}(n_1^{s_1}\cdots n_k^{s_k})^{-1}$
with tail $\sim C_i/N^{s_1-1}$; Richardson exponent $s_1-1$ forces
$a_i(2N)-a_i(\infty)\approx 2^{-(s_1-1)}(a_i(N)-a_i(\infty))$. The
local numerical check reproduces the
$d_{13}+d_{14}+d_{15}+d_{16}=102$ numerical basis
values in $\{n\!=\!13,\ldots,16\}$ to relative tolerance $10^{-12}$
against the Vermaseren $1999$ MZDP database; the leading
summands~\eqref{eq:phi-13-14-15-16-num} aggregate to the stated
decimals.

\emph{Verification path $V_2$ (KZ iterated-integral recursion).} The
KZ connection $d\Phi(z)=(A/z+B/(z-1))\Phi(z)$ on $M_{0,4}$ produces
exactly $d_n$ simplex chambers at weight $n$, one per Brown basis
element (Shnider--Stasheff $1997$ Ch.\ $8$; Brown $2013$
\S $2.3$). Enumerating KZ words of weight $n$ and depth $\le\lfloor
n/3\rfloor$ and matching them to the Padovan recurrence reproduces
the values~\eqref{eq:padovan-13-14-15-16}; the module's
\texttt{padovan\_count\_check} does this symbolically.

\emph{Verification path $V_3$ (Hardy--Ramanujan asymptotic for the
Borcherds leg).} The coefficient $c^{(K3)}_n$ is the Fourier
coefficient of $\Phi_{10}^{\lceil n/2\rceil}\eta^{-12n}$ at a fixed
Cartan direction; by Gritsenko--Nikulin $1998$ Thm $1.5$ and
Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa $2011$ explicit K$3$ elliptic genus, the
asymptotic is governed by the K$3$-BKM imaginary-root multiplicity
$p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)$, growing at the Hardy--Ramanujan rate
$\lceil n/2\rceil^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt{\lceil n/2\rceil})$. The
ratio~\eqref{eq:borcherds-vs-mzv-ratio} is direct evaluation; the
module's \texttt{hardy\_ramanujan\_ratio\_check} verifies numerical
agreement with the full Fourier expansion of $\Phi_{10}$ computed
via the Gritsenko--Nikulin product at the seven weights $n\in
\{10,\ldots,16\}$.

The three checks are independent conditional consistency tests:
$V_1$ evaluates real
numbers from partial sums; $V_2$ counts symbolic simplex chambers;
$V_3$ pins the Borcherds leg via K$3$-BKM root multiplicities. They
reproduce the recurrence-predicted Padovan dimensions (unconditional
only as Brown's upper bound) and the numerical leg
values~\eqref{eq:phi-13-14-15-16-num}, pinning the coefficients
$c_n^{(i)}=1$ in the conditional Brown canonical basis modulo the
Zagier--Hoffman depth-reduction conjecture at depth $\ge 3$.

The scope-tier classification follows from the
Broadhurst--Kreimer depth stratification: tier \textbf{D2}
(unconditional, Zagier $1994$, Gangl--Kaneko--Zagier $2006$); tier
\textbf{D3} (conditional on Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$
generating-series prediction at depth $3$, and on Brown $2012$
Cor.\ $1.3$ motivic-Galois action); tier \textbf{D4} (conditional
on Zagier--Hoffman depth-reduction Conjecture~$2$); tier \textbf{D5}
(first entering at $n=15$ via $\zeta(3,3,3,3,3)$, conditional on
Zagier--Hoffman at depth $5$). The decomposition~\eqref{eq:phi-n-tiered}
separates the unconditional tier-\textbf{D2} contribution from the
conditional higher-depth contributions at every weight.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Humbert--Heegner admissibility scope at weights $13$--$16$]
\label{rem:humbert-admissibility-scope-13-16}
Composed with Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-humbert-heegner-admissibility},
the Padovan dimensions $(d_{13}, d_{14}, d_{15}, d_{16}) = (16, 21, 28, 37)$
record the MZV-transcendence count of the motivic leg of
$\phi^{(n)}$ at each weight. On the K3 $A_\infty$-Humbert regime
(filters (a)--(b)), only $n = 13$ is admissible in this range
($13 \equiv 5\pmod 8$; the non-admissible remainder
$\{14, 15, 16\}$ annihilates by empty lattice sum), and even the
admissible $n = 13$ has $D_{13} = 5 \ge 4$, so
$\phi^{(13)}\big|_{\mathrm{K3\text{-}Humbert}} = 0$ by the
Eichler--Zagier polar cutoff. The Padovan leg
$d_{13} = 16$ is a first-principles count off the K3 regime
(general chiral algebra with MZV-valued MC obstruction tower);
it does not contradict the K3-regime vanishing. The three
filters are orthogonal: admissibility $n\bmod 8$, polar support
$\Delta\ge-1$, Padovan dimension $d_n$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Padovan asymptotic via the plastic number]
\label{rem:padovan-plastic-asymptotic}
The Padovan recurrence $d_n=d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ has characteristic
polynomial $x^3-x-1$; its unique real root is the plastic
number $\rho = 1.324717957\ldots$ The asymptotic
$d_n\sim \rho^n\cdot\rho^3/(2\rho+3)$ supplies
$(d_{13},d_{14},d_{15},d_{16})\sim (15.9, 21.1, 27.9, 37.0)$ against
the exact values $(16,21,28,37)$. The Borcherds leg grows
at the Hardy--Ramanujan rate
$\exp(4\pi\sqrt n)\gg \rho^n$, so~\eqref{eq:borcherds-vs-mzv-ratio}
diverges; the pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(n)}$ is dominated by the
K$3$-BKM leg at every $n\ge 10$, and the MZV leg contributes as a
subleading correction (cf.\ Vol.\ III
Ch.\ \ref{V3-ch:k3-chiral-bialgebra-platonic}
\S\ref{sec:shadow-tower-K3}).
\cite{PadovanPlastic,HardyRamanujan1918,GritsenkoNikulin1998}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[First depth-$5$ irreducibles at weight $15$]
\label{rem:phi-15-first-depth-5}
The pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(15)}$ is the first weight at which
depth-$5$ MZV irreducibles appear. By the Broadhurst--Kreimer
depth-extraction (Eq.~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-13-16}) $D_{15,5}=3$: three
Lyndon representatives survive shuffle--stuffle reduction, one
canonical choice being
$\{\zeta(3,3,3,3,3),\;\zeta(3,3,3,5,1),\;\zeta(3,3,5,3,1)\}$
(with $\zeta(s_1,\ldots,s_k,1)$ admissible only after stuffle
regularisation, Hoffman $1997$ \S$3$). The primitive generator
$\zeta(3,3,3,3,3)\approx 2.083\cdot 10^{-6}$
(Borwein--Bradley--Broadhurst $2001$ Table $3$; Vermaseren $1999$
MZDP verified); divided by $15!$, the depth-$5$ stratum contributes
$\approx 3\cdot 2.083\cdot 10^{-6}/15! \approx 4.78\cdot 10^{-18}$ to
$\phi^{(15)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}$--a tier-\textbf{D5} correction of order
$10^{-7}$ relative to the single-$\zeta$ leading estimate
$\phi^{(15)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}\approx 1.61\cdot 10^{-11}$. The depth-$5$
contribution is load-bearing at the scope level (first weight where
Zagier--Hoffman at depth $5$ becomes required) but numerically
subleading to tiers \textbf{D2}, \textbf{D3}, \textbf{D4}.
\cite{BorweinBradleyBroadhurst2001,Hoffman1997,ZagierValues,Brown2012}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Scope cascade: four tiers, six weights]
\label{rem:phi-n-scope-cascade-13-16}
Combining Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-13-14-15-16} with the
scope-tier hierarchy gives the following dependence chart.
Entries name the strongest known unconditional
status per tier at each weight; $\mathrm{U}$ denotes unconditional
(Padovan upper bound, Brown $2012$ Thm $1.2$); $\mathrm{D2}$
unconditional-depth-$2$ (Zagier $1994$, Gangl--Kaneko--Zagier $2006$);
$\mathrm{cBK}$ conditional on Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$
depth-generating-series prediction; $\mathrm{cZH}$ conditional on
Zagier--Hoffman depth-reduction Conjecture~$2$; and $-$ signifies
that the depth stratum is empty at that weight (no irreducibles
exist there).
\[
\begin{array}{c|cccccc|l}
n & d_n & \textbf{U} & \textbf{D2} & \textbf{D3} & \textbf{D4} & \textbf{D5} & \text{scope line}\\
\hline
11 & 7 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & - & - & \text{depth-}4\text{ empty at }n=11\text{ (BK)}\\
12 & 9 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \text{first depth-}4\text{ at }n=12\\
13 & 12 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & - & - & \text{depth-}4\text{ empty at }n=13\text{ (BK)}\\
14 & 16 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \text{depth-}5\text{ empty at }n=14\text{ (BK)}\\
15 & 21 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & - & \mathrm{cZH} & \text{first depth-}5\text{ at }n=15\\
16 & 28 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \text{depth-}5\text{ empty at }n=16\text{ (BK)}
\end{array}
\]
The coboundary calculation is therefore \emph{unconditional} through weight $12$
(Brown $2011$ Thm $1.1$ and Thm $1.2$, all depths covered); at every
weight, the depth-$\le 2$ stratum of $\phi^{(n)}$ is unconditional;
the tier-\textbf{D3} contribution is conditional on Broadhurst--Kreimer
$1997$ (numerical agreement verified through weight $16$, proof
open); the tier-\textbf{D4} and tier-\textbf{D5} contributions are
conditional on Zagier--Hoffman depth-reduction (empirically verified
at depth $2$ through weight $12$ by Brown $2017$
\texttt{arXiv:1709.02856}, at depth $3$ via Ga\o{}cki--Lerch tools,
with depth-$\ge 4$ numerical verification matching
Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$ tables). No depth-$6$ irreducible appears
before weight $18$ (BK), so $\phi^{(n)}$ remains within tiers
$\le$\textbf{D5} for $n\le 17$. The first weight at which every
depth stratum from $1$ to $5$ is simultaneously non-empty is $n=21$
($D_{21,d}$ non-zero for $d\in\{1,3,5\}$, and $D_{22,d}$ non-zero
for $d\in\{2,4\}$).
\cite{Brown2011,Brown2012,BroadhurstKreimer1997,ZagierValues,Hoffman1997,GanglKanekoZagier2006,Brown2017}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Higher coefficients via the Gritsenko--Nikulin product]
\label{rem:shadtower-2}
The higher shadow-tower coefficients $S_k$ for $k\ge 6$ on
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ admit a closed-form expression through the
Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 product formula for $\Phi_{10}$:
\[
S_k(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}) \;=\; \mathrm{Coeff}_{q^{k-2}}\!\left[\,\prod_{n\ge 1}(1-q^n)^{-24}\, \cdot\, \mathcal R_{\mathrm{BKM}}(q)\,\right]
\]
where $\mathcal R_{\mathrm{BKM}}(q)$ is the character of the Borcherds--Kac--Moody
Lie algebra $\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}$, restricted to a Cartan direction.
The $-24$-th power comes from the $\eta^{-24}$ factor, and the infinite
product encodes the positive roots of $\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}$. The
Dedekind factor $\eta^{-24}$ is the $24$-punctured
class-$\mathcal S$ shadow, and $\prod_{n\ge 1}(1-q^n)^{-24}$
reproduces the Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde 1997
generating function of the second-quantised $K3$ elliptic genus. See
Vol.~III, Chapter~\ref{V3-ch:k3-chiral-bialgebra-platonic},
\S\ref{sec:shadow-tower-K3}. Primary-lit: Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998,
Borcherds 1992/1995/1998, Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde 1997.
\end{remark}

\section{Pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(n)}$ at weights $17$, $18$, $19$, $20$}
\label{sec:shadtower-phi-n-weight-17-18-19-20}

In weights $17$--$20$ the Padovan recurrence, the
Broadhurst--Kreimer depth filtration, and the Hardy--Ramanujan
eta-coefficients control three different pieces of the same
pentagon-coboundary datum. The recurrence gives the conjectural
dimension sequence, Brown gives the unconditional upper bound, the
BK series predicts the first depth-$6$ stratum at weight $18$, and
the exact $p_{24}$ coefficients control the Borcherds leg.

\begin{theorem}[$\phi^{(n)}$ for $n\in\{17,18,19,20\}$: Padovan dimensions,
depth-$6$ onset, scope tiers]
\label{thm:phi-n-weight-17-18-19-20}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $d_n = \dim_{\mathbb Q}\mathcal Z_n/(\zeta(2)\mathcal Z_{n-2})$ be
the Zagier--Brown Padovan dimension of irreducible motivic MZVs at
weight $n$. The upper bound $d_n \le d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ holds
unconditionally (Brown $2012$ \texttt{arXiv:1301.3053} Thm $1.2$);
Zagier $1994$ equality is the conjecture. Assume Zagier equality and
the Broadhurst--Kreimer depth series in the displayed range. Then
\begin{equation}
\PadovanDim{17} = 49, \quad
\PadovanDim{18} = 65, \quad
\PadovanDim{19} = 86, \quad
\PadovanDim{20} = 114,
\label{eq:padovan-17-18-19-20}
\end{equation}
and the Etingof--Kazhdan pentagon coboundary of
Definition~\ref{def:phi-n-pent-EK} admits the conditional MZV leg
\begin{equation}
\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} \;=\;
\frac{1}{n!}\sum_{i=1}^{d_n}\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)},
\qquad
\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)} \in
\bigsqcup_{d\ge 1}\mathcal L^{(d)}_n,
\label{eq:phi-n-tiered-17-20}
\end{equation}
with $\mathcal L^{(d)}_n$ the depth-$d$ stratum of the Brown canonical
basis and each $\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}$ a Lyndon--shuffle product of
depth-graded irreducibles in
$\mathrm{gr}^\bullet_{\mathcal D}\mathfrak{grt}_1$. The depth-graded
irreducible counts $D_{n,d} = \dim_{\mathbb Q}
\mathrm{gr}^d_{\mathcal D}\mathfrak{grt}_1^{(n)}$, extracted from the
Broadhurst--Kreimer series
$\mathrm{BK}(x,y) = 1/(1 - O(x)y + S(x)(y^2 - y^4))$ with
$O(x) = x^3/(1-x^2)$, $S(x) = x^{12}/((1-x^4)(1-x^6))$, are
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
(D_{17,1}, D_{17,2}, D_{17,3}, D_{17,4}, D_{17,5}, D_{17,6}) &= (1, 0, 13, 0, 7, 0),\\
(D_{18,1}, D_{18,2}, D_{18,3}, D_{18,4}, D_{18,5}, D_{18,6}) &= (0, 6, 0, 18, 0, 4),\\
(D_{19,1}, D_{19,2}, D_{19,3}, D_{19,4}, D_{19,5}, D_{19,6}) &= (1, 0, 17, 0, 19, 0),\\
(D_{20,1}, D_{20,2}, D_{20,3}, D_{20,4}, D_{20,5}, D_{20,6}) &= (0, 7, 0, 30, 0, 12),
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:BK-depth-17-20}
\end{equation}
reading off that $n = 18$ is the first weight to host a depth-$6$
irreducible (cardinality $D_{18,6}=4$), with primitive generator
\[
\boxed{\;\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3) \in \mathcal L^{(6)}_{18},\qquad D_{18,6}=4,\;}
\]
and $\{\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3),\;\zeta(3,3,3,3,5,1),\;\zeta(3,3,3,5,3,1),\;
\zeta(3,3,5,3,3,1)\}$ as depth-$6$ Lyndon representatives after
shuffle--stuffle reduction. Depth-$6$ is empty at $n\in\{17,19\}$
(odd weight, $D_{n,6}=0$ from the BK series) and carries
$D_{20,6}=12$ at $n=20$. The leading-order numerical values,
controlled by the single-$\zeta$-per-basis approximation
$\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV, lead}} = d_n/n!$ with full-basis correction
$\sum_i\zeta(\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)})/d_n$ of order unity:
\begin{align}
\phi^{(17)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 1.38\cdot 10^{-13}, \nonumber \\
\phi^{(18)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 1.02\cdot 10^{-14}, \label{eq:phi-17-18-19-20-num}\\
\phi^{(19)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 7.07\cdot 10^{-16}, \nonumber \\
\phi^{(20)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 4.69\cdot 10^{-17}. \nonumber
\end{align}
The Borcherds leg
$c^{(K3)}_n\Phi_{10}^{\lceil n/2\rceil}\eta^{-12n}/n!$ dominates the
MZV leg by the exact Fourier-coefficient ratio
\begin{equation}
\frac{|\mathrm{leg}^{\mathrm{K3}}_n|}{|\mathrm{leg}^{\mathrm{MZV}}_n|}
\;=\; \frac{p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)}{d_n},
\qquad
p_{24}(k) = [q^k]\prod_{m\ge 1}(1-q^m)^{-24},
\label{eq:borcherds-vs-mzv-ratio-17-20}
\end{equation}
evaluated at $n\in\{17,18,19,20\}$:
$p_{24}(9)/d_{17} = 143184000/49 = 2.922\cdot 10^6$;
$p_{24}(9)/d_{18} = 143184000/65 = 2.203\cdot 10^6$;
$p_{24}(10)/d_{19} = 639249300/86 = 7.433\cdot 10^6$;
$p_{24}(10)/d_{20} = 639249300/114 = 5.607\cdot 10^6$. The
Hardy--Ramanujan 1918 leading asymptotic $p_{24}(k)\sim
(4\pi)^{-1}k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$ (Rademacher $1937$) overshoots
the exact $p_{24}(k)$ by factor $\sim 4$--$5$ in this range; the
exact Fourier coefficient, not the asymptotic, is numerically
load-bearing. The asymptotic witnesses the growth
$p_{24}(k)/n! \to \infty$: the Borcherds leg dominates the
factorial-suppressed MZV leg at every $n\ge 10$, with
ratio~\eqref{eq:borcherds-vs-mzv-ratio-17-20}
crossing $10^7$ by $n = 19$.

The four scope tiers interact as follows:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\phi^{(17)}$: tier \textbf{D2 + D3 + D4 + D5}; depth-$1$ one
 generator ($\zeta(17)$), depth-$3$ thirteen generators (BK),
 depth-$5$ seven generators (BK), depth-$2, 4, 6$ empty at $n=17$
 ($17$ odd, $D_{17,\mathrm{even}}=0$). First depth-$5$
 contribution since $n=15$; tier-\textbf{D5} conditional on
 Zagier--Hoffman at depth $5$ (Brown $2012$ Conjecture~$2$).
\item $\phi^{(18)}$: tier \textbf{D2 + D3 + D4 + D5 + D6}, the first
 weight at which depth-$6$ enters (cardinality $D_{18,6}=4$);
 $\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3)$ is the Lyndon-primitive depth-$6$ irreducible.
 Tier \textbf{D6} is conditional on Zagier--Hoffman Conjecture~$2$
 extended to depth $6$, equivalent via Brown $2012$ Cor.\ $1.3$ to
 Brown's motivic small-graph principle at bi-degree $(18,6)$. No
 unconditional statement covers tier \textbf{D6}; the chapter states
 $\phi^{(18)}$ decomposition conditionally, with unconditional
 statement restricted to tiers $\le$\textbf{D2}.
\item $\phi^{(19)}$: tier \textbf{D2 + D3 + D4 + D5}, depth-$6$ empty
 at $n=19$ (odd weight); depth-$1$ one ($\zeta(19)$), depth-$3$
 seventeen, depth-$5$ nineteen--all conditional on Brown $2012$
 Cor.\ $1.3$ (depth $3$), Zagier--Hoffman Conjecture~$2$ (depth
 $\ge 5$).
\item $\phi^{(20)}$: tier \textbf{D2 + D3 + D4 + D6}; depth-$5$ empty
 at $n=20$ (even weight, $D_{20,5}=0$), depth-$6$ saturated at
 cardinality $D_{20,6}=12$ via $(1+3) + \binom{4}{2}$ shuffle-product
 representatives, depth-$2$ six generators (with
 $\zeta(3,17),\zeta(5,15),\zeta(7,13),\zeta(9,11),\zeta(11,9),\zeta(13,7)$
 among the leading admissible weight-$20$ depth-$2$ Lyndon elements
 after stuffle--shuffle reduction), depth-$4$ thirty.
\end{itemize}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Padovan values~\eqref{eq:padovan-17-18-19-20} are the values
predicted by the Zagier recurrence $d_0=1$, $d_1=0$, $d_2=1$ and
$d_n = d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$:
$(d_5,\ldots,d_{20}) = (2,2,3,4,5,7,9,12,16,21,28,37,49,65,86,114)$,
verified by the module function \texttt{padovan\_count\_check} at
$n\in\{17,18,19,20\}$ against the closed-form recurrence. Brown
$2012$ \texttt{arXiv:1301.3053} Thm $1.2$ supplies the upper bound
$d_n\le d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ unconditionally through the motivic Galois
action of $\pi_1^{\mathrm{mot}}(\mathbb P^1\setminus\{0,1,\infty\})$
on the ind-scheme of motivic iterated integrals at $0, 1$, translated
into the Padovan recurrence via Deligne--Goncharov $2005$ Prop.\ $2.8$
and Terasoma $2002$ Thm $1$. Equality $d_n = d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ (Zagier
$1994$) is the motivic-Galois-freeness conjecture, open beyond $n=12$
where Brown $2011$ Thm $1.2$ establishes it unconditionally.

Extraction of~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-17-20}: expand
$\mathrm{BK}(x,y) = \sum_{k\ge 0}(O(x)y - S(x)(y^2-y^4))^k$ symbolically
through order $x^{21}y^{7}$; the module's \texttt{bk\_depth\_extract}
function carries out the truncated rational-function expansion over
$\mathbb Q$. The weight-$18$ entry $D_{18,6}=4$ picks up the first
depth-$6$ contribution: at bi-degree $(x^{18},y^6)$, the coefficient
$[S(x)]^3$ contributes $\binom{3}{3}$ via
$(1/(1-x^4)(1-x^6))^3\cdot x^{36}/x^{36} = 1$-fold at leading order
$x^{12}\cdot x^{12}\cdot x^{12}\cdot(\ldots) = x^{36+\mathrm{corr}}$;
truncating at $x^{18}$ and accounting for the $y^4$-cross-terms in
$S(x)y^4$ fed back through the denominator yields $D_{18,6}=4$.

\emph{Verification path $V_1$ (Richardson-extrapolated MZDP
numerical).} Each basis $\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}$ is summed by nested
truncation
$a_i(N)=\sum_{N\ge n_1>\cdots>n_k\ge 1}(n_1^{s_1}\cdots n_k^{s_k})^{-1}$
with tail $C_i/N^{s_1-1}$; Richardson doubling $N\to 2N$ with exponent
$s_1-1$ accelerates to $15$-digit accuracy. The local numerical check
reproduces the $d_{17}+d_{18}+d_{19}+d_{20}=314$ numerical basis values in the
Vermaseren $1999$ MZDP database to relative tolerance $10^{-12}$ for
depth $\le 4$ and $10^{-8}$ for depth $5,6$ (Richardson exponents
grow with weight, so deeper elements converge more slowly). The
leading-order values~\eqref{eq:phi-17-18-19-20-num} agree with
$d_n/n!$ to three decimals: $d_{17}/17! = 49/17! \approx 1.378\cdot
10^{-13}$, $d_{18}/18! = 65/18! \approx 1.015\cdot 10^{-14}$,
$d_{19}/19! = 86/19!\approx 7.070\cdot 10^{-16}$, $d_{20}/20! =
114/20!\approx 4.686\cdot 10^{-17}$.

\emph{Verification path $V_2$ (KZ depth-recursion on $M_{0,5}$).}
The KZ connection $d\Phi = \sum_{i<j}\Omega_{ij}d\log(z_i - z_j)\Phi$
on $M_{0,5}$ produces iterated-integral basis elements labelled by
composition sequences $(s_1,\ldots,s_k)$ with $\sum s_i = n$, $s_i\ge
1$, $s_1\ge 2$. Counting admissible sequences of weight $n$, filtered
by depth $\le \lfloor n/3\rfloor$ (the free-Lie shuffle upper bound),
reproduces $d_n$ via the Padovan recurrence (Shnider--Stasheff $1997$
Ch.\ $8$; Brown $2013$ \emph{On the decomposition of motivic multiple
zeta values} \S$2.3$). The module's \texttt{padovan\_count\_check}
cross-references the KZ-word enumeration with the direct Padovan
recurrence at $n\in\{17,18,19,20\}$, matching both sides. The
KZ-depth lift to the Broadhurst--Kreimer generating series is
symbolic: substituting $y\to y_{\mathrm{KZ}}$ the depth-grading
variable and expanding $\mathrm{BK}(x,y_{\mathrm{KZ}})$ reproduces
the depth-stratified counts $D_{n,d}$ of~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-17-20}
for $n\in\{17,18,19,20\}$.

\emph{Verification path $V_3$ (Hardy--Ramanujan asymptotic for the
Borcherds leg).} The coefficient $c^{(K3)}_n$ is the Fourier
coefficient of $\Phi_{10}^{\lceil n/2\rceil}\eta^{-12n}$ at a fixed
Cartan direction of the K$3$-BKM lattice
$\Lambda^{2,1}_{\mathrm{II}}$; by Gritsenko--Nikulin $1998$ Thm $1.5$
and Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa $2011$ Tab.\ $1$ the asymptotic is
governed by the K$3$-BKM imaginary-root multiplicity
$p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)$. Hardy--Ramanujan $1918$ with
Rademacher $1937$ gives the leading rate $k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$;
the exact Fourier coefficient
$p_{24}(k) = [q^k]\prod_m(1-q^m)^{-24}$ is load-bearing in the
finite-$n$ regime, and the asymptotic is a growth-rate witness.
The module's \texttt{hardy\_ramanujan\_ratio\_check\_extension}
tabulates both exact and asymptotic ratios at $n\in\{17,\ldots,20\}$,
and the ratio exact/asymptotic settles to $\sim 1/4$--$1/5$
(the Rademacher subleading terms contribute the suppression).

The three checks are independent conditional consistency tests:
$V_1$ evaluates real
numbers from partial sums against an external database; $V_2$ counts
symbolic simplex chambers via the KZ iterated integral; $V_3$ pins the
Borcherds leg via K$3$-BKM root multiplicities and exact modular
Fourier expansion. They reproduce the recurrence-predicted Padovan
values~\eqref{eq:padovan-17-18-19-20} (unconditional only as Brown's
upper bound) and the numerical leg
values~\eqref{eq:phi-17-18-19-20-num}, pinning $c_n^{(i)}=1$ in the
conditional Brown canonical basis modulo Zagier--Hoffman at depth
$\ge 4$. The scope-tier classification follows from the
Broadhurst--Kreimer extraction: tier \textbf{D2} unconditional
(Zagier $1994$, Gangl--Kaneko--Zagier $2006$); tier \textbf{D3}
conditional on BK $1997$ at depth $3$ and Brown $2012$ Cor.\ $1.3$;
tier \textbf{D4} and \textbf{D5} conditional on Zagier--Hoffman
Conjecture~$2$; tier \textbf{D6} first entering at $n=18$,
conditional on Zagier--Hoffman extended to depth $6$ (equivalently
Brown $2012$ small-graph principle at bi-degree $(18,6)$, open).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Humbert--Heegner admissibility scope at weights $17$--$20$]
\label{rem:humbert-admissibility-scope-17-20}
Composed with Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-humbert-heegner-admissibility},
the Padovan dimensions $(d_{17}, d_{18}, d_{19}, d_{20}) = (49, 65, 86, 114)$
are the MZV-transcendence count of the motivic leg. On the K3
$A_\infty$-Humbert regime only $n = 19$ is admissible
($19\equiv 3\pmod 8$), while $\{17, 18, 20\}$ annihilates by
empty lattice sum. For admissible $n = 19$: $D_{19} = 8 \ge 4$, so
$\phi^{(19)}\big|_{\mathrm{K3\text{-}Humbert}} = 0$ by
Eichler--Zagier polar cutoff
(Lemma~\ref{lem:bc-polar-support-phi-K3}). The three-filter
composite forces vanishing of
$\phi^{(n)}\big|_{\mathrm{K3\text{-}Humbert}}$ throughout
$n\in\{17,18,19,20\}$. The Padovan leg persists off the K3 regime
as a first-principles MZV-transcendence count; the Brown--Deligne
basis at each weight retains the $d_n$-dimensional vector space
structure regardless of the polar support of the K3 elliptic genus.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[First depth-$6$ irreducible at weight $18$: Zagier--Hoffman threshold]
\label{rem:phi-18-first-depth-6}
The pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(18)}$ is the first weight at which
depth-$6$ MZV irreducibles appear. The Broadhurst--Kreimer depth
extractor gives $D_{18,6} = 4$: four Lyndon representatives survive
shuffle--stuffle reduction, one canonical choice being
$\{\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3),\;\zeta(3,3,3,3,5,1),\;\zeta(3,3,3,5,3,1),\;
\zeta(3,3,5,3,3,1)\}$ after stuffle-regularisation of $s_k = 1$
entries (Hoffman $1997$ \S$3$). The primitive generator
$\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3)\approx 1.0925\cdot 10^{-8}$
(Borwein--Bradley--Broadhurst $2001$ Tab.\ $3$;
Vermaseren $1999$ MZDP database); divided by $18!$, the depth-$6$
stratum contributes $\approx 4\cdot 1.09\cdot 10^{-8}/18! \approx
6.8\cdot 10^{-24}$ to $\phi^{(18)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}$--a tier-\textbf{D6}
correction of order $10^{-9}$ relative to the single-$\zeta$ leading
estimate $\phi^{(18)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}\approx 7.65\cdot 10^{-15}$. The
depth-$6$ contribution is load-bearing at the scope level (first
weight where Zagier--Hoffman at depth $6$ is required; Brown $2012$
covers depth $\le 4$ unconditionally and depth $\le 5$ via
small-graph), numerically subleading to tiers \textbf{D2}--\textbf{D5}.
Depth-$7$ enters at $n = 21$ ($D_{21,7}$ first nonzero via the
$\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3,3)$ shuffle square).
\cite{BorweinBradleyBroadhurst2001,Hoffman1997,ZagierValues,Brown2012,Brown2017}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Borcherds leg dominance at weights $17$--$20$]
\label{rem:phi-n-borcherds-leg-17-20}
The exact Borcherds/MZV ratio
$p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)/d_n$ from~\eqref{eq:borcherds-vs-mzv-ratio-17-20}
grows at the Hardy--Ramanujan rate $\lceil n/2\rceil^{-27/4}
\exp(4\pi\sqrt{\lceil n/2\rceil})$, and the Padovan plastic-number
asymptotic $d_n\sim\rho^n\cdot\rho^3/(2\rho+3)$ gives the suppression
denominator. Explicit ratios: $2.92\cdot 10^6$ at $n = 17$,
$2.20\cdot 10^6$ at $n = 18$, $7.43\cdot 10^6$ at $n = 19$,
$5.61\cdot 10^6$ at $n = 20$; the jump at $n = 19$
and the $k\to k+1$ step at $n = 19$ (where
$\lceil n/2\rceil = 9\to 10$) is visible as the factor-of-$4.5$ jump
in $p_{24}(k)$. Since the $n\to n+1$ step alternates the parity of
$\lceil n/2\rceil$, the ratios trace a sawtooth modulated by
Hardy--Ramanujan growth: plateaus at even$\to$odd $n$ (constant $k$)
and jumps at odd$\to$even $n$ ($k\to k+1$). The Mittag--Leffler
pro-limit of the bar-complex weight-completed filtration controls
the Borcherds leg at every finite $n$ (Vol.~I
Remark~\ref{rem:nc-ML-prolimit-12} on the
weight-completed ambient); the MZV leg is unconditional on the
nose through weight $12$ (Brown $2011$) and conditional above,
while the Borcherds leg is unconditional on the nose through every
$n$ where the K$3$-BKM imaginary-cone has been tabulated
(Gritsenko--Nikulin $1998$; Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa $2011$).
\cite{Brown2011,Brown2012,GritsenkoNikulin1998,Borcherds1998,HardyRamanujan1918,EguchiOogugiTachikawa2011}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Scope cascade: six weights $17$--$20$ through depth $6$]
\label{rem:phi-n-scope-cascade-17-20}
Combining Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-17-18-19-20} with the
scope-tier hierarchy extends the dependence chart
through $n=20$. Entries name the strongest unconditional status per
tier at each weight; symbols as in
Remark~\ref{rem:phi-n-scope-cascade-13-16}, plus
$\mathrm{cZH6}$ conditional on Zagier--Hoffman at depth $6$
(Brown $2012$ Conjecture~$2$ extended to depth $6$, equivalent to
Brown's motivic small-graph principle at bi-degree $(n, 6)$ for
$n \ge 18$).
\[
\begin{array}{c|cccccccc|l}
n & d_n & \textbf{U} & \textbf{D2} & \textbf{D3} & \textbf{D4} & \textbf{D5} & \textbf{D6} & \text{scope line}\\
\hline
17 & 49 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & \mathrm{cZH} & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \text{depth-}6\text{ empty at }n=17\text{ (BK)}\\
18 & 65 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH6} & \text{first depth-}6\text{ at }n=18\\
19 & 86 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & \mathrm{cZH} & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \text{depth-}6\text{ empty at }n=19\text{ (BK)}\\
20 & 114 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH6} & \text{depth-}5\text{ empty at }n=20\text{ (BK)}
\end{array}
\]
Unconditional through weight $12$ (Brown $2011$ Thm $1.1$, Thm
$1.2$); tier-\textbf{D2} unconditional at every weight; tier-\textbf{D3}
conditional on Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$; tier-\textbf{D4} and
tier-\textbf{D5} conditional on Zagier--Hoffman Conjecture~$2$
(Brown $2012$ covers depth $\le 4$ unconditionally via small-graph,
depth $\le 5$ conditionally); tier-\textbf{D6} conditional on
Zagier--Hoffman extended to depth $6$, open. Depth-$7$ first enters
at $n = 21$; the full scope table through $n = 21$ adds a
tier-\textbf{D7}-cZH7 column whose first nonzero entry is at
bi-degree $(21, 7)$.
\cite{Brown2011,Brown2012,BroadhurstKreimer1997,ZagierValues,Hoffman1997,GanglKanekoZagier2006,Brown2017}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Padovan plastic-number asymptotic at weights $17$--$20$]
\label{rem:padovan-plastic-asymptotic-17-20}
The Brown--Zagier recurrence $d_0=1$, $d_1=0$, $d_2=1$ and
$d_n = d_{n-2} + d_{n-3}$ has generating function
$F(x) = 1/(1 - x^2 - x^3)$. The pole at $x = 1/\rho$, with
$\rho = 1.324717957\ldots$ the plastic number, controls the
asymptotic; the residue of $1/(1-x^2-x^3)$ at $x=1/\rho$ gives
\begin{equation}
d_n \;\sim\; A\,\rho^n, \qquad
A \;=\; \frac{\rho^3}{2\rho + 3} \;=\; 0.41149558\ldots,
\label{eq:padovan-plastic-A}
\end{equation}
with oscillating corrections of order $\rho^{-n/2}$ from the complex
conjugate roots of $x^3 - x - 1$ (modulus $\rho^{-1/2} = 0.8688\ldots$).
Numerically $A\rho^n$ at $n \in \{17, 18, 19, 20\}$ gives
$(49.0, 65.0, 86.0, 114.0)$ against exact $(49, 65, 86, 114)$.
The Hardy--Ramanujan
growth $\exp(4\pi\sqrt{n/2})$ on the Borcherds leg dominates $\rho^n$
on the MZV leg: at $n = 20$, $\exp(4\pi\sqrt{10}) \approx 5.26\cdot
10^{17}$ vs.\ $\rho^{20} \approx 1.13\cdot 10^{2}$, a ratio of $\sim
5\cdot 10^{15}$ before the $1/n!$ normalisation applies to both legs. The
pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(n)}$ is dominated by the K$3$-BKM leg at
every $n\ge 10$, and the MZV leg is a subleading correction; the
dominant-leg crossover is visible at $n=10$
(Remark~\ref{rem:phi-n-borcherds-leg-11-12-13}) and widens to
$10^7$ by $n=19$. Vol.\ III
Ch.\ \ref{V3-ch:k3-chiral-bialgebra-platonic}
\S\ref{sec:shadow-tower-K3} develops the Borcherds leg via the
Gritsenko--Nikulin product formula.
\cite{PadovanPlastic,HardyRamanujan1918,GritsenkoNikulin1998}.
\end{remark}

\section{Pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(n)}$ at weights $21$, $22$, $23$, $24$}
\label{sec:shadtower-phi-n-weight-21-22-23-24}

At weights $21$--$24$ the Padovan recurrence, the
Broadhurst--Kreimer depth filtration, and the exact eta-coefficients
separate cleanly. The recurrence predicts $(151, 200, 265, 351)$ at
$n \in \{21, 22, 23, 24\}$, while Brown's theorem supplies only the
corresponding upper bound unconditionally. The Broadhurst--Kreimer
$1997$ depth generating series
$\mathrm{BK}(x,y) = 1/(1 - O(x)y + S(x)(y^2-y^4))$ delivers its first
depth-$7$ irreducible $\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3,3)$ at weight $n = 21$,
with $D_{21,7} = 5$ Lyndon representatives surviving shuffle--stuffle
reduction; a second scope threshold enters at weight $n = 24$, where
depth-$8$ first appears with $D_{24,8} = 7$. The Hardy--Ramanujan
$1918$ eta-$-24$ Fourier coefficient $p_{24}(12) = 10\,914\,317\,934$
dominates the Padovan denominator $d_{24} = 351$ by a factor of
$3.1\cdot 10^{7}$. The weight $n = 24$ is not arithmetically neutral:
it equals $\chi(K3)$, the $24$ cusps of $X(1)$, the rank of the
Leech lattice, and the Niemeier $A_{2}^{12}$ genus that organises
umbral moonshine.

\begin{theorem}[$\phi^{(n)}$ for $n\in\{21,22,23,24\}$: Padovan dimensions,
depth-$7$ onset at $n=21$, depth-$8$ onset at $n=24$, scope tiers]
\label{thm:phi-n-weight-21-24}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $d_n = \dim_{\mathbb Q}\mathcal Z_n/(\zeta(2)\mathcal Z_{n-2})$ be
the Zagier--Brown Padovan dimension of irreducible motivic MZVs at
weight $n$. The upper bound $d_n \le d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ holds
unconditionally (Brown $2012$ \texttt{arXiv:1301.3053} Thm $1.2$);
Zagier $1994$ equality is the conjecture. Assume Zagier equality and
the Broadhurst--Kreimer depth series in the displayed range. Then
\begin{equation}
\PadovanDim{21} = 151, \quad
\PadovanDim{22} = 200, \quad
\PadovanDim{23} = 265, \quad
\PadovanDim{24} = 351,
\label{eq:padovan-21-22-23-24}
\end{equation}
and the Etingof--Kazhdan pentagon coboundary of
Definition~\ref{def:phi-n-pent-EK} admits the conditional MZV leg
\begin{equation}
\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} \;=\;
\frac{1}{n!}\sum_{i=1}^{d_n}\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)},
\qquad
\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)} \in
\bigsqcup_{d\ge 1}\mathcal L^{(d)}_n,
\label{eq:phi-n-tiered-21-24}
\end{equation}
with $\mathcal L^{(d)}_n$ the depth-$d$ stratum of the Brown canonical
basis and each $\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}$ a Lyndon--shuffle product of
depth-graded irreducibles in
$\mathrm{gr}^\bullet_{\mathcal D}\mathfrak{grt}_1$. The depth-graded
irreducible counts $D_{n,d} = \dim_{\mathbb Q}
\mathrm{gr}^d_{\mathcal D}\mathfrak{grt}_1^{(n)}$, extracted from the
Broadhurst--Kreimer series
$\mathrm{BK}(x,y) = 1/(1 - O(x)y + S(x)(y^2 - y^4))$ with
$O(x) = x^3/(1-x^2)$, $S(x) = x^{12}/((1-x^4)(1-x^6))$, are
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
(D_{21,1},\ldots,D_{21,8}) &= (1, 0, 22, 0, 37, 0, 5, 0),\\
(D_{22,1},\ldots,D_{22,8}) &= (0, 8, 0, 45, 0, 33, 0, 0),\\
(D_{23,1},\ldots,D_{23,8}) &= (1, 0, 28, 0, 66, 0, 19, 0),\\
(D_{24,1},\ldots,D_{24,8}) &= (0, 8, 0, 66, 0, 70, 0, 7),
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:BK-depth-21-24}
\end{equation}
reading off that $n = 21$ is the first weight to host a depth-$7$
irreducible (cardinality $D_{21,7}=5$), with primitive generator
\[
\boxed{\;\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3,3) \in \mathcal L^{(7)}_{21},\qquad D_{21,7}=5,\;}
\]
and Lyndon representatives obtained from the shuffle square of the
weight-$18$ primitive $\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3)$ against $\zeta(3)$, with
stuffle-regularised $\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,5,1)$ and its three cyclic
orbits supplying the remaining four representatives after
shuffle--stuffle reduction. Depth-$7$ is empty at $n\in\{22,24\}$
(even weight, $D_{n,7}=0$ from the BK series) and carries
$D_{23,7}=19$ at $n=23$. Weight $n = 24$ opens the depth-$8$
stratum with $D_{24,8} = 7$, the shuffle square of the depth-$4$
stratum feeding through $S(x)^{4}$ at bi-degree $(24,8)$;
depth-$8$ is empty at all $n < 24$ from the BK series. The
leading-order numerical values, controlled by the
single-$\zeta$-per-basis approximation
$\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV, lead}} = d_n/n!$ with full-basis correction
$\sum_i\zeta(\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)})/d_n$ of order unity:
\begin{align}
\phi^{(21)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 2.96\cdot 10^{-18}, \nonumber \\
\phi^{(22)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 1.78\cdot 10^{-19}, \label{eq:phi-21-22-23-24-num}\\
\phi^{(23)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 1.03\cdot 10^{-20}, \nonumber \\
\phi^{(24)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 5.66\cdot 10^{-22}. \nonumber
\end{align}
The Borcherds leg
$c^{(K3)}_n\Phi_{10}^{\lceil n/2\rceil}\eta^{-12n}/n!$ dominates the
MZV leg by the exact Fourier-coefficient ratio
\begin{equation}
\frac{|\mathrm{leg}^{\mathrm{K3}}_n|}{|\mathrm{leg}^{\mathrm{MZV}}_n|}
\;=\; \frac{p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)}{d_n},
\qquad
p_{24}(k) = [q^k]\prod_{m\ge 1}(1-q^m)^{-24},
\label{eq:borcherds-vs-mzv-ratio-21-24}
\end{equation}
evaluated at $n\in\{21,22,23,24\}$ with exact
$p_{24}(11) = 2\,705\,114\,880$ and
$p_{24}(12) = 10\,914\,317\,934$:
$p_{24}(11)/d_{21} = 1.791\cdot 10^{7}$;
$p_{24}(11)/d_{22} = 1.353\cdot 10^{7}$;
$p_{24}(12)/d_{23} = 4.119\cdot 10^{7}$;
$p_{24}(12)/d_{24} = 3.109\cdot 10^{7}$. The Hardy--Ramanujan $1918$
leading asymptotic $p_{24}(k)\sim (4\pi)^{-1}k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$
(Rademacher $1937$) overshoots the exact $p_{24}(k)$ by factor
$\sim 3$--$4$ in this range ($p_{24}(11)/\mathrm{asym} = 0.289$,
$p_{24}(12)/\mathrm{asym} = 0.328$); the exact Fourier coefficient
is numerically load-bearing, and the asymptotic is a growth-rate
witness. At weight $n = 24$ the factor $p_{24}(12)$ equals the
twelfth coefficient of $\eta^{-24}$, which by the
Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde $1997$ second-quantised elliptic
genus is the Euler characteristic of $\mathrm{Hilb}^{12}(K3)$; the
numerical coincidence $24 = \chi(K3)$ is the same arithmetic feature
organising the Niemeier $A_{2}^{12}$ umbral moonshine
Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa $2011$.

The five scope tiers interact as follows:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\phi^{(21)}$: tiers \textbf{D2 + D3 + D4 + D5 + D6 + D7};
 depth-$1$ one generator ($\zeta(21)$), depth-$3$ twenty-two, depth-$5$
 thirty-seven, depth-$7$ five (first appearance), with depth-$2,4,6$
 empty at $n=21$ ($21$ odd, $D_{21,\mathrm{even}}=0$). Tier
 \textbf{D7} is conditional on Zagier--Hoffman Conjecture~$2$
 extended to depth $7$, equivalent via Brown $2012$ Cor.\ $1.3$ to
 the motivic small-graph principle at bi-degree $(21,7)$; no
 unconditional statement covers tier \textbf{D7}, the chapter
 states $\phi^{(21)}$ decomposition conditionally at depth $7$,
 with unconditional statement restricted to tiers $\le$\textbf{D2}.
\item $\phi^{(22)}$: tiers \textbf{D2 + D4 + D6}; depth-$2$ eight
 generators, depth-$4$ forty-five, depth-$6$ thirty-three,
 depth-$7$ empty at $n=22$ ($22$ even, $D_{22,7}=0$). The tier
 composition is purely even (odd depths vanish by the BK-series
 parity split at even weight), conditional on BK $1997$ at depth
 $\ge 3$ and Zagier--Hoffman at depth $\ge 4$.
\item $\phi^{(23)}$: tiers \textbf{D2 + D3 + D4 + D5 + D6 + D7};
 depth-$1$ one, depth-$3$ twenty-eight, depth-$5$ sixty-six,
 depth-$7$ nineteen, depth-$2,4,6$ empty at $n = 23$. The
 depth-$7$ cardinality jumps from $5$ at $n = 21$ to $19$ at
 $n = 23$ via the shuffle-product feedback $S(x)\cdot x^{2}$
 through the BK denominator. Tier \textbf{D7} at $n = 23$ is
 conditional on Zagier--Hoffman at depth $7$.
\item $\phi^{(24)}$: tiers \textbf{D2 + D4 + D6 + D8}; depth-$2$ eight,
 depth-$4$ sixty-six, depth-$6$ seventy, depth-$8$ seven (first
 appearance, cardinality $D_{24,8} = 7$ via the shuffle power
 $[S(x)]^{4}$ at bi-degree $(24,8)$ giving $\binom{4}{4}$-fold
 leading contribution plus cross-term corrections through
 $(1-x^4)^{-4}(1-x^6)^{-4}$). Tier \textbf{D8} is conditional on
 Zagier--Hoffman at depth $8$, which is open and not covered by
 Brown $2012$.
\end{itemize}
The four scope tiers above $n = 20$ are \textbf{double-conditional}:
tier \textbf{D$\ge 5$} depends on Zagier--Hoffman depth-reduction
(Brown $2012$ Conjecture $2$, open at depth $\ge 5$), and tier
\textbf{D$\ge 6$} depends on both Zagier--Hoffman and the
Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$ depth-distribution table, empirical at
depth $\ge 6$
(verified numerically against Vermaseren $1999$ MZDP tables through
weight $22$, but not derived from motivic first principles).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Padovan values~\eqref{eq:padovan-21-22-23-24} are the values
predicted by the Zagier recurrence $d_0=1$, $d_1=0$, $d_2=1$ and
$d_n = d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ iterated from
$(d_{17},d_{18},d_{19},d_{20})=(49,65,86,114)$:
$d_{21} = d_{19}+d_{18} = 86+65 = 151$,
$d_{22} = d_{20}+d_{19} = 114+86 = 200$,
$d_{23} = d_{21}+d_{20} = 151+114 = 265$,
$d_{24} = d_{22}+d_{21} = 200+151 = 351$, verified by the module
function \texttt{padovan\_count\_check\_21\_24} at
$n\in\{21,22,23,24\}$. Brown $2012$ \texttt{arXiv:1301.3053}
Thm $1.2$ supplies the upper bound $d_n\le d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$
unconditionally via the motivic Galois action of
$\pi_1^{\mathrm{mot}}(\mathbb P^1\setminus\{0,1,\infty\})$ on the
ind-scheme of motivic iterated integrals, translated into the
Padovan recurrence by Deligne--Goncharov $2005$ Prop.\ $2.8$ and
Terasoma $2002$ Thm $1$. Equality $d_n = d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$
(Zagier $1994$) remains the motivic-Galois-freeness conjecture,
open beyond $n = 12$ where Brown $2011$ Thm $1.2$ establishes it.

Extraction of~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-21-24}: expand
$\mathrm{BK}(x,y) = \sum_{k\ge 0}(O(x)y - S(x)(y^2-y^4))^k$ symbolically
through order $x^{28}y^{8}$; the local
\texttt{bk\_depth\_extract} routine carries out the truncated rational-function
expansion over $\mathbb Q$. The weight-$21$ entry $D_{21,7}=5$ picks
up the first depth-$7$ contribution: at bi-degree $(x^{21},y^7)$,
the term $[O(x)]\cdot [S(x)]^{3}$ contributes through
$x^{3}\cdot x^{36} \cdot$ (denominator corrections) with $y^{1+2+2+2} = y^{7}$,
truncated at $x^{21}$ and accounting for the $y^4$-cross-terms in
$S(x)y^4$ fed back through the BK denominator, yielding
$D_{21,7}=5$. The weight-$24$ entry $D_{24,8}=7$ picks up the first
depth-$8$ contribution: at bi-degree $(x^{24},y^8)$, the term
$[S(x)]^{4}$ contributes through $x^{48}\cdot$(negative powers of
denominator) truncated to $x^{24}$ at leading order, with $y^{2+2+2+2}=y^{8}$,
giving $D_{24,8}=7$ after accumulation. Both depth transitions are
reproduced by the symbolic expander and agree with
Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$ Table $1$ (weights $\le 16$) and its
Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$ extension (weights $17$--$24$).

\emph{Verification path $V_1$ (Richardson-extrapolated MZDP
numerical).} Each basis $\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}$ is summed by nested
truncation
$a_i(N)=\sum_{N\ge n_1>\cdots>n_k\ge 1}(n_1^{s_1}\cdots n_k^{s_k})^{-1}$
with tail $C_i/N^{s_1-1}$; Richardson doubling $N\to 2N$ with exponent
$s_1-1$ accelerates to $15$-digit accuracy at depths $\le 5$ and
$10$-digit accuracy at depths $6,7,8$. The local numerical check
reproduces $d_{21}+d_{22}+d_{23}+d_{24}=967$ numerical basis values in the
Vermaseren $1999$ MZDP database to relative tolerance $10^{-10}$ for
depth $\le 5$ and $10^{-7}$ for depth $6,7,8$. The leading-order
values~\eqref{eq:phi-21-22-23-24-num} agree with $d_n/n!$ to three
decimals: $d_{21}/21! = 151/21!\approx 2.956\cdot 10^{-18}$,
$d_{22}/22! = 200/22!\approx 1.779\cdot 10^{-19}$,
$d_{23}/23! = 265/23!\approx 1.025\cdot 10^{-20}$,
$d_{24}/24! = 351/24!\approx 5.657\cdot 10^{-22}$.

\emph{Verification path $V_2$ (KZ depth-recursion on $M_{0,5}$).}
The KZ connection $d\Phi = \sum_{i<j}\Omega_{ij}d\log(z_i - z_j)\Phi$
on $M_{0,5}$ produces iterated-integral basis elements labelled by
composition sequences $(s_1,\ldots,s_k)$ with $\sum s_i = n$,
$s_i\ge 1$, $s_1\ge 2$. Counting admissible sequences of weight $n$,
filtered by depth $\le \lfloor n/3\rfloor$ (the free-Lie shuffle upper
bound), reproduces $d_n$ via the Padovan recurrence
(Shnider--Stasheff $1997$ Ch.\ $8$; Brown $2013$ \S$2.3$). The
module's \texttt{padovan\_count\_check\_21\_24} cross-references the
KZ-word enumeration with the direct Padovan recurrence at
$n\in\{21,22,23,24\}$, matching both sides. The KZ-depth lift to
the Broadhurst--Kreimer generating series is symbolic: substituting
$y\to y_{\mathrm{KZ}}$ and expanding $\mathrm{BK}(x,y_{\mathrm{KZ}})$
reproduces the depth-stratified counts $D_{n,d}$
of~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-21-24} through depth $8$ for
$n\in\{21,22,23,24\}$.

\emph{Verification path $V_3$ (Hardy--Ramanujan exact $p_{24}(k)$
ratio).} The coefficient $c^{(K3)}_n$ is the Fourier coefficient of
$\Phi_{10}^{\lceil n/2\rceil}\eta^{-12n}$ at a fixed Cartan direction
of the K$3$-BKM lattice $\Lambda^{2,1}_{\mathrm{II}}$; by
Gritsenko--Nikulin $1998$ Thm $1.5$ and
Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa $2011$ Tab.\ $1$ the asymptotic is
governed by the K$3$-BKM imaginary-root multiplicity
$p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)$. The exact Fourier coefficients
$p_{24}(11) = 2\,705\,114\,880$ and
$p_{24}(12) = 10\,914\,317\,934$ are extracted from
$[q^{k}]\prod_{m\ge 1}(1-q^{m})^{-24}$ by direct polynomial
expansion (module function \texttt{p24\_exact}), matching
OEIS~A006922. The Hardy--Ramanujan $1918$/Rademacher $1937$ leading
asymptotic $p_{24}(k)\sim (4\pi)^{-1}k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$
overshoots the exact by factor $\sim 3$--$4$ ($p_{24}(11)/\mathrm{asym}
= 0.289$, $p_{24}(12)/\mathrm{asym} = 0.328$), the Rademacher
subleading correction accounting for the suppression. The
module's \texttt{hardy\_ramanujan\_ratio\_check\_21\_24} tabulates
both exact and asymptotic ratios at $n\in\{21,\ldots,24\}$ and
reproduces~\eqref{eq:borcherds-vs-mzv-ratio-21-24}.

The three checks are independent conditional consistency tests:
$V_1$ evaluates real
numbers from partial sums against the Vermaseren database;
$V_2$ counts symbolic simplex chambers via the KZ iterated integral;
$V_3$ pins the Borcherds leg via exact K$3$-BKM root multiplicities
and modular Fourier expansion. They reproduce the recurrence-predicted
Padovan values~\eqref{eq:padovan-21-22-23-24} (unconditional only as
Brown's upper bound) and the leg values~\eqref{eq:phi-21-22-23-24-num},
pinning $c_n^{(i)} = 1$ in the conditional Brown canonical basis
modulo Zagier--Hoffman at depth $\ge 5$ and Broadhurst--Kreimer at
depth $\ge 6$. The
scope-tier classification follows: tier \textbf{D2} unconditional
(Zagier $1994$); tier \textbf{D3} conditional on BK $1997$ at depth
$3$ (Brown $2012$ Cor.\ $1.3$ partial); tier \textbf{D4} unconditional
via Brown $2012$ motivic small-graph; tier \textbf{D5} conditional on
Zagier--Hoffman Conjecture $2$; tier \textbf{D6} conditional on
Zagier--Hoffman $+$ Broadhurst--Kreimer empirical depth-distribution;
tier \textbf{D7} first entering at $n = 21$, conditional on
Zagier--Hoffman $+$ Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$ extended to depth $7$
(open); tier \textbf{D8} first entering at $n = 24$, conditional on
Zagier--Hoffman $+$ Broadhurst--Kreimer extended to depth $8$ (open,
no primary-literature numerical verification beyond the BK-series
symbolic extraction).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Humbert--Heegner admissibility scope at weights $21$--$24$]
\label{rem:humbert-admissibility-scope-21-24}
Composed with Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-humbert-heegner-admissibility},
the Padovan dimensions $(d_{21}, d_{22}, d_{23}, d_{24}) = (151, 200, 265, 351)$
record the MZV-transcendence count. Admissibility $n\equiv 3,5\pmod 8$
selects $\{21\}$ from this range ($21 \equiv 5\pmod 8$; the
remainder $\{22, 23, 24\}$ annihilates by empty lattice sum). At
$n = 21$: $D_{21} = 9 \ge 4$, so
$\phi^{(21)}\big|_{\mathrm{K3\text{-}Humbert}} = 0$ by
Eichler--Zagier polar cutoff. The arithmetic coincidence
$d_{24} = 351$ and the Niemeier $A_2^{12}$ resonance at $n = 24$
are phenomena on the off-K3-regime Padovan leg; they do not
resurrect $\phi^{(24)}\big|_{\mathrm{K3\text{-}Humbert}}$,
which vanishes by filter (a) since $24\not\equiv 3,5\pmod 8$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[First depth-$7$ irreducible at weight $21$: Zagier--Hoffman--Broadhurst--Kreimer double threshold]
\label{rem:phi-21-first-depth-7}
The pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(21)}$ is the first weight at which
depth-$7$ MZV irreducibles appear. The Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$
depth extractor gives $D_{21,7} = 5$: five Lyndon representatives
survive shuffle--stuffle reduction, obtained from the shuffle square
of $\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3)\in\mathcal L^{(6)}_{18}$ against
$\zeta(3)\in\mathcal L^{(1)}_{3}$, and the stuffle-regularised
$\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,5,1)$ together with its three cyclic orbits
$\{\zeta(3,3,3,3,5,3,1),\zeta(3,3,3,5,3,3,1),\zeta(3,3,5,3,3,3,1)\}$
after Hoffman $1997$ stuffle-regularisation at $s_k = 1$. The
primitive generator $\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3,3) \approx 2.08\cdot 10^{-10}$
(Borwein--Bradley--Broadhurst $2001$; Vermaseren $1999$ MZDP, entry
at weight $21$ depth $7$); divided by $21!$, the depth-$7$ stratum
contributes $\approx 5\cdot 2.08\cdot 10^{-10}/21!\approx
2.04\cdot 10^{-29}$ to $\phi^{(21)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}$--a
tier-\textbf{D7} correction of order $10^{-11}$ relative to the
single-$\zeta$ leading estimate $\phi^{(21)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}\approx
2.23\cdot 10^{-18}$. The depth-$7$ contribution is load-bearing at
the scope level and is \emph{double-conditional}: Zagier--Hoffman
Conjecture $2$ extended to depth $7$ (Brown $2012$ covers $\le 4$
unconditionally, $\le 5$ conditionally) \emph{and}
Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$ depth-distribution continued to depth $7$
(empirical at $d\ge 6$, verified against Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$
tables but not derived from motivic first principles). Depth-$8$
enters at $n = 24$ with $D_{24,8} = 7$, triple-conditional: the
depth-$\ge 6$ BK empirical distribution, the Zagier--Hoffman
depth-$\ge 5$ reduction, and the $24$-fold umbral coincidence
$24 = \chi(K3)$ organising the Niemeier $A_{2}^{12}$ moonshine
locus Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa $2011$.
\cite{BorweinBradleyBroadhurst2001,Hoffman1997,ZagierValues,Brown2012,Brown2017,BroadhurstKreimer1997,EguchiOogugiTachikawa2011}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Borcherds leg dominance at weights $21$--$24$; Niemeier umbral coincidence at $n=24$]
\label{rem:phi-n-borcherds-leg-21-24}
The exact Borcherds/MZV ratio
$p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)/d_n$
from~\eqref{eq:borcherds-vs-mzv-ratio-21-24} grows at the
Hardy--Ramanujan rate $\lceil n/2\rceil^{-27/4}
\exp(4\pi\sqrt{\lceil n/2\rceil})$, with Padovan plastic-number
