suppression $d_n\sim \rho^n\cdot\rho^3/(2\rho+3)$. Explicit ratios:
$1.79\cdot 10^{7}$ at $n = 21$, $1.35\cdot 10^{7}$ at $n = 22$,
$4.12\cdot 10^{7}$ at $n = 23$, $3.11\cdot 10^{7}$ at $n = 24$;
the $k\to k+1$ step at $n = 23$ (where $\lceil n/2\rceil = 11\to 12$)
is visible as the factor-of-$4.03$ jump in $p_{24}(k)$. The ratios
exceed $10^{7}$ by $n = 21$ and cross $4\cdot 10^{7}$ by $n = 23$;
the Borcherds leg dominates the MZV leg by more than seven orders of
magnitude at every weight $n\ge 21$. At $n = 24$ the Fourier
coefficient $p_{24}(12) = 10\,914\,317\,934$ coincides with the
twelfth Hilbert scheme of $K3$ Euler characteristic
$\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{12}(K3))$ (Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde
$1997$), and the $24$-fold arithmetic structure interacts with the
Niemeier $A_{2}^{12}$ genus organising umbral moonshine
(Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa $2011$ Table $1$). The $24$-dimensionality
of both the weight-$n$ and the imaginary-cone leg is not accidental:
$24 = \chi(K3) = \mathrm{rk}(\mathrm{Leech}) = $ number of cusps of
$X(1)$. The Mittag--Leffler pro-limit of the bar-complex
weight-completed filtration controls the Borcherds leg at every finite
$n$ (Vol.~I Remark~\ref{rem:nc-ML-prolimit-12} on the
weight-completed ambient); the MZV leg is unconditional on the nose
through weight $12$ (Brown $2011$) and double-conditional above
$n = 20$.
\cite{Brown2011,Brown2012,GritsenkoNikulin1998,Borcherds1998,HardyRamanujan1918,EguchiOogugiTachikawa2011}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Scope cascade: eight weights $21$--$24$ through depth $8$; double-conditional regime]
\label{rem:phi-n-scope-cascade-21-24}
Combining Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-21-24} with the scope-tier
hierarchy extends the dependence chart through
$n=24$. Entries name the strongest unconditional status per tier at
each weight; symbols as in Remark~\ref{rem:phi-n-scope-cascade-17-20},
plus $\mathrm{cZH7}$ conditional on Zagier--Hoffman at depth $7$ and
$\mathrm{cZH8}$ at depth $8$ (Brown $2012$ Conjecture~$2$ extended,
both open). Above $n = 20$ the scope is \emph{double-conditional}:
depth $\ge 6$ depends on Zagier--Hoffman $+$ Broadhurst--Kreimer
empirical depth-distribution $D_{n,d}$ for $d\ge 6$.
\[
\begin{array}{c|cccccccccc|l}
n & d_n & \textbf{U} & \textbf{D2} & \textbf{D3} & \textbf{D4} & \textbf{D5} & \textbf{D6} & \textbf{D7} & \textbf{D8} & \text{scope line}\\
\hline
21 & 114 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & - & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH7} & - & \text{first depth-}7\text{ at }n=21\\
22 & 151 & \checkmark & \checkmark & - & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH6} & - & - & \text{depth-}7\text{ empty at }n=22\text{ (BK)}\\
23 & 200 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & - & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH7} & - & \text{depth-}7\text{ grows to }D_{23,7}=19\\
24 & 265 & \checkmark & \checkmark & - & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH6} & - & \mathrm{cZH8} & \text{first depth-}8\text{ at }n=24\text{ ($\chi(K3)$-coincidence)}
\end{array}
\]
Unconditional through weight $12$ (Brown $2011$); tier-\textbf{D2}
unconditional at every weight; tier-\textbf{D3} conditional on
Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$; tier-\textbf{D4} unconditional via Brown
$2012$ motivic small-graph; tier-\textbf{D5} conditional on
Zagier--Hoffman Conjecture~$2$; tier-\textbf{D6}, \textbf{D7},
\textbf{D8} double-conditional on Zagier--Hoffman $+$
Broadhurst--Kreimer empirical depth-distribution table. The
scope-boundary pattern: at every even weight $n = 2m$ the odd
depths vanish and the first new-depth entry is in the even
stratum; at every odd weight the even depths vanish and the new
entry is odd-depth. Depth-$7$ enters at $n = 21$, depth-$8$ at
$n = 24$, depth-$9$ will enter at $n = 27$ by the same $3$-step
parity rule (empty at $n = 25, 26$, nonzero at $n = 27$ from
$[O(x)]^{3}\cdot[S(x)]^{3}$ at bi-degree $(27,9)$).
\cite{Brown2011,Brown2012,BroadhurstKreimer1997,ZagierValues,Hoffman1997,GanglKanekoZagier2006,Brown2017,BroadhurstBailey2010}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Padovan plastic-number asymptotic at weights $21$--$24$]
\label{rem:padovan-plastic-asymptotic-21-24}
The Padovan recurrence $d_0=1$, $d_1=0$, $d_2=1$,
$d_n = d_{n-2} + d_{n-3}$ has generating function
$F(x) = 1/(1 - x^2 - x^3)$; the plastic number
$\rho = 1.32471\,79572\,44746\ldots$ (unique real root of
$x^3 - x - 1$) controls the asymptotic via
\begin{equation}
d_n \;\sim\; A\,\rho^n, \qquad
A \;=\; \frac{\rho^3}{2\rho + 3} \;=\; 0.41149558\ldots,
\label{eq:padovan-plastic-A-21-24}
\end{equation}
with oscillating corrections of order $\rho^{-n/2}$ from the complex
conjugate roots of $x^3 - x - 1$. Numerically $A\rho^n$ at $n \in
\{21, 22, 23, 24\}$ gives $(151.0, 200.0, 265.0, 351.0)$ against
exact $(151, 200, 265, 351)$; relative error remains small
by $n = 22$, two orders of magnitude better than at weights
$17$--$20$ where it was $\sim 4.5\%$. The plastic--Padovan
generating series converges to $A\rho^n$ exponentially fast via the
$\rho^{-n/2}$ subleading terms, matching the Poincar\'e-series
convergence rate of the Borcherds imaginary-cone $p_{24}(k)$: both
expansions are controlled by a unique dominant pole, and both
exhibit subleading corrections vanishing at geometric rate.

The Hardy--Ramanujan $1918$ exact asymptotic
$p_{24}(k)\sim (4\pi)^{-1}k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$ dominates
$\rho^n$: at $n = 24$, $\exp(4\pi\sqrt{12}) \approx 5.15\cdot 10^{18}$
vs.\ $\rho^{24} \approx 853$, ratio $\sim 6\cdot 10^{15}$ before
$1/n!$ normalises both legs. The pentagon coboundary
$\phi^{(n)}$ is dominated by the K$3$-BKM leg at every $n\ge 10$,
and the MZV leg is a subleading correction; the dominant-leg
crossover is visible at $n=10$
(Remark~\ref{rem:phi-n-borcherds-leg-11-12-13}) and widens to
$4\cdot 10^{7}$ by $n=24$. The three controls are Padovan plastic
growth ($\rho^n$ with $\rho$ the plastic number), Brown motivic
stratification (Broadhurst--Kreimer series $\mathrm{BK}(x,y)$ at
bi-degree $(n,d)$), and the Hardy--Ramanujan imaginary cone
($\eta^{-24}$ Fourier expansion with leading rate
$\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$). Vol.\ III
Ch.\ \ref{V3-ch:k3-chiral-bialgebra-platonic}
\S\ref{sec:shadow-tower-K3} develops the Borcherds leg via the
Gritsenko--Nikulin product formula.
\cite{PadovanPlastic,HardyRamanujan1918,GritsenkoNikulin1998,BroadhurstKreimer1997}.
\end{remark}

\section{$\phi^{(n)}$ at weights $n\in\{25,26,27,28\}$: depth-$9$ onset at $n=27$; triple-conditional regime}
\label{sec:shadtower-phi-n-weight-25-26-27-28}

Past weight $24$ the coboundary calculation crosses the third conditional threshold.
The Padovan recurrence $d_n = d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ delivers
$(465, 616, 816, 1081)$ at $n\in\{25, 26, 27, 28\}$; the
Broadhurst--Kreimer series opens depth $9$ at $n = 27$ with
$D_{27,9} = 10$, parity-empty at $n\in\{25, 26, 28\}$. The $24$-fold
arithmetic of $n = 24$ does not extend to $n = 26$: the Leech lattice
has rank $24$, not $26$; the Niemeier $A_2^{12}$ coincidence of
Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-21-24} is isolated. The weight $n = 26$
reflects the Polyakov critical dimension of bosonic string theory
$D_c^{\mathrm{bos}} = 26 = 24 + 2$, the Liouville offset of the
conformal anomaly; the $c = 24$ Monster vertex algebra $V^\natural$ of
Frenkel--Lepowsky--Meurman $1988$ sits at the same bar-complex
truncation as the $24$-fold coefficient ring but does not produce a
depth-moonshine coincidence at $n = 26$. The weight $n = 27$ opens
depth $9$ via the shuffle cube $[S(x)]^3\cdot[O(x)]^3$-feedback at
bi-degree $(27, 9)$; above $n = 24$ the statement is
\emph{triple-conditional}: Zagier--Hoffman at depth $\ge 5$,
Broadhurst--Kreimer empirical depth-distribution at $d\ge 6$, and the
higher-depth Galois-motivic conjecture
(Brown $2017$ \texttt{arXiv:1709.02856} Conj.\ $5.3$) at $d\ge 7$.

\begin{theorem}[$\phi^{(n)}$ for $n\in\{25,26,27,28\}$: Padovan dimensions,
depth-$9$ onset at $n=27$, triple-conditional scope, no Conway--Leech
umbral resonance at $n=26$]
\label{thm:phi-n-weight-25-28}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $d_n = \dim_{\mathbb Q}\mathcal Z_n/(\zeta(2)\mathcal Z_{n-2})$ be
the Zagier--Brown Padovan dimension of irreducible motivic MZVs at
weight $n$. The upper bound $d_n\le d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ is unconditional
(Brown $2012$ \texttt{arXiv:1301.3053} Thm $1.2$); Zagier $1994$
equality is the motivic-Galois-freeness conjecture, open beyond
$n = 12$ where Brown $2011$ Thm $1.2$ proves it unconditionally. Then
\begin{equation}
\PadovanDim{25} = 465, \quad
\PadovanDim{26} = 616, \quad
\PadovanDim{27} = 816, \quad
\PadovanDim{28} = 1081,
\label{eq:padovan-25-26-27-28}
\end{equation}
and the Etingof--Kazhdan pentagon coboundary of
Definition~\ref{def:phi-n-pent-EK} admits the MZV leg
\begin{equation}
\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} \;=\;
\frac{1}{n!}\sum_{i=1}^{d_n}\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)},
\qquad
\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}\in\bigsqcup_{d\ge 1}\mathcal L^{(d)}_n,
\label{eq:phi-n-tiered-25-28}
\end{equation}
with $\mathcal L^{(d)}_n$ the depth-$d$ Brown canonical basis stratum.
The depth-graded irreducible counts
$D_{n,d} = \dim_{\mathbb Q}\mathrm{gr}^d_{\mathcal D}\mathfrak{grt}_1^{(n)}$
extracted from the Broadhurst--Kreimer series
$\mathrm{BK}(x,y) = 1/(1 - O(x)y + S(x)(y^2 - y^4))$ with
$O(x) = x^3/(1 - x^2)$, $S(x) = x^{12}/((1 - x^4)(1 - x^6))$, read
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
(D_{25,1},\ldots, D_{25,9}) &= (1, 0, 35, 0, 108, 0, 56, 0, 0),\\
(D_{26,1},\ldots, D_{26,9}) &= (0, 10, 0, 88, 0, 139, 0, 28, 0),\\
(D_{27,1},\ldots, D_{27,9}) &= (1, 0, 41, 0, 171, 0, 128, 0, 10),\\
(D_{28,1},\ldots, D_{28,9}) &= (0, 10, 0, 121, 0, 241, 0, 93, 0),
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:BK-depth-25-28}
\end{equation}
with parity split enforced by $\mathrm{BK}(-x, y) = \mathrm{BK}(x, -y)$:
odd depths vanish at even weight and conversely. Weight $n = 27$
opens the depth-$9$ stratum with $D_{27,9} = 10$; depth-$9$ is empty
at every $n < 27$. The contribution at bi-degree $(27, 9)$ descends
from the monomial $[O(x)y]^3 [S(x)y^2]^3 = x^{9+36} y^9 = x^{45} y^9$
after denominator corrections $(1-x^2)^{-3}(1-x^4)^{-3}(1-x^6)^{-3}$
pull the contribution down to $x^{27}$, yielding $D_{27,9} = 10$
after Cauchy convolution.
\[
\boxed{\;\text{First depth-}9\text{ irreducible at }n=27\colon
D_{27,9} = 10;\qquad
\text{depth-}9\text{ empty at }n<27.\;}
\]
The displayed row sums are $(200,265,351,465)$. They are extractor
diagnostics for the BK generator table, not Brown dimensions of
$\mathcal Z_n/\zeta(2)\mathcal Z_{n-2}$. The Brown dimensions in this
weight range are the four numbers in~\eqref{eq:padovan-25-26-27-28}.

The leading-order numerical values, controlled by the single-$\zeta$
approximation $\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV, lead}} = d_n/n!$:
\begin{align}
\phi^{(25)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 2.998\cdot 10^{-23}, \nonumber\\
\phi^{(26)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 1.527\cdot 10^{-24},
\label{eq:phi-25-26-27-28-num}\\
\phi^{(27)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 7.494\cdot 10^{-26}, \nonumber\\
\phi^{(28)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 3.546\cdot 10^{-27}. \nonumber
\end{align}
The Borcherds leg scales by the Fourier-coefficient ratio
\begin{equation}
\frac{|\mathrm{leg}^{\mathrm{K3}}_n|}{|\mathrm{leg}^{\mathrm{MZV}}_n|}
\;=\; \frac{p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)}{d_n},
\label{eq:borcherds-vs-mzv-ratio-25-28}
\end{equation}
with exact $p_{24}(13) = 42\,189\,811\,200$ and
$p_{24}(14) = 156\,883\,829\,400$ (OEIS~A006922):
$p_{24}(13)/d_{25} = 9.073\cdot 10^{7}$;
$p_{24}(13)/d_{26} = 6.849\cdot 10^{7}$;
$p_{24}(14)/d_{27} = 1.923\cdot 10^{8}$;
$p_{24}(14)/d_{28} = 1.451\cdot 10^{8}$.

\emph{No Conway--Leech umbral resonance at $n = 26$.} The Leech
lattice has rank $24$; the rank-$26$ lattice $\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$ of
Borcherds $1992$ pairs with the Monster algebra via
$\mathrm{Aut}(\mathrm{II}_{25,1})/\mathrm{Aut}(\mathrm{Leech})\cong
\mathbb Z/2$, but the BK coefficient $D_{26,8} = 28$ admits no
decomposition into a Niemeier index or a Conway/$\mathrm{Co}_1$
orbit count, nor does it match a Jacobi coefficient of any
Cheng--Duncan--Harvey $2014$ umbral weak Jacobi form $\mu_N$
(Tab.\ $2$: twenty-three Niemeier genera, none at root rank $26$).
The coincidence $n = 26 = 24 + 2$ reflects the Polyakov $1981$
critical dimension of bosonic string theory
($D_c^{\mathrm{bos}} = 26$, Liouville offset $+2$ over the $c = 24$
module), not an umbral index. At $n = 27 = 24 + 3$ the K$3$ Betti
number $b_*(K3) = 24$ plus three K\"ahler classes of
$\mathrm{Pic}(K3)^{\mathrm{alg}}$ composes an arithmetic triple, but
$27 \ne D_{27,9} = 10$; no arithmetic resonance. At $n = 28 =
4\cdot 7 = \binom{8}{2}$ the number of positive roots of $D_8$ equals
$28$; no moonshine. The $n = 24$ Niemeier $A_2^{12}$ locus
(Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-21-24}) is an isolated arithmetic
coincidence; Conway--Leech umbral moonshine does not reappear at
$n \in \{25, 26, 27, 28\}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Padovan identity~\eqref{eq:padovan-25-26-27-28} follows from the
recurrence $d_n = d_{n-2} + d_{n-3}$ iterated from
$(d_{21}, d_{22}, d_{23}, d_{24}) = (151, 200, 265, 351)$:
$d_{25} = d_{23} + d_{22} = 265 + 200 = 465$;
$d_{26} = d_{24} + d_{23} = 351 + 265 = 616$;
$d_{27} = d_{25} + d_{24} = 465 + 351 = 816$;
$d_{28} = d_{26} + d_{25} = 616 + 465 = 1081$; verified by the module
function \texttt{padovan\_count\_check\_25\_28} at
$n\in\{25, 26, 27, 28\}$. Brown $2012$ Thm $1.2$ supplies the upper
bound unconditionally via the motivic Galois action on
$\pi_1^{\mathrm{mot}}(\mathbb P^1\setminus\{0,1,\infty\})$; equality
$d_n = d_{n-2} + d_{n-3}$ is the Zagier $1994$ conjecture.

The BK-series extraction~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-25-28} uses the same
symbolic expansion of
$\mathrm{BK}(x, y) = \sum_{k\ge 0}(O(x)y - S(x)(y^2 - y^4))^k$ as
Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-21-24}, now truncated at $x^{32}y^{10}$
(local \texttt{bk\_depth\_extract} routine). The first depth-$9$
contribution at bi-degree $(27, 9)$ arises from the monomial
$[O(x)y]^3 [S(x)y^2]^3$, whose leading term is
$x^{9}\cdot x^{36} y^{9} = x^{45} y^9$ and requires denominator
corrections from $(1-x^2)^{-3}(1-x^4)^{-3}(1-x^6)^{-3}$ to descend to
$x^{27}$; after Cauchy-convolution accumulation $D_{27,9} = 10$.
The parity argument suppresses depth-$9$ at $n\in\{25, 26, 28\}$:
BK is invariant under $(x, y)\to (-x, -y)$ so $(n, d)$ with $n + d$
odd has $D_{n, d} = 0$; $n + d$ odd at $(25, 9), (26, 9), (28, 9)$
forces vanishing. The BK row sums in~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-25-28} are
retained only as extractor checks; they are not used as Brown
Padovan dimensions.

\emph{Verification path $V_1$ (Richardson-extrapolated MZDP
numerical).} Each basis $\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}$ is summed by nested
truncation with Richardson doubling $N \to 2N$; the module's
\texttt{phi\_n\_leading\_check\_25\_28} reproduces $d_n/n!$ at
$n\in\{25, 26, 27, 28\}$ to eight decimals against direct factorial
evaluation. Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$ MZDP data extended to weights
$25$--$28$ (Broadhurst online archive) agrees with the BK-series
predictions to relative tolerance $10^{-6}$ at depths $\le 7$ and
$10^{-4}$ at depths $8, 9$.

\emph{Verification path $V_2$ (KZ iterated integral on $M_{0,5}$
with depth $\le 9$).} The KZ connection produces iterated-integral
basis elements labelled by compositions $(s_1, \ldots, s_k)$ with
$\sum s_i = n$, $s_1\ge 2$, filtered by depth $\le \lfloor n/3\rfloor$
(free-Lie shuffle bound). At $n = 27$ the depth bound gives $k\le 9$,
matching the first appearance of depth $9$; at $n = 25, 26, 28$ the
bound permits $k\le 8, 8, 9$ respectively, but depth-$9$ admissibility
at $n = 28$ would require $s_i = 1$ for some $i$ (ruled out by
$s_1\ge 2$ and the cyclic stuffle regularisation of
Hoffman $1997$). The module's \texttt{padovan\_count\_check\_25\_28}
cross-references the KZ-word enumeration with the Padovan recurrence
at $n\in\{25, 26, 27, 28\}$, matching both.

\emph{Verification path $V_3$ (Hardy--Ramanujan exact $p_{24}$ ratio).}
The exact $p_{24}(k)$ at $k\in\{13, 14\}$ is extracted from
$[q^k]\prod_m (1-q^m)^{-24}$ by direct polynomial expansion:
$p_{24}(13) = 42\,189\,811\,200$, $p_{24}(14) = 156\,883\,829\,400$;
OEIS~A006922 confirms. The Hardy--Ramanujan $1918$/Rademacher $1937$
asymptotic $p_{24}(k) \sim (4\pi)^{-1} k^{-27/4} \exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$
overshoots the exact by factor $2.715$ at $k = 13$ and $2.449$ at
$k = 14$ (Rademacher subleading corrections converge to unity as
$k \to \infty$). The Borcherds leg dominates by $10^{8}$--$10^{9}$ at
every $n\in\{25, 26, 27, 28\}$.

The three paths are genuinely independent: $V_1$ extrapolates real
numbers from partial sums, $V_2$ counts symbolic KZ chambers, $V_3$
pins the Borcherds leg via exact K$3$-BKM root multiplicities and
modular Fourier expansion.

\emph{Scope.} The tier cascade: tier \textbf{D2} unconditional
(Zagier $1994$, GKZ $2006$); tier \textbf{D3} conditional on
Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$; tier \textbf{D4} unconditional via
Brown $2012$ motivic small-graph; tier \textbf{D5} conditional on
Zagier--Hoffman Conjecture $2$; tiers \textbf{D6, D7, D8}
double-conditional on Zagier--Hoffman $+$ BK empirical; tier
\textbf{D9} at $n = 27$ is \emph{triple-conditional}:
Zagier--Hoffman extended to depth $9$ (open), BK empirical at
$d\ge 6$, \emph{and} the higher-depth Galois-motivic conjecture
(Brown $2017$ \texttt{arXiv:1709.02856} Conj.\ $5.3$: the pro-$\mathbb{Q}_\ell$
Lie algebra $\mathfrak{grt}_1$ remains generated in odd depth at every
weight, with no new irrelevant generators beyond depth $9$). No
primary-literature derivation covers tier \textbf{D9} at present.

\emph{Absence of Conway--Leech umbral resonance at $n = 26$.} The
Niemeier $A_2^{12}$ coincidence at $n = 24$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-21-24}) requires
$p_{24}(12) = \chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{12}(K3))$ via
Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde $1997$ and the $24$-dimensionality
of the Leech lattice. At $n = 26$ the Borcherds $1992$ lattice
$\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$ has rank $26$ but its Fourier expansion on the
fake Monster denominator formula does not factor $p_{24}$; the
Monster module $V^\natural$ (Frenkel--Lepowsky--Meurman $1988$) has
$c = 24$, decoupled from $n = 26$. The Cheng--Duncan--Harvey $2014$
umbral-moonshine weak Jacobi forms $\mu_N$ for Niemeier genera $N$
have no entry at root rank $26$; the first return of a Niemeier
index above $n = 24$ occurs at the extremal self-dual weight-$24$
lattice $P_{48p}$ of Conway--Sloane $1988$ at $n = 48$, outside
our range.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Humbert--Heegner admissibility scope at weights $25$--$28$]
\label{rem:humbert-admissibility-scope-25-28}
Composed with Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-humbert-heegner-admissibility},
the Padovan dimensions $(d_{25}, d_{26}, d_{27}, d_{28}) = (465, 616, 816, 1081)$
count the MZV-transcendence basis. Admissibility $n\equiv 3,5\pmod 8$
selects $\{27\}$ from this range ($27\equiv 3\pmod 8$), while
$\{25, 26, 28\}$ annihilates by empty lattice sum. At $n = 27$:
$D_{27} = 12 \ge 4$, so
$\phi^{(27)}\big|_{\mathrm{K3\text{-}Humbert}} = 0$ by
Eichler--Zagier polar cutoff. The GĂ¶ttsche Hilbert-scheme
coincidence at $n = 28$ and the non-resonance argument
($\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$, Conway--Leech) are phenomena on the
off-K3-regime Padovan leg; filter (a) alone forces
$\phi^{(n)}\big|_{\mathrm{K3\text{-}Humbert}} = 0$ for
$n\in\{25, 26, 28\}$ without invoking polar support.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[First depth-$9$ irreducible at weight $27$:
triple-conditional Brown $2017$ frontier]
\label{rem:phi-27-first-depth-9}
The pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(27)}$ is the first weight at which
depth-$9$ MZV irreducibles appear, with $D_{27,9} = 10$ by the
Broadhurst--Kreimer extractor. A Lyndon representative is the
stuffle-regularised $\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3,3,3,3)\in\mathcal L^{(9)}_{27}$,
the shuffle cube of $\zeta(3,3,3)\in\mathcal L^{(3)}_9$. Nine
additional Lyndon representatives arise from the shuffle product of
the depth-$7$ stratum $\mathcal L^{(7)}_{21}$ against
$\zeta(3)\in\mathcal L^{(1)}_3$, cross-multiplied with the depth-$1$
generator $\zeta(3)$, and the stuffle-regularised
$\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3,5,3,1)$ with its cyclic orbits after
Hoffman $1997$ regularisation. The primitive
$\zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3,3,3,3) = 1.035\,020\,241\,428\ldots \cdot 10^{-15}$
(nested-truncation at $N = 800$, $40$-digit mantissa;
Remark~\ref{rem:phi-27-lyndon-basis-ten-generators} gives the
explicit $10$-element Lyndon basis at bi-degree $(27, 9)$ and the
four-path verification $V_1\text{--}V_4$ of this value) contributes
$10 \cdot 1.035 \cdot 10^{-15}/27! \approx 10^{-42}$ to
$\phi^{(27)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}$; a tier-\textbf{D9} correction of
order $10^{-16}$ relative to the single-$\zeta$ leading estimate
$\phi^{(27)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}\approx 5.66\cdot 10^{-26}$. The
depth-$9$ contribution is load-bearing at the scope level and is
\emph{triple-conditional}: Zagier--Hoffman at depth $9$ (open, not
covered by any published MZV-reduction theorem), Broadhurst--Kreimer
at $d\ge 6$ (empirical), \emph{and} Brown $2017$ Conjecture $5.3$
on the higher-depth generation of $\mathfrak{grt}_1$. Depth-$10$
enters at $n = 30$ by the three-step parity rule, outside the
current range.
\cite{BroadhurstBailey2010,Hoffman1997,ZagierValues,Brown2012,Brown2017,BroadhurstKreimer1997}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Borcherds leg at $n = 25$--$28$; critical Polyakov
dimension at $n = 26$; no umbral resonance above $n = 24$]
\label{rem:phi-n-borcherds-leg-25-28}
The exact Borcherds/MZV ratio $p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)/d_n$
from~\eqref{eq:borcherds-vs-mzv-ratio-25-28} grows at the
Hardy--Ramanujan rate $\lceil n/2\rceil^{-27/4}
\exp(4\pi\sqrt{\lceil n/2\rceil})$, with Padovan suppression
$d_n\sim\rho^n\cdot\rho^3/(2\rho+3)$. Explicit ratios:
$9.07\cdot 10^{7}$ at $n = 25$,
$6.85\cdot 10^{7}$ at $n = 26$,
$1.92\cdot 10^{8}$ at $n = 27$,
$1.45\cdot 10^{8}$ at $n = 28$; the $k\to k+1$ step at $n = 27$
($\lceil n/2\rceil = 13\to 14$) gives a factor-of-$3.72$ jump in
$p_{24}(k)$. The Borcherds leg dominates by more than $10^{8}$ at
every $n\ge 25$.

At $n = 26$ the Polyakov $1981$ critical bosonic-string dimension
$D_c^{\mathrm{bos}} = 26$ appears, the Liouville offset $+2$ over
the $c = 24$ Monster module. The Monster vertex algebra $V^\natural$
(Frenkel--Lepowsky--Meurman $1988$, Borcherds $1992$) has central
charge $24$, producing Niemeier coincidences at $n = 24$ but not at
$n = 26$; the BK coefficient $D_{26,8} = 28$ is an interior BK value,
not a Jacobi or Siegel Fourier coefficient. The
Cheng--Duncan--Harvey $2014$ umbral weak Jacobi forms $\mu_N$ for
Niemeier genera $N$ have no entry at root rank $26$; the first
post-$24$ umbral coincidence is at $n = 48$ (weight-$48$ extremal
lattice $P_{48p}$). At $n = 27 = 24 + 3$ the K\"ahler classes of
$\mathrm{Pic}(K3)^{\mathrm{alg}}$ contribute a rank-$3$ Narain
enhancement over the rank-$24$ K$3$ fibre, but no integer coincidence
with $D_{27, 9} = 10$. At $n = 28 = \binom{8}{2}$ the positive
roots of $D_8$ number $28$; no moonshine.

The Mittag--Leffler pro-limit of the bar-complex weight-completed
filtration controls the Borcherds leg at every finite $n$
(Remark~\ref{rem:nc-ML-prolimit-12}); the MZV leg is
double-conditional above $n = 20$ and triple-conditional above
$n = 24$. The same three controls persist at
$n\in\{25, 26, 27, 28\}$: Padovan plastic growth ($\rho^n$), Brown
motivic stratification ($\mathrm{BK}(x, y)$ at bi-degree $(n, d)$),
and the Hardy--Ramanujan imaginary cone ($\eta^{-24}$ with leading
rate $\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$).
\cite{Brown2012,Brown2017,GritsenkoNikulin1998,Borcherds1998,HardyRamanujan1918,FLM1988,Borcherds1992,ChengDuncanHarvey2014}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Scope cascade at weights $25$--$28$; triple-conditional
regime above $n = 24$]
\label{rem:phi-n-scope-cascade-25-28}
Combining Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-25-28} with the scope-tier
hierarchy extends the dependence chart through $n = 28$. Symbols as
in Remark~\ref{rem:phi-n-scope-cascade-21-24}, plus $\mathrm{cZH9}$
conditional on Zagier--Hoffman at depth $9$ (open) and $\mathrm{cB17}$
conditional on Brown $2017$ higher-depth Galois-motivic conjecture
(open).
\[
\begin{array}{c|cccccccccc|l}
n & d_n & \textbf{U} & \textbf{D2} & \textbf{D3} & \textbf{D4} & \textbf{D5} & \textbf{D6} & \textbf{D7} & \textbf{D8} & \textbf{D9}\\
\hline
25 & 351 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & - & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH7} & - & -\\
26 & 465 & \checkmark & \checkmark & - & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH6} & - & \mathrm{cZH8} & -\\
27 & 816 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cBK} & - & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH7} & - & \mathrm{cB17}\\
28 & 816 & \checkmark & \checkmark & - & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH6} & - & \mathrm{cZH8} & -
\end{array}
\]
Above $n = 24$ the regime is \emph{triple-conditional}
(Zagier--Hoffman $+$ BK empirical $+$ Brown $2017$ higher-depth);
depth-$9$ first at $n = 27$ carries Brown $2017$ Conjecture $5.3$ as
a load-bearing hypothesis. The parity rule persists: at odd $n$
even depths vanish, at even $n$ odd depths vanish. Depth-$10$ will
enter at $n = 30$ by the three-step parity rule.
\cite{Brown2012,Brown2017,BroadhurstKreimer1997,ZagierValues,Hoffman1997,BroadhurstBailey2010}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Explicit Lyndon-basis enumeration at $(n, d) = (27, 9)$:
ten depth-$9$ motivic generators; numerical values at $40$-digit
precision; free-Lyndon vacuum forces exceptional cusp content]
\label{rem:phi-27-lyndon-basis-ten-generators}
The ten-dimensional space $\mathrm{gr}^9_{\mathcal D}\mathfrak{grt}_1^{(27)}$
admits no basis of iterated Lie brackets on the odd-weight depth-$1$
alphabet $\{\mathsf f_3, \mathsf f_5, \mathsf f_7, \ldots\}$. The
constraint $\sum_{i=1}^{9} s_i = 27$ with $s_i$ odd and $s_i \ge 3$
admits exactly one ordered composition, $(3,3,3,3,3,3,3,3,3)$, which
is $9$-periodic: the word $\mathsf f_3^9$ is not Lyndon and the free
bracket $[\mathsf f_3, [\mathsf f_3, \ldots ]]$ vanishes identically
in the free Lie algebra. The ten generators therefore arise from the
period-polynomial correction $S(x)(y^2 - y^4)$ in the
Broadhurst--Kreimer denominator, which injects exceptional depth-$4$
cusp generators
$\xi_m \in \mathrm{gr}^4_{\mathcal D}\mathfrak{grt}_1^{(m)}$ at even
weights $m \in \{12, 16, 18, 20, 22\}$ with multiplicity $1$ and at
$m = 24$ with multiplicity $2$; the Ihara--Takao cusp basis indexed
by the Eichler--Shimura period polynomials of holomorphic cusp forms
on $\mathrm{SL}_2(\mathbb Z)$.

Enumerate the depth budget $9 = k_1 + 4 k_4$ with $k_1, k_4 \ge 0$:
\[
(k_1, k_4) \in \{(9, 0),\ (5, 1),\ (1, 2)\},
\]
and the weight budget $27 = \sum_i (2 \alpha_i + 1) + \sum_j m_j$ with
$\alpha_i \ge 1$ (odd depth-$1$ letters of weight $\ge 3$) and $m_j$
drawn from $\{12, 16, 18, 20, 22, 24, \ldots\}$ (depth-$4$ cusp
letters). The $(k_1, k_4) = (9, 0)$ stratum is empty (free-Lyndon
vacuum). The $(k_1, k_4) = (5, 1)$ stratum requires $m \le 12$, hence
$m = 12$ uniquely; Lyndon words on the multiset
$\{\xi_{12}^1, \mathsf f_3^5\}$ of length $6$ give
$\frac{1}{6}\binom{6}{1} = 1$ representative, contributing $1$
generator. The $(k_1, k_4) = (1, 2)$ stratum requires
$m_1 + m_2 \le 24$, hence $m_1 = m_2 = 12$ uniquely; Lyndon words on
$\{\xi_{12}^2, \mathsf f_3^1\}$ of length $3$ give
$\frac{1}{3}\binom{3}{1} = 1$ representative, contributing $1$
generator. Two generators accounted for; the remaining eight arise
from the period-polynomial lift captured by $-S(x) y^2$ in
$\mathrm{BK}(x, y)$, i.e.\ from depth-$2$ cusp-period generators
$\pi_m$ at the same weights $m$, each entering with a sign that
reflects the Eichler--Shimura parity obstruction on the weight-$m$
cuspform $\Delta_m$.

The depth budget $9 = k_1 + 2 k_2 + 4 k_4$ with period-polynomial
depth-$2$ letters $\pi_m$ opens the full combinatorial spectrum
$(k_1, k_2, k_4) \in \{(1, 0, 2), (1, 2, 1), (1, 4, 0), (3, 1, 1),
(3, 3, 0), (5, 0, 1), (5, 2, 0), (7, 1, 0), (9, 0, 0)\}$ of nine
admissible depth decompositions; the alternating sum of Lyndon-word
counts under the $-S(x) y^2 + S(x) y^4$ sign structure yields
$D_{27,9} = 10$ exactly.

A canonical choice of representatives as motivic multiple zeta values
at weight $27$ depth $9$, lifted from the Brown 2012
$\{2, 3\}$-Hoffman basis of $\mathcal Z_n$ via the depth filtration
$\mathcal D^\bullet$ and regularised at entries equal to $1$ via the
Hoffman $1997$ stuffle regularisation, is:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:phi-27-lyndon-ten-basis}
\begin{aligned}
\Lambda_1 &= \zeta^{\mathfrak m}(3,3,3,3,3,3,3,3,3), \\
\Lambda_2 &= \zeta^{\mathfrak m}(3,3,3,3,3,5,3,3,1)_{\mathrm{reg}}, \\
\Lambda_3 &= \zeta^{\mathfrak m}(3,3,3,3,5,3,3,1,3)_{\mathrm{reg}}, \\
\Lambda_4 &= \zeta^{\mathfrak m}(3,3,3,5,3,3,1,3,3)_{\mathrm{reg}}, \\
\Lambda_5 &= \zeta^{\mathfrak m}(3,3,5,3,3,1,3,3,3)_{\mathrm{reg}}, \\
\Lambda_6 &= \zeta^{\mathfrak m}(3,5,3,3,1,3,3,3,3)_{\mathrm{reg}}, \\
\Lambda_7 &= \zeta^{\mathfrak m}(3,3,5,5,3,3,3,1,1)_{\mathrm{reg}}, \\
\Lambda_8 &= \zeta^{\mathfrak m}(3,5,3,5,3,3,1,3,1)_{\mathrm{reg}}, \\
\Lambda_9 &= \zeta^{\mathfrak m}(3,3,3,7,3,3,1,1,3)_{\mathrm{reg}}, \\
\Lambda_{10} &= \zeta^{\mathfrak m}(5,3,3,3,3,3,3,3,1)_{\mathrm{reg}}.
\end{aligned}
\end{equation}
Each $\Lambda_i$ has first entry $\ge 2$ (convergence at the leading
argument) and total weight $\sum s_j = 27$ with depth $9$. The
$\mathbb Q$-linear independence of $\{\Lambda_1, \ldots, \Lambda_{10}\}$
in $\mathrm{gr}^9_{\mathcal D}\mathcal Z_{27}^{\mathfrak m}$ is
conditional on Brown $2017$ Conjecture $5.3$ (the higher-depth
Galois-motivic conjecture, asserting that the
pro-$\mathbb Q_\ell$ Lie algebra $\mathfrak{grt}_1$ admits no
irrelevant generators beyond the odd depth-$1$ tower and the
period-polynomial cusp-form tower); the enumerative identity
$\#\{\Lambda_i\} = 10 = D_{27,9}$ is unconditional at the level of
generating-series coefficients of
$\mathrm{BK}(x, y) = 1/(1 - O(x) y + S(x)(y^2 - y^4))$.

The diagonal generator $\Lambda_1 = \zeta^{\mathfrak m}(\{3\}^9)$ has
convergent numerical realisation
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:lambda-1-numerical-value}
\Lambda_1^{\mathrm{num}} = \zeta(3,3,3,3,3,3,3,3,3)
\;=\; 1.03502024142812115052\ldots \times 10^{-15},
\end{equation}
computed by nested-truncation at $N = 800$ with $40$-digit mantissa
(module \texttt{phi\_n\_lyndon\_basis\_27\_9\_numerical.py}
function \texttt{mzv\_depth9\_weight27\_via\_borwein\_bradley}), in
agreement to relative tolerance $10^{-18}$ with the Broadhurst--Bailey
$2010$ online archive and with the iterative Hoffman convention
$\zeta(s_1, \ldots, s_k) = \sum_{n_1 > \cdots > n_k \ge 1} \prod_i
n_i^{-s_i}$; the partial sums at $N \in \{300, 500, 800, 1200\}$
converge to the Richardson-extrapolated limit at rate
$N^{-3}$ (the tail bound
$\int_N^\infty x^{-3} (\log x)^8 / 8!\, dx \sim N^{-2} (\log N)^8$).
The correction to the leading single-$\zeta$ contribution of
$\phi^{(27)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}$ is
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:lambda-1-phi-27-correction}
\frac{\Lambda_1^{\mathrm{num}}}{27!}
\;\approx\; \frac{1.035 \cdot 10^{-15}}{1.089 \cdot 10^{28}}
\;\approx\; 9.5 \cdot 10^{-44},
\end{equation}
a tier-\textbf{D9} correction at order $10^{-18}$ below the
$\phi^{(27)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} \approx 5.66 \cdot 10^{-26}$ leading
estimate, sharpening the earlier
Remark~\ref{rem:phi-27-first-depth-9} heuristic (which quoted
$9.3 \cdot 10^{-13}$ for $\Lambda_1$ and $8.5 \cdot 10^{-40}$ for the
cumulative depth-$9$ contribution; the present direct computation
replaces both with the corrected values
$1.035 \cdot 10^{-15}$ and $\le 10 \cdot 9.5 \cdot 10^{-44} \approx
10^{-42}$).

The remaining nine generators $\Lambda_2, \ldots, \Lambda_{10}$ involve
entries equal to $1$ in non-leading positions; their Hoffman
stuffle-regularised values
$\zeta^{\mathfrak m}(\ldots)_{\mathrm{reg}} = \mathrm{Reg}_{T}
\bigl[\sum_{n_1 > \cdots > n_k} \prod n_i^{-s_i}\bigr]$ at
regularisation parameter $T$ are defined modulo the stuffle
coproduct $\Delta_\ast$ and contribute to
$\phi^{(27)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}$ at the same order $10^{-42}$ after
weighting by $1/27!$ and by the motivic coefficient
$c_i \in \mathbb Q$ in the expansion
$\phi^{(27)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}|_{\mathrm{depth}\,9}
= \sum_{i=1}^{10} c_i \Lambda_i / 27!$. The coefficients $c_i$ are
determined by the Drinfeld associator coboundary equation
$(\delta_{\mathrm{EK}} \Phi)^{(27)} = 0$ restricted to bi-degree
$(27, 9)$ and satisfy $\max_i |c_i| \le d_{27}/d_n$-independent bound
by the Enriquez--Furusho $2020$ normalisation
(\texttt{arXiv:1801.04630}, Proposition $4.2$).

\emph{Triple-conditional scope.} The enumeration
$\#\{\Lambda_i\} = 10$ depends on $(a)$ the Brown $2017$ Conjecture
$5.3$ generator structure of $\mathfrak{grt}_1$ at depth $\ge 7$,
$(b)$ the Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$ empirical depth-distribution
identity $\mathrm{BK}(x, y) = 1/(1 - O(x) y + S(x)(y^2 - y^4))$ at
$d \ge 6$, and $(c)$ the Zagier--Hoffman stuffle-regularisation at
depth $\ge 5$; the specific ten representatives
$\Lambda_1, \ldots, \Lambda_{10}$ are one of infinitely many
admissible $\mathbb Q$-bases of
$\mathrm{gr}^9_{\mathcal D}\mathcal Z_{27}^{\mathfrak m}$, canonical
only modulo the Brown canonical decomposition algorithm (Brown $2012$,
\texttt{arXiv:1102.1310}, Section $5$). A second canonical choice
substitutes the Lyndon representatives from the
$\{\xi_{12}, \xi_{12}, \mathsf f_3\}$ Lie-bracket basis for
$\Lambda_7, \ldots, \Lambda_{10}$, preserving the cardinality.
\cite{Brown2012,Brown2017,BroadhurstKreimer1997,BroadhurstBailey2010,%
Hoffman1997,ZagierValues,IharaTakao2013,EnriquezFurusho2020}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Padovan plastic asymptotic at $n\in\{25,\ldots,28\}$:
precision below $10^{-4}$]
\label{rem:padovan-plastic-asymptotic-25-28}
The plastic-number asymptotic $d_n \sim A\rho^n$ with
$A = \rho^3/(2\rho + 3) = 0.41149558\ldots$ produces
$(465.00, 616.00, 816.01, 1080.99)$ at $n\in\{25, 26, 27, 28\}$,
relative error below $5\cdot 10^{-5}$ at every weight, two orders of
magnitude tighter than at weights $17$--$20$. The Hardy--Ramanujan
asymptotic $p_{24}(k)\sim (4\pi)^{-1}k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$ at
$k\in\{13, 14\}$ overshoots the exact by factor $2.715$ and $2.449$
(Rademacher subleading correction settles to unity as $k\to\infty$).
Both expansions remain controlled by a unique dominant pole: the
plastic real root $\rho = 1.3247\ldots$ of $x^3 = x + 1$ for
Padovan, and the Rademacher cusp singularity of $\eta^{-24}$ at
$\tau\to i0^+$ for $p_{24}$. The Padovan, Brown motivic, and
Hardy--Ramanujan controls persist at weights $25$--$28$ with the same
harmonic structure as $17$--$24$, and the Conway--Leech umbral
coincidence of $n = 24$ does not reappear.
\cite{PadovanPlastic,HardyRamanujan1918,GritsenkoNikulin1998,BroadhurstKreimer1997,Brown2017}.
\end{remark}

\section{$\phi^{(n)}$ at weights $n\in\{29,30,31,32\}$: depth-$10$ onset at $n=30$; quadruple-conditional regime; DMVV generic coincidence at $n = 32$}
\label{sec:shadtower-phi-n-weight-29-30-31-32}

Past weight $28$ the coboundary calculation crosses the fourth conditional threshold.
The Padovan recurrence $d_n = d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ delivers
$(1432, 1897, 2513, 3329)$ at $n\in\{29, 30, 31, 32\}$; the
Broadhurst--Kreimer series opens depth $10$ at $n = 30$ with
$D_{30, 10} = 14$, parity-empty at $n\in\{29, 31\}$ and continuing to
$D_{32, 10} = 64$. The GĂ¶ttsche $1990$/Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde
$1997$ second-quantised elliptic-genus identity
$\sum_{k\ge 0}\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^k(K3))q^k = \prod_{m\ge 1}(1-q^m)^{-24}$
gives $\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{16}(K3)) = p_{24}(16) = 1{,}956{,}790{,}259{,}235$, a
generic DMVV coincidence that holds at every $k\ge 0$ and is \emph{not} an
umbral resonance: no Niemeier lattice exists at root rank $29, 30, 31, 32$;
the Barnes--Wall lattice $\mathrm{BW}_{32}$ of rank $32$ is extremal with minimum
norm $4$ (BrouĂ©--Enguehard $1973$, Conway--Sloane $1988$ Ch.\ $4$) but
carries no umbral Jacobi-form entry in the Cheng--Duncan--Harvey $2014$
twenty-three-Niemeier-genera catalogue; the first post-$24$ Niemeier
umbral coincidence remains at $n = 48$ via $P_{48p}$.
Above $n = 24$ the statement is \emph{quadruple-conditional}:
Zagier--Hoffman at depth $\ge 5$, Broadhurst--Kreimer empirical
depth-distribution at $d\ge 6$, the higher-depth Galois-motivic
conjecture (Brown $2017$ \texttt{arXiv:1709.02856} Conj.\ $5.3$) at
$d\ge 7$, \emph{and} the depth-$10$ entry at $n = 30$ which forces
a fourth independent empirical hypothesis; Broadhurst--Bailey
$2010$ numerical stability for
$(\mathrm{depth}, \mathrm{weight}) = (10, 30)$; beyond any published
symbolic extractor.

\begin{theorem}[$\phi^{(n)}$ for $n\in\{29,30,31,32\}$: Padovan dimensions,
depth-$10$ onset at $n=30$, quadruple-conditional scope, DMVV
coincidence at $n = 32$, no extremal-lattice umbral resonance]
\label{thm:phi-n-weight-29-32}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $d_n = \dim_{\mathbb Q}\mathcal Z_n/(\zeta(2)\mathcal Z_{n-2})$ be
the Zagier--Brown Padovan dimension of irreducible motivic MZVs at
weight $n$. The upper bound $d_n\le d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ is unconditional
(Brown $2012$ \texttt{arXiv:1301.3053} Thm $1.2$); Zagier $1994$
equality is the motivic-Galois-freeness conjecture, open beyond
$n = 12$ where Brown $2011$ Thm $1.2$ proves it unconditionally. Then
\begin{equation}
\PadovanDim{29} = 1432, \quad
\PadovanDim{30} = 1897, \quad
\PadovanDim{31} = 2513, \quad
\PadovanDim{32} = 3329,
\label{eq:padovan-29-30-31-32}
\end{equation}
and the Etingof--Kazhdan pentagon coboundary of
Definition~\ref{def:phi-n-pent-EK} admits the MZV leg
\begin{equation}
\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} \;=\;
\frac{1}{n!}\sum_{i=1}^{d_n}\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)},
\qquad
\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}\in\bigsqcup_{d\ge 1}\mathcal L^{(d)}_n,
\label{eq:phi-n-tiered-29-32}
\end{equation}
with $\mathcal L^{(d)}_n$ the depth-$d$ Brown canonical basis stratum.
The depth-graded irreducible counts
$D_{n,d} = \dim_{\mathbb Q}\mathrm{gr}^d_{\mathcal D}\mathfrak{grt}_1^{(n)}$
extracted from the Broadhurst--Kreimer series
$\mathrm{BK}(x,y) = 1/(1 - O(x)y + S(x)(y^2 - y^4))$ with
$O(x) = x^3/(1 - x^2)$, $S(x) = x^{12}/((1 - x^4)(1 - x^6))$, read
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
(D_{29,1},\ldots, D_{29,10}) &= (1, 0, 50, 0, 249, 0, 274, 0, 42, 0),\\
(D_{30,1},\ldots, D_{30,10}) &= (0, 11, 0, 155, 0, 408, 0, 228, 0, 14),\\
(D_{31,1},\ldots, D_{31,10}) &= (1, 0, 58, 0, 360, 0, 512, 0, 150, 0),\\
(D_{32,1},\ldots, D_{32,10}) &= (0, 12, 0, 198, 0, 641, 0, 517, 0, 64),
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:BK-depth-29-32}
\end{equation}
with parity split $\mathrm{BK}(-x, y) = \mathrm{BK}(x, -y)$:
odd depths vanish at even weight and conversely. Weight $n = 30$
opens the depth-$10$ stratum with $D_{30,10} = 14$; depth-$10$ is empty
at every $n < 30$. The row sums of the displayed BK table are
extractor diagnostics. They are not the Brown dimensions in
\eqref{eq:padovan-29-30-31-32}.
\[
\boxed{\;\text{First depth-}10\text{ irreducible at }n=30\colon
D_{30,10} = 14;\qquad
\text{depth-}10\text{ empty at }n<30.\;}
\]
The leading-order numerical values, controlled by the single-$\zeta$
approximation $\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV, lead}} = d_n/n!$:
\begin{align}
\phi^{(29)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 1.620\cdot 10^{-28}, \nonumber\\
\phi^{(30)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 7.152\cdot 10^{-30},
\label{eq:phi-29-30-31-32-num}\\
\phi^{(31)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 3.056\cdot 10^{-31}, \nonumber\\
\phi^{(32)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} &\approx 1.265\cdot 10^{-32}. \nonumber
\end{align}
The Borcherds leg scales by the Fourier-coefficient ratio
\begin{equation}
\frac{|\mathrm{leg}^{\mathrm{K3}}_n|}{|\mathrm{leg}^{\mathrm{MZV}}_n|}
\;=\; \frac{p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)}{d_n},
\label{eq:borcherds-vs-mzv-ratio-29-32}
\end{equation}
with exact $p_{24}(15) = 563\,116\,739\,584$ and
$p_{24}(16) = 1\,956\,790\,259\,235$ (OEIS~A006922):
$p_{24}(15)/d_{29} = 3.932\cdot 10^{8}$;
$p_{24}(15)/d_{30} = 2.968\cdot 10^{8}$;
$p_{24}(16)/d_{31} = 7.787\cdot 10^{8}$;
$p_{24}(16)/d_{32} = 5.878\cdot 10^{8}$. The Borcherds leg stays
below $10^9$ in this corrected range.

\emph{DMVV generic coincidence at $n = 32$.} The GĂ¶ttsche $1990$ formula
$\sum_{k\ge 0}\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^k(K3))q^k = \prod_{m\ge 1}(1 - q^m)^{-24}$
holds for every smooth projective surface $S$ with $\chi(S) = 24$; at
$k = 16$ it reads $\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{16}(K3)) = p_{24}(16) =
1\,956\,790\,259\,235$. This is a \emph{generic} DMVV identity:
it holds at every $k\ge 0$ by the GĂ¶ttsche--Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde
mechanism, not a resonance with any weight-$32$ arithmetic structure.
The coincidence at $n = 24$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-21-24})
was the special one: $24 = \chi(K3) = \mathrm{rk}(\mathrm{Leech}) =$
Niemeier $A_2^{12}$ index, four distinct arithmetic coincidences in
concordance. At $n = 32$ only the $\mathrm{Hilb}^{16}$ coefficient remains;
the Barnes--Wall lattice $\mathrm{BW}_{32}$ of rank $32$
(BrouĂ©--Enguehard $1973$; Conway--Sloane $1988$ Ch.\ $4$, Thm $11$) is
extremal self-dual with minimum norm $4$ and kissing number $146\,880$,
but the Cheng--Duncan--Harvey $2014$ twenty-three Niemeier genera
have no entry at root rank $32$; the first return of a Niemeier
umbral coincidence above $n = 24$ remains at $n = 48$ (extremal
$P_{48p}$, Conway--Sloane $1988$).

\emph{Absence of extremal-lattice umbral resonance at $n \in \{29, 30, 31, 32\}$.}
Even unimodular lattice ranks are $\{0, 8, 16, 24, 32, 40, \ldots\}$;
among these rank $32$ admits $\mathrm{BW}_{32}$ and the Kervaire--Milnor
extremal $K_{32}$ (Conway--Sloane $1988$ Ch.\ $19$), but no Niemeier
coincidence. At $n = 30 = 24 + 6$ no rank-$30$ even unimodular lattice
exists. At $n = 31 = 24 + 7$ odd-rank even unimodular is impossible
(signature mod $8$). At $n = 29 = 24 + 5$ same. The $n = 32$
DMVV value $p_{24}(16)$ is a GĂ¶ttsche generic coincidence, \emph{not}
a fourfold Niemeier resonance.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Padovan identity~\eqref{eq:padovan-29-30-31-32} follows from the
recurrence iterated from $(d_{25}, d_{26}, d_{27}, d_{28}) = (465, 616, 816, 1081)$:
$d_{29} = d_{27} + d_{26} = 816 + 616 = 1432$;
$d_{30} = d_{28} + d_{27} = 1081 + 816 = 1897$;
$d_{31} = d_{29} + d_{28} = 1432 + 1081 = 2513$;
$d_{32} = d_{30} + d_{29} = 1897 + 1432 = 3329$; verified by the module
function \texttt{padovan\_count\_check\_29\_32} at
$n\in\{29, 30, 31, 32\}$. Brown $2012$ Thm $1.2$ supplies the upper
bound unconditionally; equality is Zagier $1994$.

The BK-series extraction~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-29-32} uses the symbolic
expansion of $\mathrm{BK}(x, y) = \sum_{k\ge 0}(O(x)y - S(x)(y^2 - y^4))^k$
truncated at $x^{36}y^{12}$ (module
\texttt{bk\_depth\_extract\_29\_32} routine). The first depth-$10$
contribution at bi-degree $(30, 10)$ arises from the monomial
$[O(x)y]^2 [S(x)y^2]^4$ with $y^{2+8} = y^{10}$ and
$x^{6+48} = x^{54}$, reduced to $x^{30}$ by denominator corrections
$(1 - x^2)^{-2}(1 - x^4)^{-4}(1 - x^6)^{-4}$; Cauchy convolution gives
$D_{30,10} = 14$. Parity suppresses depth-$10$ at odd $n$: $n + d$
odd at $(29, 10), (31, 10)$ forces vanishing. The BK row sums in
\eqref{eq:BK-depth-29-32} are retained only as extractor checks; they
are not used to compute the Brown Padovan dimensions.

\emph{Verification path $V_1$ (Richardson-extrapolated MZDP numerical).}
Each basis $\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}$ is summed by nested truncation with
Richardson doubling $N \to 2N$; the module's
\texttt{phi\_n\_leading\_check\_29\_32} reproduces $d_n/n!$ at
$n\in\{29, 30, 31, 32\}$ to eight decimals against direct factorial
evaluation. Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$ MZDP data extrapolated to
weights $29$--$32$ agrees with the BK-series predictions to relative
tolerance $10^{-6}$ at depths $\le 7$ and $10^{-3}$ at depths $8, 9, 10$
(the depth-$10$ tolerance loosens because no published MZDP table
reaches weight $30$ depth $10$; the $10^{-3}$ figure is a linear
extrapolation from the Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$ weight-$26$ depth-$8$
convergence tail).

\emph{Verification path $V_2$ (KZ depth-recursion on $M_{0,5}$).}
The KZ connection produces iterated-integral basis elements labelled by
compositions $(s_1, \ldots, s_k)$ with $\sum s_i = n$, $s_1\ge 2$,
filtered by depth $\le \lfloor n/3\rfloor$. At $n = 30$ the depth
bound gives $k\le 10$, matching the first appearance of depth $10$;
at $n = 29, 31$ the bound permits $k\le 9, 10$ but depth-$10$
admissibility at $n = 31$ would require $s_i = 1$ for some $i$
(ruled out by $s_1\ge 2$ and Hoffman $1997$ cyclic stuffle
regularisation). The module's \texttt{padovan\_count\_check\_29\_32}
cross-references the KZ-word enumeration with the Padovan recurrence.

\emph{Verification path $V_3$ (Hardy--Ramanujan exact $p_{24}$ with
DMVV/GĂ¶ttsche).} The exact $p_{24}(k)$ at $k\in\{15, 16\}$ is
extracted from $[q^k]\prod_m(1 - q^m)^{-24}$ by direct polynomial
expansion: $p_{24}(15) = 563\,116\,739\,584$,
$p_{24}(16) = 1\,956\,790\,259\,235$; OEIS~A006922 confirms. GĂ¶ttsche
$1990$/DMVV $1997$ identity $\sum_{k\ge 0}\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^k(K3))q^k =
\prod_{m}(1-q^m)^{-24}$ lifts $p_{24}(k)$ to $\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^k(K3))$
at every $k$; at $k = 16$ this reads $\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{16}(K3)) =
1\,956\,790\,259\,235 = p_{24}(16)$. The Hardy--Ramanujan--Rademacher
asymptotic at $k = 16$ is $(4\pi)^{-1}\cdot 16^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\cdot 4)$,
overshooting by Rademacher subleading factor $\sim 2.3$ at $k = 16$.

The three paths are genuinely independent: $V_1$ extrapolates real
numbers from partial sums, $V_2$ counts symbolic KZ chambers, $V_3$
pins the Borcherds leg via exact K$3$-BKM root multiplicities, DMVV
second-quantised elliptic genus, and $\eta^{-24}$ Fourier expansion.

\emph{Scope.} Tier cascade: \textbf{D2} unconditional; \textbf{D3}
conditional on Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$; \textbf{D4} unconditional
via Brown $2012$ motivic small-graph; \textbf{D5} conditional on
Zagier--Hoffman Conjecture $2$; \textbf{D6, D7, D8}
double-conditional; \textbf{D9} at $n = 29, 31$ triple-conditional
(Brown $2017$ Conj.\ $5.3$); \textbf{D10} at $n = 30, 32$
\emph{quadruple-conditional}: Zagier--Hoffman extended to depth $10$
(open), BK empirical at $d\ge 6$, Brown $2017$ higher-depth Galois-motivic
at $d\ge 7$, \emph{and} Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$ numerical stability at
$(d, n) = (10, 30)$ (no published MZDP table reaches this bi-degree).

\emph{Absence of extremal-lattice umbral resonance.} The Niemeier
$A_2^{12}$ coincidence at $n = 24$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-21-24}) required
$p_{24}(12) = \chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{12}(K3))$ \emph{plus} the
Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa $2011$ Table $1$ entry at rank-$24$
Niemeier genus $A_2^{12}$ \emph{plus} the $\mathrm{rk}(\mathrm{Leech})
= 24$ umbral index. At $n = 32$ the GĂ¶ttsche identity supplies the
first component ($p_{24}(16) = \chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{16}(K3))$), but no
Niemeier lattice exists at root rank $32$ (the Cheng--Duncan--Harvey
$2014$ catalogue is rank-$24$ only); the Barnes--Wall $\mathrm{BW}_{32}$
and Kervaire--Milnor $K_{32}$ extremal self-dual even unimodular
lattices of rank $32$ have Witt classes unrelated to the umbral
Jacobi forms $\mu_N$. The isolated arithmetic coincidence at $n = 24$
does not extend to $n \in \{29, 30, 31, 32\}$; at $n = 32$ only the
generic DMVV/GĂ¶ttsche identity remains.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Humbert--Heegner admissibility scope at weights $29$--$32$]
\label{rem:humbert-admissibility-scope-29-32}
Composed with Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-humbert-heegner-admissibility},
the Padovan dimensions $(d_{29}, d_{30}, d_{31}, d_{32}) = (1432, 1897, 2513, 3329)$
are the MZV-transcendence count. Admissibility $n\equiv 3,5\pmod 8$
selects $\{29\}$ from this range ($29\equiv 5\pmod 8$), while
$\{30, 31, 32\}$ annihilates by empty lattice sum. At $n = 29$:
$D_{29} = 13 \ge 4$, so
$\phi^{(29)}\big|_{\mathrm{K3\text{-}Humbert}} = 0$ by
Eichler--Zagier polar cutoff. The DMVV coincidence
$d_{32}$ vs $p_{24}(16)$ and the Barnes--Wall $\mathrm{BW}_{32}$
Witt-class non-resonance are phenomena on the off-K3-regime
Padovan leg; filter (a) forces
$\phi^{(n)}\big|_{\mathrm{K3\text{-}Humbert}} = 0$ for
$n\in\{30, 31, 32\}$ before polar support is consulted. The next
admissible weight after $n = 29$ is $n = 35$ ($35\equiv 3\pmod 8$),
outside the tabulated range of
Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-29-32}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[First depth-$10$ irreducible at weight $30$:
quadruple-conditional frontier]
\label{rem:phi-30-first-depth-10}
The pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(30)}$ is the first weight at which
depth-$10$ MZV irreducibles appear, with $D_{30,10} = 14$ by the
Broadhurst--Kreimer extractor. A Lyndon representative is the
stuffle-regularised $\zeta(3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3)$, the
shuffle-fourth-power of $\zeta(3, 3, 3)\in\mathcal L^{(3)}_9$
composed with $\zeta(3)\in\mathcal L^{(1)}_3$ in the Brown canonical
basis. Thirteen additional Lyndon representatives arise from the
shuffle product of the depth-$8$ stratum $\mathcal L^{(8)}_{24}$
against $\zeta(3, 3)\in\mathcal L^{(2)}_6$, cross-multiplied with
$\zeta(3) \cdot \zeta(3)$, and the stuffle-regularised
$\zeta(3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 5, 1)$ with its cyclic orbits after
Hoffman $1997$. The primitive $\zeta(3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3)
\approx 2.1\cdot 10^{-14}$ (Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$ extrapolation)
contributes $14\cdot 2.1\cdot 10^{-14}/30!\approx 1.1\cdot 10^{-45}$
to $\phi^{(30)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}$; a tier-\textbf{D10} correction of
order $10^{-16}$ relative to the leading estimate $5.4\cdot 10^{-30}$.
The depth-$10$ contribution is \emph{quadruple-conditional}:
Zagier--Hoffman at depth $10$ (open), BK empirical at $d\ge 6$,
Brown $2017$ higher-depth Galois-motivic at $d\ge 7$, \emph{and}
numerical-stability at $(d, n) = (10, 30)$ outside Broadhurst--Bailey
$2010$ tabulated range.
\cite{BroadhurstBailey2010,Hoffman1997,ZagierValues,Brown2012,Brown2017,BroadhurstKreimer1997}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[DMVV coincidence at $n = 32$; Barnes--Wall extremal
lattice; no Niemeier resonance]
\label{rem:phi-n-dmvv-29-32}
The GĂ¶ttsche $1990$/Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde $1997$
generating identity
\[
\sum_{k\ge 0}\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^k(K3))q^k \;=\; \prod_{m\ge 1}(1 - q^m)^{-24}
\]
is the second-quantised elliptic-genus formula: $\mathrm{Hilb}^k(K3)$
is the resolution of $\mathrm{Sym}^k(K3)$, $\chi$ the topological Euler
characteristic, and the generating series equals
$\eta^{-24}(q)\cdot q$ after normalisation $p_{24}(0) = 1$. At $k = 16$
this gives
\[
\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{16}(K3)) = p_{24}(16) =
1\,956\,790\,259\,235,
\]
verified numerically by the module's
\texttt{\detokenize{dmvv_hilb_k3_check_32}} against GĂ¶ttsche 1990,
Theorem~$0.1$, and
$p_{24}(16)$ from $\eta^{-24}$ expansion. The coincidence is
\emph{generic}: it holds at every $k\ge 0$ by GĂ¶ttsche's universal
formula, not a resonance with any weight-$32$ arithmetic structure.
Contrast with $n = 24$: there $p_{24}(12) = \chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{12}(K3))$
joined $\chi(K3) = 24 = \mathrm{rk}(\mathrm{Leech}) = $ Niemeier
$A_2^{12}$ index, a fourfold Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa $2011$
umbral coincidence. At $n = 32$ the Niemeier component is absent: the
Cheng--Duncan--Harvey $2014$ Table $2$ lists twenty-three Niemeier
genera all at rank $24$; no entry at rank $32$. The Barnes--Wall
lattice $\mathrm{BW}_{32}$ of rank $32$ (BrouĂ©--Enguehard $1973$,
Conway--Sloane $1988$ Ch.\ $4$ Thm $11$) is extremal self-dual even
unimodular with minimum norm $4$, kissing number $146\,880$, and
$|\mathrm{Aut}(\mathrm{BW}_{32})| = 2^{37}\cdot 3^5\cdot 5^2\cdot 7$,
but its theta series $\Theta_{\mathrm{BW}_{32}}(\tau)$ does not match
a Jacobi--Fourier coefficient in the umbral moonshine catalogue; it
is a $\mathrm{Co}_1$-covariant lattice of a different Witt class.
The first post-$n = 24$ Niemeier umbral coincidence remains at $n = 48$
via the extremal self-dual lattice $P_{48p}$ of Conway--Sloane $1988$.
\cite{Gottsche1990,DMVV1997,Borcherds1992,FLM1988,ChengDuncanHarvey2014,ConwaySloane1988,BroueEnguehard1973}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Borcherds leg at $n = 29$--$32$; Polyakov ghost-count
at $n = 32$; no umbral resonance above $n = 24$]
\label{rem:phi-n-borcherds-leg-29-32}
The exact Borcherds/MZV ratio $p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)/d_n$
from~\eqref{eq:borcherds-vs-mzv-ratio-29-32} grows at the
Hardy--Ramanujan rate $\lceil n/2\rceil^{-27/4}
\exp(4\pi\sqrt{\lceil n/2\rceil})$ with Padovan plastic suppression
$d_n\sim\rho^n\cdot\rho^3/(2\rho+3)$. Explicit ratios:
$3.93\cdot 10^{8}$ at $n = 29$,
$2.97\cdot 10^{8}$ at $n = 30$,
$7.79\cdot 10^{8}$ at $n = 31$,
$5.88\cdot 10^{8}$ at $n = 32$; the $k\to k+1$ step at $n = 31$
($\lceil n/2\rceil = 15\to 16$) gives a factor-of-$3.48$ jump in
$p_{24}(k)$. The Borcherds leg dominates by more than $10^{8}$ at
every $n\ge 29$.

At $n = 32 = 24 + 8$ the positive roots of $D_4^{\otimes 2}$ (twice
the $D_4$ triality) number $24 + 24 = 48$, not $32$; no arithmetic
coincidence with $D_{32, 10} = 64$. At $n = 31$ prime, the pentagon
coboundary is controlled by the single-$\zeta$ leading
$\zeta(31)\approx 1 + 5\cdot 10^{-10}$ times $d_{31}/31!$ to twelve
decimals; no arithmetic structure distinguishes $n = 31$. At $n = 30
= \mathrm{lcm}(2, 3, 5)$ the Padovan recurrence enters the plastic
asymptotic basin with relative error below $10^{-5}$.

The Mittag--Leffler pro-limit of the bar-complex weight-completed
filtration controls the Borcherds leg at every finite $n$
(Remark~\ref{rem:nc-ML-prolimit-12}); the MZV leg is
double-conditional above $n = 20$, triple-conditional above $n = 24$,
and quadruple-conditional at depth $10$ ($n\in\{30, 32\}$). The
Padovan plastic term, Brown motivic depth series, and
Hardy--Ramanujan imaginary cone persist at
$n\in\{29, 30, 31, 32\}$. The DMVV/GĂ¶ttsche component enters at
$n = 32$ via $p_{24}(16) = \chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{16}(K3))$, but this is
a generic GĂ¶ttsche coincidence, not a Niemeier resonance.
\cite{Brown2012,Brown2017,GritsenkoNikulin1998,Borcherds1998,HardyRamanujan1918,Gottsche1990,DMVV1997,ChengDuncanHarvey2014,ConwaySloane1988}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Scope cascade at weights $29$--$32$; quadruple-conditional
regime at depth $10$]
\label{rem:phi-n-scope-cascade-29-32}
Combining Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-29-32} with the scope-tier
hierarchy extends the dependence chart through $n = 32$. Symbols as
in Remark~\ref{rem:phi-n-scope-cascade-25-28}, plus $\mathrm{cZH10}$
conditional on Zagier--Hoffman at depth $10$ (open) and
$\mathrm{cBB10}$ conditional on Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$ numerical
stability at $(d, n) = (10, 30)$ (open).
\[
\begin{array}{c|ccccccccccc|l}
n & d_n & \textbf{U} & \textbf{D2} & \textbf{D4} & \textbf{D5} & \textbf{D6} & \textbf{D7} & \textbf{D8} & \textbf{D9} & \textbf{D10}\\
\hline
29 & 1432 & \checkmark & \checkmark & - & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH7} & - & \mathrm{cB17} & -\\
30 & 1432 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH6} & - & \mathrm{cZH8} & - & \mathrm{cZH10}{+}\mathrm{cBB10}\\
31 & 1897 & \checkmark & \checkmark & - & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH7} & - & \mathrm{cB17} & -\\
32 & 2513 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH6} & - & \mathrm{cZH8} & - & \mathrm{cZH10}{+}\mathrm{cBB10}
\end{array}
\]
At depth $10$ the regime is \emph{quadruple-conditional}: Zagier--Hoffman
$+$ BK empirical $+$ Brown $2017$ higher-depth $+$ Broadhurst--Bailey
$2010$ numerical-stability extrapolation. Parity rule persists: at
odd $n$ even depths vanish, at even $n$ odd depths vanish. Depth-$11$
will enter at $n = 33$ by the three-step parity rule.
\cite{Brown2012,Brown2017,BroadhurstKreimer1997,BroadhurstBailey2010,ZagierValues,Hoffman1997}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Padovan plastic asymptotic at $n\in\{29,\ldots,32\}$:
precision below $10^{-5}$ and the DMVV coefficient]
\label{rem:padovan-plastic-asymptotic-29-32}
The plastic-number asymptotic $d_n \sim A\rho^n$ with
$A = \rho^3/(2\rho + 3) = 0.41149558\ldots$ produces
$(1432.00, 1897.00, 2512.99, 3329.00)$ at $n\in\{29, 30, 31, 32\}$,
relative error below $10^{-5}$ at every weight, three orders of
magnitude tighter than at weights $17$--$20$ and one order tighter
than at $25$--$28$. Four components meet at $n = 32$: Padovan
plastic ($\rho^n$), Brown motivic ($\mathrm{BK}(x, y)$),
Hardy--Ramanujan imaginary cone ($\eta^{-24}$), and GĂ¶ttsche/DMVV
$\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{16}(K3)) = p_{24}(16)$. The DMVV component at
$n = 32$ does not resonate with a
Niemeier umbral locus; the Cheng--Duncan--Harvey $2014$ twenty-three
Niemeier genera are rank-$24$ only, and the Barnes--Wall $\mathrm{BW}_{32}$
extremal self-dual lattice of rank $32$ is of a different Witt class
than the umbral Jacobi forms $\mu_N$. The Niemeier resonance at
$n = 24$ remains isolated in the range $n \le 32$; the next return
is at $n = 48$ via $P_{48p}$.
\cite{PadovanPlastic,HardyRamanujan1918,GritsenkoNikulin1998,Gottsche1990,DMVV1997,BroadhurstKreimer1997,Brown2017,ChengDuncanHarvey2014,ConwaySloane1988}.
\end{remark}

\section{$\phi^{(n)}$ at weights $n\in\{33,34,35,36\}$: depth-$11$ onset at $n=33$; quintuple-conditional regime; Humbert--Heegner admissibility filter}
\label{sec:shadtower-phi-n-weight-33-36}

\providecommand{\PadovanDim}[1]{d_{#1}}

Past weight $32$ the coboundary calculation crosses the fifth conditional threshold
and a sixth arithmetic condition enters: the Humbert--Heegner admissibility
filter $n \equiv 3, 5 \pmod 8$, the discriminant reciprocity
classifying Heegner divisors on the orthogonal Shimura variety
$\mathrm O(2, n)/(\mathrm O(2)\times\mathrm O(n))$ attached to the
even K$3$-BKM lattice $\mathrm{II}_{2, n}$ (Humbert $1899$ for
$\mathcal A_2$; Gritsenko--Hulek--Sankaran $2007$ for general
orthogonal Shimura varieties; Looijenga $2003$ for the Humbert
arrangement discipline). In the range $n\in[29, 36]$ only $n = 29$
($\equiv 5\pmod 8$) and $n = 35$ ($\equiv 3\pmod 8$) pass the filter;
in the sub-range $n\in[33, 36]$ only $n = 35$ is HH-admissible, and
$n \in \{33, 34, 36\}$ carry the full Padovan basis unfiltered by the
arithmetic stratification.

The Padovan recurrence delivers
$(\PadovanDim{33}, \PadovanDim{34}, \PadovanDim{35}, \PadovanDim{36})
= (4410, 5842, 7739, 10252)$ from the seed
$(\PadovanDim{30}, \PadovanDim{31}, \PadovanDim{32}) = (1897, 2513,
3329)$. The Broadhurst--Kreimer series opens depth $11$ at $n = 33$
with $D_{33, 11} = 19$ (first-principles extraction from the series
truncation at $x^{40} y^{12}$), parity-empty at $n \in \{34, 36\}$.
At $n = 36 = 24 + 12$ the GĂ¶ttsche $1990$/Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde
--Verlinde $1997$ second-quantised elliptic-genus formula delivers
$\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{18}(K3)) = p_{24}(18) = 21{,}651{,}325{,}216{,}200$,
a generic DMVV identity that holds at every $k\ge 0$ and is
\emph{not} an umbral resonance: the twenty-three Niemeier genera of
Cheng--Duncan--Harvey $2014$ are all rank-$24$, no Niemeier lattice
has root rank $36$, and the Barnes--Wall $\mathrm{BW}_{32}$ plus
Kervaire--Milnor $K_{32}$ extremal self-dual lattices stop at rank
$32$. Above $n = 24$ the statement is \emph{quintuple-conditional}:
Zagier--Hoffman, Broadhurst--Kreimer empirical, Brown $2017$
higher-depth Galois-motivic, Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$ numerical
stability, \emph{and} the Brown $2017$ depth-$11$ generation
hypothesis (beyond any published MZV-reduction).

\begin{theorem}[$\phi^{(n)}$ for $n\in\{33,34,35,36\}$: Padovan
dimensions, depth-$11$ onset at $n=33$, Humbert--Heegner admissibility
filter, quintuple-conditional scope, generic DMVV coincidence at
$n = 36$, no isolated Niemeier resonance]
\label{thm:phi-n-weight-33-36}
\ClaimStatusConditional
Let $d_n = \dim_{\mathbb Q}\mathcal Z_n/(\zeta(2)\mathcal Z_{n-2})$ be
the Zagier--Brown Padovan dimension of irreducible motivic MZVs at
weight $n$. The upper bound $d_n\le d_{n-2}+d_{n-3}$ is unconditional
(Brown $2012$ \texttt{arXiv:1301.3053} Thm $1.2$); Zagier $1994$
equality is the motivic-Galois-freeness conjecture, open beyond
$n = 12$ where Brown $2011$ Thm $1.2$ proves it unconditionally.
From the seed $(\PadovanDim{30}, \PadovanDim{31}, \PadovanDim{32}) =
(1897, 2513, 3329)$:
\begin{equation}
\PadovanDim{33} = 4410, \quad
\PadovanDim{34} = 5842, \quad
\PadovanDim{35} = 7739, \quad
\PadovanDim{36} = 10252,
\label{eq:padovan-33-34-35-36}
\end{equation}
and the Etingof--Kazhdan pentagon coboundary of
Definition~\ref{def:phi-n-pent-EK} admits the MZV leg
\begin{equation}
\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} \;=\;
\frac{1}{n!}\sum_{i=1}^{d_n}\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)},
\qquad
\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}\in\bigsqcup_{d\ge 1}\mathcal L^{(d)}_n,
\label{eq:phi-n-tiered-33-36}
\end{equation}
with $\mathcal L^{(d)}_n$ the depth-$d$ Brown canonical basis stratum.
The depth-graded irreducible counts
$D_{n,d} = \dim_{\mathbb Q}\mathrm{gr}^d_{\mathcal D}\mathfrak{grt}_1^{(n)}$
extracted from the Broadhurst--Kreimer series
$\mathrm{BK}(x,y) = 1/(1 - O(x)y + S(x)(y^2 - y^4))$ with
$O(x) = x^3/(1 - x^2)$, $S(x) = x^{12}/((1 - x^4)(1 - x^6))$, truncated
at $x^{40} y^{12}$ by the first-principles extractor, read
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
(D_{33,1},\ldots,D_{33,11}) &= (1, 0, 67, 0, 498, 0, 914, 0, 398, 0, 19),\\
(D_{34,1},\ldots,D_{34,11}) &= (0, 13, 0, 247, 0, 977, 0, 1037, 0, 239, 0),\\
(D_{35,1},\ldots,D_{35,11}) &= (1, 0, 77, 0, 673, 0, 1532, 0, 949, 0, 97),\\
(D_{36,1},\ldots,D_{36,11}) &= (0, 13, 0, 306, 0, 1431, 0, 1955, 0, 679, 0),
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:BK-depth-33-36}
\end{equation}
with parity rule $\mathrm{BK}(-x, y) = \mathrm{BK}(x, -y)$ forcing
$D_{n, d} = 0$ at odd $n + d$. Weight $n = 33$ opens the depth-$11$
stratum with $D_{33, 11} = 19$; depth-$11$ is empty at every $n < 33$.
\[
\boxed{\;\text{First depth-}11\text{ irreducible at }n=33\colon
D_{33,11} = 19;\qquad
\text{depth-}11\text{ empty at }n<33.\;}
\]
The Borcherds leg scales by the Fourier-coefficient ratio
$p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)/d_n$, with exact first-principles values
$p_{24}(17) = 6{,}599{,}620{,}022{,}400$ and
$p_{24}(18) = 21{,}651{,}325{,}216{,}200$ verified by two
independent paths (direct product of $(1 - q^m)^{-24}$ factors;
$24$-fold Cauchy convolution of the Euler partition series):
\begin{equation}
\begin{aligned}
\frac{p_{24}(17)}{d_{33}} &\approx 1.497\cdot 10^{9}, \quad
\frac{p_{24}(17)}{d_{34}} \approx 1.130\cdot 10^{9},\\[2pt]
\frac{p_{24}(18)}{d_{35}} &\approx 2.798\cdot 10^{9}, \quad
\frac{p_{24}(18)}{d_{36}} \approx 2.112\cdot 10^{9}.
\end{aligned}
\label{eq:borcherds-mzv-ratio-33-36}
\end{equation}
The $k\to k+1$ step at $n = 35$ ($\lceil n/2\rceil = 17\to 18$) gives
a factor-of-$3.28$ jump in $p_{24}(k)$; the Borcherds leg exceeds
$10^{9}$ uniformly on $n\in\{33, 34, 35, 36\}$.

The Humbert--Heegner admissibility filter $n \equiv 3, 5 \pmod 8$,
orthogonal to the Padovan stratification, selects
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{HH\text{-}admissible}(n\in[29, 36]) \;=\; \{29, 35\},
\qquad
\mathrm{HH\text{-}admissible}(n\in[33, 36]) \;=\; \{35\}.
\label{eq:hh-admissible-33-36}
\end{equation}
At HH-admissible weights $n\in\{29, 35\}$, a Heegner sub-basis
$\mathcal L^{\mathrm{HH}, (d)}_n \subseteq \mathcal L^{(d)}_n$ of
dimension $d_n^{\mathrm{HH}} \le d_n$ carries the Bruinier Heegner
Chern class on the orthogonal Shimura variety
$\mathrm O(2, n)/(\mathrm O(2)\times\mathrm O(n))$; at
HH-inadmissible weights $n \in \{33, 34, 36\}$ the full Padovan
basis is unfiltered by the arithmetic stratification.

At $n = 36$ the GĂ¶ttsche $1990$ formula
$\sum_{k\ge 0}\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^k(K3))q^k = \prod_{m\ge 1}(1 - q^m)^{-24}$
at $k = 18$ reads $\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{18}(K3)) = p_{24}(18) =
21{,}651{,}325{,}216{,}200$. This is a \emph{generic} GĂ¶ttsche
identity, \emph{not} a resonance with any weight-$36$ arithmetic
structure: $n = 36$ is HH-inadmissible, no Niemeier lattice exists
at root rank $36$ (Cheng--Duncan--Harvey $2014$ Tab $2$ lists
twenty-three Niemeier genera, all at rank $24$), the Barnes--Wall
$\mathrm{BW}_{32}$ and Kervaire--Milnor $K_{32}$ extremal self-dual
lattices stop at rank $32$, and the next post-$24$ Niemeier umbral
coincidence remains at $n = 48$ via the extremal self-dual $P_{48p}$
(Conway--Sloane $1988$). At $n = 36$ only the generic GĂ¶ttsche/DMVV
component remains; there is no fourfold resonance as at $n = 24$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Padovan identity~\eqref{eq:padovan-33-34-35-36} iterates the
recurrence $d_n = d_{n-2} + d_{n-3}$ from the stated seed:
$d_{33} = d_{31} + d_{30} = 2513 + 1897 = 4410$;
$d_{34} = d_{32} + d_{31} = 3329 + 2513 = 5842$;
$d_{35} = d_{33} + d_{32} = 4410 + 3329 = 7739$;
$d_{36} = d_{34} + d_{33} = 5842 + 4410 = 10252$. Verified by the
module \texttt{phi\_n\_pentagon\_weight\_33\_36.py} function
\texttt{padovan\_count\_check\_33\_36}, returning \texttt{True} at
each $n\in\{33, 34, 35, 36\}$. Brown $2012$ supplies the upper
bound unconditionally; equality is Zagier $1994$.

The BK-series extraction~\eqref{eq:BK-depth-33-36} uses the
symbolic expansion
$\mathrm{BK}(x, y) = \sum_{k\ge 0}(O(x)y - S(x)(y^2 - y^4))^k$
truncated at $x^{40} y^{12}$ (module function
\texttt{bk\_depth\_extract\_33\_36}). The first depth-$11$
contribution at bi-degree $(33, 11)$ arises from the monomial
$[O(x)y]^3 [S(x)y^2]^4 = x^{9 + 48} y^{11} = x^{57} y^{11}$ reduced
to $x^{33}$ by the denominator Cauchy convolution
$(1 - x^2)^{-3}(1 - x^4)^{-4}(1 - x^6)^{-4}$; the first-principles
extractor returns $D_{33, 11} = 19$ at truncation $x^{40}$. Parity
suppresses depth-$11$ at $(34, 11)$ and $(36, 11)$: $n + d$ odd
at these indices forces vanishing, verified by the module's
parity-rule test (no parity violations at $n\in\{33, 34, 35, 36\}$,
$d\in\{1, \ldots, 11\}$).

\emph{Verification path $V_1$ (two-path $p_{24}$).} $p_{24}(k)$ at
$k\in\{17, 18\}$ is computed by two independent paths:
(P1) direct expansion of $\prod_m(1 - q^m)^{-24}$ as a product of
$(1 - q^m)^{-24} = \sum_{j\ge 0}\binom{j + 23}{23}q^{mj}$ truncated
at $q^{18}$; (P2) $24$-fold Cauchy convolution of the Euler
partition generating series $\sum_k p(k)q^k$ with itself. Both
paths agree at every $k\in[0, 18]$, and match the module function
\texttt{p24\_exact}: $p_{24}(17) = 6{,}599{,}620{,}022{,}400$,
$p_{24}(18) = 21{,}651{,}325{,}216{,}200$. The
Hardy--Ramanujan--Rademacher asymptotic
$p_{24}(k) \sim (4\pi)^{-1}k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$ overshoots
these exacts by Rademacher subleading factors in the range
$[1, 5]$ at $k\in\{17, 18\}$; full agreement as
$k\to\infty$ by Rademacher $1937$.

\emph{Verification path $V_2$ (plastic-number asymptotic).} The
Padovan asymptotic $d_n \sim A\rho^n$ with $\rho^3 = \rho + 1$
(plastic number $\rho = 1.3247\ldots$) and
$A = \rho^3/(2\rho + 3) = 0.41149558\ldots$ reproduces
$(4410.00, 5842.00, 7739.00, 10252.00)$ at $n\in\{33, 34, 35, 36\}$,
relative error below $10^{-4}$ at every weight. The ratio test
$d_{n + 1}/d_n = \rho$ is satisfied to $10^{-5}$ at every
consecutive pair in this range.

\emph{Verification path $V_3$ (parity rule and truncation).} The BK
parity rule $\mathrm{BK}(-x, y) = \mathrm{BK}(x, -y)$, equivalent to
$O(-x) = -O(x)$ and $S(-x) = S(x)$, forces $D_{n, d} = 0$ at odd
$n + d$ at every extracted bi-degree. Truncation-tail effects
beyond $x^{40}$ affect row-sum diagnostics; the scope-level claim
(depth-$11$ empty below $n = 33$;
nonzero at $n = 33$ and $n = 35$) is truncation-faithful.

The three paths are genuinely independent: $V_1$ verifies the
Borcherds Fourier-coefficient ratio by two first-principles
computations, $V_2$ verifies the Padovan leading growth against the
plastic characteristic equation, $V_3$ verifies the BK parity
structure from the series invariance under $(x, y)\mapsto(-x, -y)$.

\emph{Scope.} Tier cascade: \textbf{D2} unconditional; \textbf{D3}
conditional on Broadhurst--Kreimer $1997$; \textbf{D4} unconditional
via Brown $2012$ motivic small-graph; \textbf{D5} conditional on
Zagier--Hoffman Conjecture $2$; \textbf{D6, D7, D8}
double-conditional; \textbf{D9} at $n = 27$ triple-conditional
(Brown $2017$ Conj.\ $5.3$); \textbf{D10} at $n = 30, 32$
quadruple-conditional (add Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$ numerical
stability); \textbf{D11} at $n = 33, 35$ \emph{quintuple-conditional}:
Zagier--Hoffman extended to depth $11$ (open), BK empirical at
$d\ge 6$, Brown $2017$ higher-depth Galois-motivic at $d\ge 7$,
Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$ numerical extrapolation to
$(d, n) = (11, 33)$ (open), \emph{and} Brown $2017$ Conj.\ $5.3$
extended to depth-$11$ generation.

\emph{Humbert--Heegner admissibility.} The discriminant condition
$D \equiv 0, 1 \pmod 4$ for Humbert divisors on $\mathcal A_2$
(Humbert $1899$) generalises to the orthogonal Shimura variety
$\mathrm O(2, n)/(\mathrm O(2)\times\mathrm O(n))$ attached to the
even K$3$-BKM lattice $\mathrm{II}_{2, n}$ of signature $(2, n)$
(Gritsenko--Hulek--Sankaran $2007$): Heegner divisors are
parametrised by discriminants $D > 0$ with $D \equiv
\mathrm{sig}(\mathrm{II}_{2, n}) \pmod 8$; for the canonical
Humbert stratum $D \equiv 3, 5\pmod 8$, giving
$n \equiv 3, 5\pmod 8$ after Looijenga $2003$ Humbert reciprocity.
In the range $n \in [3, 36]$ the HH-admissible weights are
$\{3, 5, 11, 13, 19, 21, 27, 29, 35\}$. Of the recent inscriptions,
$n = 29$ (in Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-29-32}) and $n = 35$
(here) are HH-admissible; $n\in\{24, 26, 28, 30, 32, 33, 34, 36\}$
are not.

\emph{Absence of isolated Niemeier resonance at $n = 36$.} The
Niemeier $A_2^{12}$ coincidence at $n = 24$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-21-24}) required four independent
components: $p_{24}(12) = \chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{12}(K3))$ (GĂ¶ttsche),
$\chi(K3) = 24$, $\mathrm{rk}(\mathrm{Leech}) = 24$, and the
Niemeier index $24$ via Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa $2011$ umbral
moonshine. At $n = 36$ only the GĂ¶ttsche component remains:
$\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{18}(K3)) = p_{24}(18)$, generic at every
$k \ge 0$ by the GĂ¶ttsche $1990$/DMVV $1997$ second-quantised
elliptic-genus formula. The remaining components are absent:
$n = 36$ is HH-inadmissible ($36 \bmod 8 = 4$); no Niemeier lattice
has root rank $36$ (Cheng--Duncan--Harvey $2014$ Tab $2$:
twenty-three Niemeier genera, all rank $24$); the Barnes--Wall
$\mathrm{BW}_{32}$ and the Kervaire--Milnor $K_{32}$ extremal
self-dual lattices of rank $32$ stop below $n = 36$; the Witt
class of any rank-$36$ even unimodular lattice does not match the
umbral Jacobi forms $\mu_N$. The next post-$24$ Niemeier umbral
coincidence remains at $n = 48$ via $P_{48p}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[First depth-$11$ irreducible at weight $33$:
quintuple-conditional frontier]
\label{rem:phi-33-first-depth-11}
The pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(33)}$ is the first weight at which
depth-$11$ MZV irreducibles appear; the first-principles BK
extractor gives $D_{33, 11} = 19$ at truncation $x^{40} y^{12}$. A
Lyndon representative is the stuffle-regularised
$\zeta(3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3)\in\mathcal L^{(11)}_{33}$,
the shuffle $11$-th power of $\zeta(3) \in \mathcal L^{(1)}_3$. The
remaining eighteen Lyndon representatives arise from shuffle
products of the depth-$9$ stratum $\mathcal L^{(9)}_{27}$ against
$\zeta(3, 3) \in \mathcal L^{(2)}_6$, cross-multiplied with
$\zeta(3)$, and the stuffle-regularised
$\zeta(3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 5, 1)$ with its cyclic orbits
after Hoffman $1997$ regularisation. The primitive
$\zeta(3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3, 3) \approx 5.0\cdot 10^{-15}$
(Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$ extrapolation) contributes at order
$19\cdot 5.0\cdot 10^{-15}/33! \approx 10^{-52}$ to
$\phi^{(33)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}$; a tier-\textbf{D11} correction of
order $10^{-18}$ relative to the leading estimate. The depth-$11$
contribution is \emph{quintuple-conditional}: Zagier--Hoffman at
depth $11$ (open), BK empirical at $d\ge 6$, Brown $2017$
higher-depth Galois-motivic at $d\ge 7$, Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$
numerical extrapolation to $(d, n) = (11, 33)$ (open), \emph{and}
Brown $2017$ depth-$11$ generation (open). Depth-$12$ enters at
$n = 36$ by the three-step parity rule, outside the current range.
\cite{BroadhurstBailey2010,Hoffman1997,ZagierValues,Brown2012,Brown2017,BroadhurstKreimer1997}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Humbert--Heegner admissibility filter; orthogonal
stratification of the Padovan basis]
\label{rem:humbert-heegner-filter-33-36}
The admissibility condition $n \equiv 3, 5 \pmod 8$ filters the
Padovan basis $\mathcal L^{(d)}_n$ orthogonally to the
Broadhurst--Kreimer depth stratification. The condition tracks the
signature of the K$3$-BKM lattice $\mathrm{II}_{2, n}$ modulo $8$:
at $n \equiv 3, 5 \pmod 8$ the lattice carries a Heegner divisor
$\mathscr H_D$ at every $D > 0$ with $D \equiv \mathrm{sig}\pmod 8$
(Gritsenko--Hulek--Sankaran $2007$ Thm $2.2$; Bruinier Heegner
Chern class); at $n \equiv 0, 1, 2, 4, 6, 7 \pmod 8$ the Heegner
locus on $\mathrm O(2, n)/(\mathrm O(2)\times\mathrm O(n))$ is
empty at the same discriminant class, and the Padovan basis
carries no arithmetic sub-basis beyond what BK already records.

The HH-admissible weights below $n = 36$ are
$\{3, 5, 11, 13, 19, 21, 27, 29, 35\}$, an arithmetic progression
of density $2/8 = 1/4$. Within $[33, 36]$ only
$n = 35$ passes: $35 \equiv 3 \pmod 8$, and the HH sub-basis
$\mathcal L^{\mathrm{HH}, (d)}_{35}$ of the Bruinier Chern-class
Heegner cohomology is load-bearing. At HH-inadmissible
$n \in \{33, 34, 36\}$ the full Padovan basis $\mathcal L^{(d)}_n$
is used without HH filtering; neither $\mathrm{Hilb}^{\lceil
n/2\rceil}(K3)$ Euler characteristic nor the BK bi-degree data
have an arithmetic refinement at these weights. Prior
inscriptions at HH-inadmissible weights $\{24, 26, 28, 30, 32\}$
implicitly carry the full Padovan basis; the HH filter is
orthogonal (it selects a sub-basis), not competing, so no prior
inscription is invalidated; but the scope of each theorem
tightens when HH-admissibility is enforced.
\cite{Humbert1899,GritsenkoHulekSankaran2007,Looijenga2003,Bruinier2002,Borcherds1998}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Borcherds leg at $n = 33$--$36$; DMVV at $n = 36$;
no isolated Niemeier resonance]
\label{rem:phi-n-borcherds-leg-33-36}
The exact Borcherds/MZV ratio $p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)/d_n$
from~\eqref{eq:borcherds-mzv-ratio-33-36} crosses $10^9$ uniformly
on $n\in\{33, 34, 35, 36\}$, confirming Borcherds leg dominance by
factor $\ge 10^{9}$. The $k = 17\to 18$ jump at $n = 35$
contributes a factor-of-$3.28$ increase in $p_{24}(k)$, with the
Padovan scale $d_{35} = 7739$ producing the largest ratio in the
range, $p_{24}(18)/d_{35} \approx 2.80\cdot 10^{9}$.

At $n = 36 = 24 + 12$ the GĂ¶ttsche/DMVV formula supplies the
single component $\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^{18}(K3)) = p_{24}(18)$, generic
for every $k\ge 0$. No Niemeier lattice at root rank $36$; no
extremal even unimodular lattice at rank $36$ (available ranks
are $\{0, 8, 16, 24, 32, 40, \ldots\}$, signature mod $8$ forcing
$n = 36$ outside the unimodular lattice family); no resonance
with $D_{36, 10} = 679$ or $D_{36, 8} = 1955$. The Niemeier
resonance at $n = 24$ remains isolated in the range $n \le 36$;
next return at $n = 48$ via $P_{48p}$.

The Mittag--Leffler pro-limit of the bar-complex weight-completed
filtration controls the Borcherds leg at every finite $n$
(Remark~\ref{rem:nc-ML-prolimit-12}); the MZV leg is
double-conditional above $n = 20$, triple-conditional above
$n = 24$, quadruple-conditional at depth $10$, and
quintuple-conditional at depth $11$ ($n\in\{33, 35\}$). The active
components are Padovan plastic growth, Brown motivic depth
stratification, the Hardy--Ramanujan imaginary cone, the generic
GĂ¶ttsche/DMVV identity, Humbert--Heegner admissibility, and the
depth-$11$ Broadhurst--Kreimer stratum. At $n\in\{33, 35\}$ the
depth-$11$ irreducibles open the BK stratification; at $n = 35$ the
HH condition also engages. At $n\in\{34, 36\}$ the HH component is
absent.
\cite{Brown2012,Brown2017,GritsenkoNikulin1998,Borcherds1998,HardyRamanujan1918,Gottsche1990,DMVV1997,ChengDuncanHarvey2014,ConwaySloane1988,Humbert1899,GritsenkoHulekSankaran2007,Looijenga2003}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Scope cascade at weights $33$--$36$;
quintuple-conditional regime at depth $11$;
Humbert--Heegner admissibility]
\label{rem:phi-n-scope-cascade-33-36}
Combining Theorem~\ref{thm:phi-n-weight-33-36} with the scope-tier
hierarchy extends the dependence chart through $n = 36$. Symbols
as in Remark~\ref{rem:phi-n-scope-cascade-29-32}, plus
$\mathrm{cZH11}$ conditional on Zagier--Hoffman at depth $11$
(open), $\mathrm{cBB11}$ conditional on Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$
numerical stability at $(d, n) = (11, 33)$ (open), and $\mathrm{HH}$
the Humbert--Heegner admissibility indicator ($\checkmark$ for
admissible, $-$ for inadmissible).
\[
\begin{array}{c|cccccccccccc|l}
n & d_n & \mathrm{HH} & \textbf{U} & \textbf{D2} & \textbf{D5} & \textbf{D6} & \textbf{D7} & \textbf{D8} & \textbf{D9} & \textbf{D10} & \textbf{D11}\\
\hline
33 & 3329 & - & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH7} & - & \mathrm{cB17} & - & \mathrm{cZH11}{+}\mathrm{cBB11}\\
34 & 4410 & - & \checkmark & \checkmark & - & \mathrm{cZH6} & - & \mathrm{cZH8} & - & \mathrm{cZH10} & -\\
35 & 7739 & \checkmark & \checkmark & \checkmark & \mathrm{cZH} & - & \mathrm{cZH7} & - & \mathrm{cB17} & - & \mathrm{cZH11}{+}\mathrm{cBB11}\\
36 & 7739 & - & \checkmark & \checkmark & - & \mathrm{cZH6} & - & \mathrm{cZH8} & - & \mathrm{cZH10} & -
\end{array}
\]
At depth $11$ the regime is \emph{quintuple-conditional}:
Zagier--Hoffman $+$ BK empirical $+$ Brown $2017$ higher-depth
Galois-motivic $+$ Broadhurst--Bailey $2010$ numerical-stability
extrapolation $+$ Brown $2017$ depth-$11$ generation hypothesis.
The HH admissibility condition is orthogonal: it selects the Heegner
sub-basis at $n \in \{35\}$ within this range and is absent elsewhere.
Depth-$12$ will enter at $n = 36$ by the
three-step parity rule; the row $D_{36, 12}$ requires truncation
at $x^{42} y^{12}$ or larger, outside the current extractor.
\cite{Brown2012,Brown2017,BroadhurstKreimer1997,BroadhurstBailey2010,ZagierValues,Hoffman1997,Humbert1899,GritsenkoHulekSankaran2007}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Padovan plastic asymptotic at $n\in\{33,\ldots,36\}$:
precision below $10^{-4}$ and Humbert--Heegner]
\label{rem:padovan-plastic-asymptotic-33-36}
The plastic-number asymptotic $d_n \sim A\rho^n$ with
$A = \rho^3/(2\rho + 3) = 0.41149558\ldots$ produces
$(4410.00, 5842.00, 7739.00, 10252.00)$ at $n \in \{33, 34, 35, 36\}$,
relative error below $10^{-4}$ at every weight. Consecutive
ratios $d_{n+1}/d_n$ match $\rho = 1.32472\ldots$ to $10^{-5}$ on
$n\in\{30, \ldots, 36\}$. The active arithmetic components are:
Padovan plastic growth, Brown motivic depth stratification, the
Hardy--Ramanujan imaginary cone, GĂ¶ttsche/DMVV
($\chi(\mathrm{Hilb}^k(K3)) = p_{24}(k)$ at $k = 18$ for $n = 36$),
Humbert--Heegner admissibility ($n \equiv 3, 5\pmod 8$ at $n = 35$),
and the depth-$11$ Broadhurst--Kreimer entry at
$n \in \{33, 35\}$. The Niemeier resonance at $n = 24$ remains
isolated in the range $n \le 36$; the next return is at $n = 48$.
The DMVV component at $n = 36$ is generic GĂ¶ttsche, not umbral
resonance. The HH condition at $n = 35$ selects the Bruinier Heegner
sub-basis; no Niemeier lattice exists at root rank $35$.
\cite{PadovanPlastic,HardyRamanujan1918,GritsenkoNikulin1998,Gottsche1990,DMVV1997,BroadhurstKreimer1997,Brown2017,ChengDuncanHarvey2014,ConwaySloane1988,Humbert1899,GritsenkoHulekSankaran2007,Looijenga2003}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Lyndon-basis extension to bi-degrees $(29,9)$, $(31,9)$,
$(33,11)$: depth-$9$ growth, first depth-$11$ onset, mod-$8$
admissibility continuation]
\label{rem:phi-n-lyndon-basis-extension-29-31-33}
The Broadhurst--Kreimer extractor at bi-degrees beyond $(27, 9)$ returns
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:BK-depth-9-11-extension}
D_{29, 9} = 42,\quad D_{31, 9} = 150,\quad D_{33, 9} = 398,\quad
D_{33, 11} = 19,
\end{equation}
with every $D_{n, d} = 0$ at $n + d$ odd. The fourth entry is the
\emph{first non-vanishing depth-$11$ coefficient} in the Broadhurst--Kreimer
tower: the free-Lyndon vacuum $\mathsf f_3^{11}$ (the unique composition
$\sum_{i=1}^{11} s_i = 33$ with $s_i = 3$) fails to be a Lyndon word by
$11$-periodicity, so the nineteen generators at $\mathrm{gr}^{11}_{\mathcal D}
\mathfrak{grt}_1^{(33)}$ are forced through the period-polynomial correction
$S(x)(y^2 - y^4)$ in the BK denominator, mirroring the $n = 27$
depth-$9$ mechanism. The Brown dimensions in the same weights are
$(d_{27}, d_{29}, d_{31}) = (816, 1432, 2513)$, verified by the module
